from reportlab.pdfgen import canvas
from reportlab.lib.pagesizes import landscape
from reportlab.lib.units import inch

# We'll define a 16:9-ish custom size (11 x 6.1875 inches ~ 16:9)
PAGE_WIDTH = 11 * inch
PAGE_HEIGHT = 6.1875 * inch
PAGE_SIZE = (PAGE_WIDTH, PAGE_HEIGHT)

def create_brand_guide_pdf(path):
    c = canvas.Canvas(path, pagesize=PAGE_SIZE)
    w, h = PAGE_WIDTH, PAGE_HEIGHT

    # Title Page
    c.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 32)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-1.2*inch, "PureTask Brand Guide")
    c.setFont("Helvetica", 16)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-1.7*inch, "Colors • Typography • UI System")
    c.setFont("Helvetica-Oblique", 12)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-2.1*inch, "Internal use for product, marketing, and design teams.")
    c.showPage()

    # Brand Personality & Promise
    c.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 24)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-1.0*inch, "1. Brand Personality & Promise")

    text = c.beginText(1*inch, h-1.6*inch)
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Personality")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Clean • Trustworthy • Modern • Effortless")
    text.textLine("")

    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Core Promise")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("“Book trusted cleaners in minutes. GPS check-in/out, before & after photos,")
    text.textLine(" and pay only when you approve.”")
    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Social Shorthand")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("“PureTask — Like Uber, but for cleaning. Book, track, approve.")
    text.textLine(" Photo proof before payment.”")
    c.drawText(text)
    c.showPage()

    # Color System
    c.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 24)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-1.0*inch, "2. Color System")

    text = c.beginText(1*inch, h-1.6*inch)
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Primary Brand Gradient")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• PureTask Blue — #0078FF (Primary buttons, main CTAs, key headings)")
    text.textLine("• PureTask Aqua — #00D4FF (Gradient accent, highlights, secondary CTAs)")
    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Neutrals & States")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Graphite Slate — #1D2533 (Text, icons, navigation, high-contrast UI)")
    text.textLine("• Soft Cloud — #F7F9FC (Backgrounds, cards, light sections)")
    text.textLine("• Fresh Mint — #28C76F (Success states, confirmations, trust cues)")
    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Usage Rules")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Primary CTAs always use the Blue → Aqua gradient on full-pill buttons.")
    text.textLine("• Never use outline-only styles for primary actions.")
    text.textLine("• Reserve Fresh Mint for success states and positive highlights, not primary CTAs.")
    text.textLine("• Use Soft Cloud as the default app and marketing background color.")
    c.drawText(text)
    c.showPage()

    # Typography
    c.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 24)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-1.0*inch, "3. Typography System")

    text = c.beginText(1*inch, h-1.6*inch)
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Primary Display & UI Labels")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Fredoka — used for H1/H2/H3, navigation labels, and key UI labels.")
    text.textLine("  - H1 / Page Titles: Fredoka Bold 48–64px")
    text.textLine("  - H2 / Section Headings: Fredoka SemiBold 32–48px")
    text.textLine("  - H3 / Card Titles / Feature Headers: Fredoka Medium 22–28px")
    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Body Copy")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Verdana — used for paragraphs, descriptions, and legal copy.")
    text.textLine("  - Body: Verdana Regular 16–18px")
    text.textLine("  - Legal/Microcopy: Verdana Regular 14px")
    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Marketing Accent")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Lilita One — used sparingly for big campaign headlines and social graphics.")
    text.textLine("  - Example use: “Book. Clean. Done.” in ads and landing headers.")
    c.drawText(text)
    c.showPage()

    # Buttons & UI Elements
    c.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 24)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-1.0*inch, "4. Buttons & Interactive Elements")

    text = c.beginText(1*inch, h-1.6*inch)
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Primary CTA Button")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Shape: Full pill (border-radius: 9999px)")
    text.textLine("• Padding: 14px vertical, 32px horizontal")
    text.textLine("• Gradient: #0078FF → #00D4FF, white text")
    text.textLine("• Font: Fredoka Medium, Title Case labels (e.g., “Book Cleaning”)")
    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("States")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Default: Gradient background, white text, subtle drop shadow.")
    text.textLine("• Hover: Slight scale (1.02) and stronger shadow; do not darken gradient.")
    text.textLine("• Disabled: Gradient at ~40% opacity, label remains legible (AA contrast).")
    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Pills, Tags & Badges")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Cleaner tier badges use pill shapes with clear labels (Bronze, Silver, Gold, Platinum).")
    text.textLine("• Status badges (Approved, In Progress, Disputed) use Fresh Mint or warning colors sparingly.")
    c.drawText(text)
    c.showPage()

    c.save()


def create_messaging_manual_pdf(path):
    c = canvas.Canvas(path, pagesize=PAGE_SIZE)
    w, h = PAGE_WIDTH, PAGE_HEIGHT

    # Title
    c.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 32)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-1.2*inch, "PureTask Messaging & Positioning")
    c.setFont("Helvetica", 16)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-1.7*inch, "Taglines • Bios • Value Propositions • Voice")
    c.showPage()

    # Core Positioning
    c.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 24)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-1.0*inch, "1. Core Positioning")

    text = c.beginText(1*inch, h-1.6*inch)
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("What PureTask Is")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• A platform/app (like Uber, but for cleaning) where clients can:")
    text.textLine("  - Book verified cleaners in minutes")
    text.textLine("  - Track arrival via GPS check-in/out")
    text.textLine("  - See before & after photos")
    text.textLine("  - Approve the job before payment is released")
    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("What PureTask Is Not")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Not a traditional cleaning company with employees.")
    text.textLine("• Not random classifieds/Craigslist cleaners with no accountability.")
    text.textLine("• Not a franchise — it is a marketplace that connects clients with independent cleaners.")
    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Brand Identity")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Voice: Clean, confident, professional, real.")
    text.textLine("• Vibe: Modern, trustworthy, straightforward.")
    text.textLine("• Emotion: Relief and confidence — “I can finally trust this cleaning.”")
    text.textLine("• Core belief: Transparency builds trust.")
    text.textLine("• Promise: You see the results before you pay.")
    c.drawText(text)
    c.showPage()

    # Taglines

    text.textLine("   and pay only when you approve.”")
    text.textLine("")

    text.textLine("Social & Short-Form Options")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• “PureTask — like Uber, but for cleaning.”")
    text.textLine("• “Book. Clean. Approve. Pay.”")
    text.textLine("• “Cleaning, without the guesswork.”")
    text.textLine("• “Cleaning done right — with proof.”")

    text.textLine("• “Set your rates. Build your reputation. Get paid weekly.”")

    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Brand Voice Guidelines")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Always be clear and direct. Avoid corporate jargon or over-promises.")
    text.textLine("• Emphasize transparency, proof, and control for the client.")
    text.textLine("• For cleaners, emphasize fairness, independence, and earning potential.")
    text.textLine("• Use simple language at a 6th–8th grade reading level.")
    c.drawText(text)
    c.showPage()

    c.save()


def create_logo_usage_pdf(path):
    c = canvas.Canvas(path, pagesize=PAGE_SIZE)
    w, h = PAGE_WIDTH, PAGE_HEIGHT

    # Title
    c.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 32)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-1.2*inch, "PureTask Logo Usage Guide")
    c.setFont("Helvetica", 16)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-1.7*inch, "Lockups • Spacing • Backgrounds • Do & Don’t")
    c.showPage()

    # Core Logo Rules
    c.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 24)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-1.0*inch, "1. Core Logo Rules")

    text = c.beginText(1*inch, h-1.6*inch)
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Primary Logo")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Use the full PureTask wordmark with icon as the default logo in most cases.")
    text.textLine("• The primary version uses PureTask Blue (#0078FF) with Aqua accent (#00D4FF).")
    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Minimum Size")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Digital: Do not display the logo smaller than 24px in height.")
    text.textLine("• Print: Do not display the logo smaller than 0.5 inches in height.")
    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Clear Space")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Maintain clear space around the logo equal to the height of the “P” in PureTask.")
    text.textLine("• No text, icons, or UI elements should overlap this clear space.")
    c.drawText(text)
    c.showPage()

    # Backgrounds & Color Variants
    c.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 24)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-1.0*inch, "2. Backgrounds & Variants")

    text = c.beginText(1*inch, h-1.6*inch)
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Approved Backgrounds")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Soft Cloud (#F7F9FC) — preferred background for most marketing and product UI.")
    text.textLine("• White (#FFFFFF) — safe for documents, PDFs, and investor decks.")
    text.textLine("• Deep Graphite Slate (#1D2533) — for dark mode or hero sections, with white logo.")
    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Logo Color Variants")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Full-color logo: Use on light backgrounds (Soft Cloud or white).")
    text.textLine("• White logo: Use on dark backgrounds (Graphite Slate or dark imagery).")
    text.textLine("• Avoid using the logo in arbitrary colors or gradients outside the brand palette.")
    c.drawText(text)
    c.showPage()

    # Do & Don't
    c.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 24)
    c.drawString(1*inch, h-1.0*inch, "3. Do & Don’t")

    text = c.beginText(1*inch, h-1.6*inch)
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Do")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Use the logo at sufficient size so it is always legible.")
    text.textLine("• Maintain the aspect ratio; scale uniformly.")
    text.textLine("• Use approved color variants based on background tone.")
    text.textLine("• Place logo in corners or header areas with enough white space.")
    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Don’t")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Don’t stretch, skew, or rotate the logo.")
    text.textLine("• Don’t apply drop shadows, outlines, or extra effects not in the brand system.")
    text.textLine("• Don’t place the logo over busy photos where it becomes hard to read.")
    text.textLine("• Don’t change the colors outside the PureTask brand palette.")
    text.textLine("")
    text.setFont("Helvetica-Bold", 14)
    text.textLine("Favicon & App Icon")
    text.setFont("Helvetica", 12)
    text.textLine("• Use the simplified PureTask icon (without text) for favicons and app icons.")
    text.textLine("• Ensure enough contrast on both light and dark OS themes.")
    c.drawText(text)
    c.showPage()

    c.save()

4. PURETASK CREDIT SYSTEM — FULL MANUAL
Purpose: Create a closed-loop economy that improves trust, cash flow, and platform engagement.

1. What Credits Are
Credits are a non-cash service unit used to book cleaning time on PureTask.

They are NOT:

cash

redeemable money

transferable between users

They ARE:

a psychological spending tool

a unit of cleaning value

a way to hold funds in escrow safely

a method for measuring cleaner earnings

Clients buy credits.
Cleaners earn credits.

2. Credit Flow
Client purchases credits

Credits go to the client’s wallet

Client books a cleaner

Required credits are held in escrow

Cleaner completes the job

Client approves

Credits are released to the cleaner

Cleaner converts credits → payout during weekly ACH (or instant payout with fee)

3. Escrow Logic
A 25% buffer is added during booking to avoid mid-job credit shortages.

Example:

Estimated hours: 3

Rate: 30 credits/hr

Base: 90

25% buffer → 112.5

System holds 113 credits

If job ends early: unused credits are released back to the wallet.
If job runs long: client is prompted to top up credits.

4. Credit Types (Ledger Entries)
Type	Description
purchase	Client buys credits
hold	Credits reserved for a job
release	Credits returned to client (unused)
charge	Credits paid to cleaner for completed work
refund	Credits returned due to dispute
reversal	Rare admin corrections
Mirrored in database: CreditTransactions

5. Why Credits Work
Psychological + business advantages:

Credits feel lighter than dollars (“90 credits” feels less painful than “$135 + fees”).

Encourages preloading (Starbucks model).

Keeps money inside PureTask longer.

Avoids money transmitter licensing (credits are not stored cash).

Allows promotions (e.g., “Buy 100 credits, get 10 free”).

Allows referrals (“Earn 25 credits”).

6. Cleaner Payout Conversion
Credits → payout:

Credits earned × payout percentage = real money earnings

Example:

500 credits earned

80% payout rate

Cleaner receives → $400

PureTask revenue → $100

Payout percentage varies by tier.

7. Legal Protection
Credits must be defined as:

non-cash

non-redeemable

service units

not a stored-value financial product

This avoids money transmitter laws and keeps only Stripe handling funds.

────────────────────────────
5. CLEANER TIER SYSTEM & RELIABILITY PROTOCOL
This system motivates good cleaner behavior and improves marketplace trust.

1. Tiers
Tier	Reliability Score	Visibility	Rate Power	Payout %
Bronze	0–69	Lowest	Limited	80%
Silver	70–84	Standard	Medium	80%
Gold	85–94	High priority	High	82%
Platinum	95–100	Top priority	Maximum	85%
Higher tiers unlock:

higher hourly rates in credits

priority exposure to clients

higher earnings (%)

2. Reliability Score (0–100)
Action	Score Change
On-time arrival (GPS check-in)	+20
Before & after photos uploaded	+15
5-star rating	+15
Late cancellation	−25
No-show	−50
Client marks job incomplete	−30
Score continuously updates after every job.

3. Hourly Rate Ranges (by Tier)
Base Rate (credits/hr)

Bronze: 15–22

Silver: 22–30

Gold: 30–38

Platinum: 38–45

Add-ons (credits/hr)

Bronze/Silver: +2 to +5

Gold/Platinum: +3 to +5

4. Cleaner Behavior Loop
Do good work

Earn credits

Earn bonuses

Improve tier

Get better visibility

Earn more money

Reinforce good behavior

This gamifies the entire platform.

5. Tier-Based Bonuses
Perfect check-in + photos: +5 credits

3 jobs with all 5-star reviews: +25 credits

30 days perfect reliability: +50 credits + auto tier upgrade

────────────────────────────
6. CLIENT WALLET + BOOKING + APPROVAL SYSTEM
1. Client Wallet
Client wallet stores credit balance:

Balance = purchases + releases + refunds − holds − charges

Wallet features:

“Add credits” button

History of transactions

Unused credits never expire while account is active

Credits cannot be cashed out

2. Booking Flow
Step 1 — Select cleaner
Cleaners are shown with:

reliability score

tier badge

hourly rate

reviews

Step 2 — Select cleaning type

Basic

Deep

Move-out

Each adds/subtracts credits/hr.

Step 3 — Choose hours
System calculates estimated credits + buffer.

Step 4 — Hold credits
Client approves hold → credits move to escrow.

3. Job In Progress
Cleaner:

GPS check-in

Uploads before photos

Completes job

Uploads after photos

GPS check-out

Client sees:

timer

status

held credits

potential top-up alert

4. Approval Flow
After job:

Client sees:

before/after

time worked

final credits owed

Client chooses:

Approve → credits release to cleaner

Dispute → credits held, case opened

Refunds return credits to wallet immediately after resolution.

5. Why This System Works
For clients:

transparent

track everything

approve before paying

dispute protection

For cleaners:

fair

performance-based

clear earnings

For PureTask:

reduced fraud

reduced disputes

increased trust

predictable economics

7. JOB LIFECYCLE SPECIFICATION
This document explains the complete flow of a job from creation to approval or dispute, including all system events and triggers.

1. Job Statuses (Full List)
Every job in PureTask moves through these stages:

created — client sets up job and selects cleaner

accepted — cleaner accepts the job

in_progress — cleaner checks in via GPS

completed — cleaner checks out, job time recorded

awaiting_client — client reviews photos + time before approving

approved — client approves, credits released

disputed — client raises a dispute

cancelled — client or cleaner cancels before job start

These statuses match the backend workflow and automation triggers.

2. Lifecycle Flow (Step-by-Step)
STEP 1 — Client Creates Job
Client:

selects cleaner

selects date + time

selects service type (basic, deep, move-out)

chooses estimated hours

System:

calculates required credits

adds buffer

holds credits from wallet

Status: created

STEP 2 — Cleaner Accepts Job
Cleaner receives:

push notification

SMS

email

Cleaner can:

Accept

Decline

Accepted → Status: accepted
Declined → Job opens for other cleaners or returns to the client.

STEP 3 — Cleaner Arrives & Checks In
At arrival, cleaner must:

tap “Check In”

system verifies GPS coordinates

cleaner uploads before photos

Status: in_progress

STEP 4 — Job Completion
Cleaner:

taps “Check Out”

uploads after photos

System:

calculates time worked

determines final credits owed

Status: completed

STEP 5 — Client Review
Client sees:

before/after photos

time worked

total credits to be charged

Client chooses:

Approve job

Dispute job

If approve → Status: approved
If dispute → Status: disputed

STEP 6 — Credits Release
If approved:

credits move from escrow → cleaner earnings

ledger updates

cleaner earnings added to next payout

If disputed:

credits remain in escrow

support reviews case

outcomes:

→ refund credits to client
→ partial release
→ full release to cleaner
→ job removal

3. Cancellation Rules
Client cancels
More than 24 hours before: no penalty

Less than 24 hours: cancellation fee deducted

Within 3 hours: late cancel fee

Cleaner cancels
Reliability score penalty

Job offered to other cleaners

4. Automated Notifications (n8n workflows)
Triggered during lifecycle:

New job → cleaner invitation

24-hour reminder → client + cleaner

1-hour reminder → client + cleaner

Check-in missing alert

Job completed → client approval request

Dispute opened

These align with your automation bundle.

────────────────────────────
8. CLEANER EARNINGS & PAYOUT SYSTEM
1. How Cleaners Earn Money
Cleaners earn credits for time worked.

Credits earned × payout % = earnings deposited to cleaner

Cleaner payout % is based on tier:

Tier	Payout %
Bronze	80%
Silver	80%
Gold	82%
Platinum	85%
Example:

100 credits earned

Gold cleaner (82%) → earns $82

2. Weekly Payout Schedule
Payouts occur:

Every Friday

via Stripe Connect (ACH payout)

Earnings included:
All approved jobs from Monday → Sunday before payout.

Rejected/disputed jobs are excluded until resolved.

3. Instant Payouts (Optional for Cleaners)
Cleaners can tap “Instant Payout” to receive funds instantly.

Fee:

Standard 3–5% (Stripe instant payout fee)

PureTask may add a small markup (e.g., +1%)

Instant payout is:

optional

capped per day

only available for approved earnings

4. Cleaner Earnings Dashboard
Displays:

total credits earned

earnings this week

estimated Friday payout

instant payout balance

reliability score

tier

job history

Cleaners clearly see:

how much they earned

how much they will earn

how to earn more

5. Internal Accounting Mechanics
Ledger stores:

credits earned

credits pending (awaiting approval)

credits disputed

real money owed

payout transactions

Stripe transfer IDs

This ensures:

transparency

auditability

compliance

6. Why This System Works
Cleaners stay motivated (tier + reliability = higher pay)

Cleaners get paid weekly → stable income

Instant payout → fast access → highly motivating

PureTask retains revenue via % spreads

────────────────────────────
9. LEGAL & COMPLIANCE FRAMEWORK
1. Credit Definitions (Important Legal Language)
Credits must always be described as:

non-refundable digital service units

not cash

no intrinsic monetary value

cannot be redeemed by clients

This protects PureTask from:

Money Transmitter regulations

Banking compliance

Stored-value rules

This language appears in the Terms of Service and UI copy.

2. Cleaner Classification
Cleaners are:

Independent Contractors

Not employees

PureTask:

does NOT control scheduling

does NOT require uniforms

does NOT set fixed hourly rates (cleaners choose within tier ranges)

does NOT dictate how cleaners perform the job

This protects against misclassification lawsuits.

3. Liability Limitations
PureTask:

is NOT responsible for damages caused by cleaners

is NOT a bank

does NOT hold funds (Stripe does)

is NOT an escrow agent

Clients agree to:

platform terms

having cleaners as independent service providers

Cleaners agree to:

reliability rules

payout policies

dispute policies

4. Dispute Resolution Policies
If a client disputes a job:

credits remain frozen

PureTask evaluates evidence

final decision may be:

full refund

partial refund

release to cleaner

Photos + GPS tracking protect both sides.

5. Terms of Service Requirements
Must include:

credit system definition

expiration rules

independent contractor language

cancellation fees

dispute flow

liability disclaimers

Stripe Connect compliance

arbitration clause (recommended)

10. DATABASE SCHEMA GUIDE (PureTask Data Model)
This is the backbone of the entire platform.

1. USERS TABLE (Clients + Cleaners + Admins)
Holds identity and role-based fields.

Key Fields
id (primary key)

role (enum: client | cleaner | admin)

email, phone, name

status (active | suspended)

Client-specific fields
wallet_credits_balance (number)

Cleaner-specific fields
tier (bronze | silver | gold | platinum)

base_rate_credits_per_hour

deep_addon_credits_per_hour

moveout_addon_credits_per_hour

reliability_score

payout_percentage

stripe_connect_id

avg_rating

jobs_completed

2. CREDIT TRANSACTIONS TABLE
Immutable ledger for all client credit movements.

Field	Purpose
id	primary key
client_id	FK → Users
type	purchase, hold, release, charge, refund, reversal
amount_credits	signed number
job_id	nullable FK
note	optional
created_at	timestamp
Wallet balance =
(purchase + release + refund) − (hold + charge)

3. JOBS TABLE
Represents a booked cleaning appointment.

Core Fields
id

client_id

cleaner_id

status

created

accepted

in_progress

completed

awaiting_client

approved

disputed

cancelled

Pricing Snapshot (VERY IMPORTANT)
To prevent price changes mid-job:

snapshot_base_rate_cph

snapshot_deep_addon_cph

snapshot_moveout_addon_cph

snapshot_hours_estimate

snapshot_total_credits_held

Job Activity Fields
cleaner_check_in_time

cleaner_check_out_time

gps_check_in_lat

gps_check_in_lon

gps_check_out_lat

gps_check_out_lon

before_photos[]

after_photos[]

actual_hours_worked

4. PAYOUTS TABLE
Tracks real money owed + Stripe payouts.

id

cleaner_id

amount_usd

status (pending, processing, paid, failed)

stripe_transfer_id

period_start

period_end

5. INDEXING STRATEGY
To keep the system extremely fast:

index Jobs on:
(cleaner_id), (client_id), (status)

index CreditTransactions on:
(client_id), (job_id)

index Users on:
(role), (email), (phone)

11. AUTOMATION ARCHITECTURE (12 WORKFLOWS)
This section explains the entire n8n automation system used by PureTask.

Based on your workflow export, these are the 12 core automation groups:

1. Stripe Event Ingest
Handles:

payment_intent.succeeded

payment_intent.payment_failed

charge.refunded

charge.dispute.created

transfer.paid

transfer.failed

Purpose:

update wallet

trigger job charge events

handle refunds

handle disputes

validate payouts

2. Credit Purchase Flow
When client buys credits:

verify Stripe payment

add ledger entry (purchase)

update wallet

notify client

3. Job Creation + Cleaner Invitation
Triggered when client creates a job:

calculate credits

hold credits in escrow

notify cleaner(s)

assign job if accepted

4. Check-In Compliance System
Triggered when cleaner checks in:

validate GPS

set status to in_progress

require before photos

alert if cleaner fails to check in

5. Check-Out + Completion Flow
Triggered when cleaner checks out:

compute actual hours

compute final credits

request client approval

6. Client Approval System
Triggered when client approves job:

release credits to cleaner ledger

add earnings

notify cleaner

update financial projections

7. Dispute Management Workflow
Triggered when client disputes:

freeze credits

notify admin

collect photos + logs

resolve → credit refund or release

8. Refund Handling
Triggered by Stripe refund events:

ledger entry: refund

update wallet

notify client

9. Cancellation Workflow
Client or cleaner cancels →
System must:

restore held credits

apply cancellation fees

penalize cleaner reliability (if applicable)

10. Weekly Payout Scheduler
Every Friday:

gather all approved earnings

calculate payout percentages

send Stripe transfers

notify cleaners

11. KPI Reporting Workflow
Daily summary:

new jobs

cancellations

disputes

credit purchases

cleaner performance

revenue

12. Automated Backups
Nightly:

export Users, Jobs, Credits, Ledger

store securely

optionally send to AWS

────────────────────────────
12. EVENT MODEL + BASE44 INTEGRATION GUIDE
This is the “nervous system” that connects app → backend → automations.

1. Event Philosophy
PureTask runs on:

Event-driven architecture
“Whenever something happens, emit an event.”

Events feed directly into n8n and drive:

notifications

payouts

reliability changes

ledger updates

reports

2. Event Format
Each event includes:

{
  "event_name": "job.completed",
  "event_id": "uuid",
  "occurred_at": "timestamp",
  "idempotency_key": "job.completed_<job_id>",
  "actor": { "type": "client | cleaner | system", "id": "123" },
  "payload": {
    "job_id": 99,
    "cleaner_id": 12,
    "client_id": 44
  }
}
3. Event Categories
User Events
user.created

user.updated

cleaner.verified

client.wallet.updated

Job Events
job.created

job.accepted

job.in_progress

job.completed

job.awaiting_client

job.approved

job.disputed

job.cancelled

Financial Events
credits.purchase

credits.hold

credits.release

credits.charge

payout.generated

payout.sent

4. HMAC Signing (Security)
Events are signed using an HMAC secret before being sent to n8n.

Purpose:

authenticate source

prevent tampering

ensure n8n only processes valid events

5. Best Practices
Always include idempotency_key to prevent duplicate processing

Never send raw sensitive data

Keep payload minimal

Emit events at every stage of job lifecycle

✅ PURETASK API SPECIFICATION — PART 1 (CORE STRUCTURE)
This document defines the API structure for PureTask: authentication, users, credits, and base endpoints.
Future messages will deliver Part 2 (Jobs), Part 3 (Credits & Wallet), Part 4 (Payouts), Part 5 (Notifications), and Part 6 (Admin).

────────────────────────────
0. GENERAL API PRINCIPLES
Base URL
https://api.puretask.com/v1

Authentication
PureTask uses JWT Auth for clients & cleaners, and API key for admin/internal systems.

Response Format
All responses use JSON.

Error Format
{
  "error": true,
  "message": "Description of error",
  "code": "ERROR_CODE"
}
Success Format
{
  "success": true,
  "data": { ... }
}
Idempotency
Required for payment-related endpoints

Uses header: Idempotency-Key: <uuid>

Pagination Query Params
?limit=20&offset=0

────────────────────────────
1. AUTHENTICATION ENDPOINTS
1.1 Register User
POST /auth/register
Registers a client or cleaner.

Request
{
  "role": "client",
  "email": "test@example.com",
  "phone": "+15555555555",
  "password": "securepass",
  "name": "John Doe"
}
Response
{
  "success": true,
  "data": {
    "user_id": 44,
    "role": "client",
    "token": "<jwt>"
  }
}
1.2 Login
POST /auth/login
Request
{
  "email": "test@example.com",
  "password": "securepass"
}
Response
{
  "success": true,
  "data": {
    "token": "<jwt>",
    "user": {
      "id": 44,
      "role": "client"
    }
  }
}
1.3 Logout
No server action needed (JWT-based), but included for convention.

POST /auth/logout
Returns:

{ "success": true }
1.4 Request Password Reset
POST /auth/request_password_reset
Triggers SendGrid email template.

{
  "email": "test@example.com"
}
1.5 Reset Password
POST /auth/reset_password
{
  "token": "reset-token",
  "new_password": "newSecurePass123"
}
────────────────────────────
2. USER PROFILE ENDPOINTS
Unified user profiles with role-based fields.

2.1 Get My Profile
GET /user/me
Response shows role-specific fields:

{
  "success": true,
  "data": {
    "id": 12,
    "role": "cleaner",
    "name": "Maria Lopez",
    "email": "maria@example.com",
    "phone": "+15555555555",
    "tier": "gold",
    "reliability_score": 92,
    "base_rate_cph": 32,
    "wallet_credits_balance": 0,
    "stripe_connect_id": "acct_xxxx"
  }
}
2.2 Update Profile
PATCH /user/me
Cleaners can update service areas, bios, rates (within tier limits).

{
  "name": "New Name",
  "bio": "Experienced cleaner with 5 years experience.",
  "service_radius_miles": 20,
  "base_rate_credits_per_hour": 28
}
2.3 Upload Profile Photo
POST /user/me/photo
Multi-part upload.

Response:

{ "success": true, "photo_url": "https://cdn..." }
────────────────────────────
3. CLEANER-SPECIFIC ENDPOINTS
3.1 Get Cleaner Public Profile
GET /cleaner/{cleaner_id}
Clients use this to view:

reliability

tier

rates

reviews

{
  "success": true,
  "data": {
    "id": 12,
    "name": "Maria Lopez",
    "tier": "gold",
    "reliability_score": 92,
    "base_rate_cph": 32,
    "deep_addon_cph": 4,
    "moveout_addon_cph": 5,
    "avg_rating": 4.8,
    "jobs_completed": 112
  }
}
3.2 Cleaner Availability Schedule
GET /cleaner/me/availability
POST /cleaner/me/availability
Cleaners can define days/times they work.

3.3 Cleaner Verification
Triggered after onboarding.

POST /cleaner/me/verification
Upload ID, background check data.

────────────────────────────
4. CLIENT-SPECIFIC ENDPOINTS
4.1 Browse Cleaners
GET /client/cleaners?lat=...&lon=...&date=...
Filters by:

availability

distance

tier

reliability score

4.2 Get Suggested Cleaners
GET /client/suggestions
Uses ranking logic:

distance

tier

reliability

rating

────────────────────────────
5. WALLET & CREDIT ENDPOINTS (Part 1 Overview)
Full detail will be in Part 3, but here’s the core skeleton.

5.1 Get Wallet Balance
GET /wallet
Response:

{
  "success": true,
  "data": {
    "balance_credits": 240
  }
}
5.2 Purchase Credits
Credits are purchased via Stripe payment intent.

POST /wallet/purchase
{
  "credits": 200
}
Backend:

creates Stripe PaymentIntent

returns client_secret

n8n handles confirmation & ledger recording

Response:

{
  "success": true,
  "client_secret": "pi_123_secret_456"
}
5.3 Wallet Transaction History
GET /wallet/transactions
{
  "success": true,
  "data": [
    { "type": "purchase", "amount": 200, "created_at": "..." },
    { "type": "hold", "amount": -80, "job_id": 44 }
  ]
}

Credits added

good events → increase

used for tier placement

=========================================================
SECTION 1A — PURETASK BRAND PHILOSOPHY & POSITIONING (ULTRA EXPANDED)
=========================================================
This section defines the psychological, strategic, emotional, and market-level identity of PureTask.
It answers the foundational questions:

What does PureTask stand for?

What emotional outcome should users experience?

How is PureTask different from other cleaning platforms?

Why does the branding look and sound the way it does?

How should PureTask be perceived (by cleaners, clients, partners, investors)?

This is the guiding philosophy that informs every design decision, UI pattern, wording choice, and feature justification across the entire company.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. BRAND PURPOSE
PureTask exists to create a trusted, transparent, fair cleaning marketplace where both sides—clients and cleaners—benefit equally.

The ultimate purpose:

"To make cleaning services feel as safe, predictable, and controlled as modern ride-share apps."
PureTask is where:

clients feel in control

cleaners feel empowered

the platform remains neutral, fair, and trustworthy

Everything flows from that.

---------------------------------------------------------
2. CORE BRAND PROMISE
“See the results before you pay.”
This is PureTask’s strongest differentiator.

It instantly communicates:

trust

transparency

accountability

client safety

cleaner professionalism

confidence in the product

This is the promise the entire company must uphold.

---------------------------------------------------------
3. BRAND TAGLINE OPTIONS (Primary + Alternates)
Primary Tagline (Official)
“Book trusted cleaners in minutes. Proof before you pay.”

Secondary Options
“Cleaning done right — with proof.”

“Like Uber, but for cleaning.”

“GPS check-in, photos, and approval before payment.”

“Cleaning, without the guesswork.”

Cleaner-Focused
“Earn more by doing great work.”

“Your schedule. Your rates. Your reputation.”

“Photos and reliability become your portfolio.”

---------------------------------------------------------
4. BRAND POSITIONING STATEMENT (Internal Only)
PureTask is a high-trust, transparent cleaning marketplace that uses:

photo verification

GPS accountability

reliability scoring

credit-based payment holds

…to ensure clients always feel safe and cleaners always feel rewarded for professionalism.

PureTask positions itself between:

low-trust platforms (Craigslist, Facebook groups)

high-cost agencies (Merry Maids, Handy)

PureTask owns the middle, where the market is largest and underserved.

---------------------------------------------------------
5. BRAND VALUES (The Non-Negotiables)
A. Transparency
Everything is visible:

GPS check-in/out

before/after photos

time tracking

reliability scores

pricing

No surprises, no uncertainty, no hidden details.

B. Fairness
PureTask is neutral and fair to both sides.

For clients:

approve before paying

disputes are handled with evidence

clear cancellation rules

safety and clarity

For cleaners:

set your own rates

reliable payout schedule

earn more by performing well

clear reliability scoring

fair dispute review

C. Trust-by-Design
PureTask must feel trustworthy at every touchpoint:

friendly tones

simple UI

consistent colors

proof of completion

visible reviews

reliability badges

The brand looks trustworthy so users feel safe.

D. Empowerment
For cleaners:

a path to higher earnings

tier system

reliability boosts

professional identity through photos & ratings

For clients:

control through approvals

clarity through before/after photos

trust through GPS

E. Professionalism
The brand is:

clean

structured

confident

modern

This signals reliability and safety.

---------------------------------------------------------
6. BRAND PERSONALITY (How PureTask Should Feel)
PureTask’s personality is:

Friendly → because it’s a home service

Smart → because it uses tech verification

Competent → because stakes are high (your home)

Trustworthy → the #1 brand trait

Effortless → booking should feel easy

Warm → people-oriented, not corporate

Direct → no fluff in messaging

Modern → gradient, round edges, clear UI

PureTask is NOT:

sarcastic

edgy

corporate

overly formal

overly playful

vague

loud or aggressive

The vibe is:
“Calm, competent, clean, and confident.”

PureTask appeals to:

For Cleaners:

PureTask appeals to cleaners who are:

Cleaner wants:

PureTask delivers that.

PureTask is DIFFERENT because it combines:

A. GPS Check-In/Out
Most cleaning platforms do not verify presence.
PureTask does.

B. Before & After Photo Proof
Clients SEE the work before approving payment.

C. Approve Before Paying
Not possible on traditional agencies.
Not common on gig platforms.

D. Credit-Based Model
A smarter psychological spending system that:

reduces cancellations

smooths cash flow

increases booking likelihood

E. Cleaner Tier & Reliability System
Creates real accountability and real earning potential.

F. Marketplace Neutrality
Neither side feels cheated—PureTask is fair and transparent.

=========================================================
SECTION 1B — TONE OF VOICE, VERBAL IDENTITY & MESSAGING FRAMEWORK (ULTRA EXPANDED)
=========================================================
This section defines how PureTask sounds, communicates, persuades, and builds trust through words.

Where Section 1A defined the brand philosophy,
Section 1B defines the brand voice in practice.

This is essential for:

app microcopy

website content

SMS notifications

onboarding flows

dispute communication

marketing messaging

cleaner recruitment

push notifications

social content

The voice must be consistent across every user-facing touchpoint.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. PURETASK VOICE TRAITS (PRIMARY IDENTITY)
PureTask has 6 core voice traits.
Every word written should reflect these.

Trait 1 — Clear
We say exactly what we mean.
No fluff. No jargon. No corporate speak.

PureTask avoids:

complicated sentences

buzzwords

unnecessary adjectives

Clean communication builds trust.

Trait 2 — Calm
We never sound rushed, aggressive, or chaotic.
We communicate with steady confidence.

Especially during:

disputes

payment issues

lateness

cancellations

Calm tone reduces emotional escalation.

Trait 3 — Friendly
Warm, not cold.
Approachable, not overly formal.

But never silly or childish.

Perfect balance:
Warm + competent.

Trait 4 — Trustworthy
We use factual, verifiable statements.
We explain processes.
We never exaggerate.

Trust is constructed with:

specificity

clarity

transparency

Trait 5 — Helpful
We guide users.
We simplify decisions.
We anticipate confusion and remove it.

PureTask is proactive in communication.

Trait 6 — Professional
Never sloppy.
Never edgy.
Never sarcastic.

We respect the importance of home cleaning and earning livelihoods.

---------------------------------------------------------
2. PURETASK MESSAGING PRINCIPLES (THE “RULES”)
These rules ensure consistency across all content.

Rule 1 — Lead with the proof system
The #1 value is:

before/after photos

GPS check-in/out

approval before payment

Any time we explain the platform, these must appear.

Rule 2 — Avoid fear-based language
PureTask is about safety and control, not fear.

We do NOT say:

“Avoid being scammed.”

“Don’t let cleaners rip you off.”

“Watch out for bad cleaners.”

We say:

“Approve the job before payment is released.”

“See exactly what was cleaned.”

Rule 3 — Speak plainly and directly
Examples:

Not:
“Upon completion, payment is processed automatically.”

Instead:
“When the cleaning is done, you review the photos and approve the job.”

Rule 4 — Neutrality between client and cleaner
We must never sound biased toward one side.

Balanced language:

“Our system protects both clients and cleaners.”

“Approval ensures fairness for everyone.”

Rule 5 — No exaggeration or hype
PureTask does not say:

“Best cleaners in the world!”

“Perfect results guaranteed!”

We say:

“Verified cleaners with reliability scores.”

“Photo proof for every job.”

Rule 6 — Show the process, don’t just state it
Instead of:
“PureTask is trustworthy.”

We say:
“You see before and after photos before you pay.”

---------------------------------------------------------
3. AUDIENCE-SPECIFIC TONES
PureTask communicates differently to clients and cleaners, while staying within brand voice.

3A. Tone for Clients
Primary emotions to create:

safety

confidence

clarity

control

Tone traits:

reassuring

structured

informative

Example phrases:

“Track your cleaner with GPS check-in/out.”

“Review photos before you approve the job.”

“You’re always in control of your booking.”

Avoid:

technical jargon

informal jokes

over-promising

3B. Tone for Cleaners
Primary emotions to create:

empowerment

fairness

opportunity

professionalism

Tone traits:

motivational

respectful

supportive

Example phrases:

“Earn more by building your reliability score.”

“Your work becomes your portfolio.”

“Instant payout available after approved jobs.”

Avoid:

paternalistic language

anything that sounds like an employer

strict demands
PureTask is not their boss; it is a marketplace partner.

---------------------------------------------------------
4. WHAT PURETASK NEVER SAYS (FORBIDDEN LANGUAGE)
These words or styles break trust or professionalism.

Forbidden categories:

A. Fear or danger framing
No:

“scam”

“unsafe”

“danger”

“bad cleaners”

“we protect you from fraud”

Use:

“verified cleaners”

“GPS check-in/out”

“approval before payment”

B. Aggressive marketing hype
No:

“best cleaner ever”

“perfect results guaranteed”

“we promise perfection”

Use:

“professional cleaners with reliability scores”

“proof of every job”

C. Corporate or robotic tone
No:

“Our proprietary technological infrastructure ensures…”

“User satisfaction metrics show…”

Use:

“We make cleaning transparent.”

“Here’s how the process works.”

D. Slang or casual humor
No:

“We gotchu.”

“Clean vibes only.”

“This is sick.”

PureTask is warm but not playful.

---------------------------------------------------------
5. MICROCOPY FRAMEWORKS
Microcopy = small, high-impact moments in UI:

buttons

tooltips

confirmations

notifications

empty states

PureTask microcopy must be:

short

instructive

calm

polite

5A. Buttons
Examples:

“Book Cleaning”

“Approve Job”

“Add Credits”

“Start Check-In”

“View Photos”

“Contact Cleaner”

Avoid:

“Let’s Go!!!”

“Smash This Button”

5B. Empty States
Example for no upcoming jobs:
“You don’t have any upcoming cleanings. Book your first cleaning to get started.”

Example for cleaner job feed:
“No jobs available right now. New bookings appear throughout the day.”

5C. Error Messages
Should:

explain clearly

offer a solution

avoid blame

Example:
“We couldn’t verify your GPS location. Try again outside or turn on location services.”

5D. Success Messages
Calm and confident.

Example:
“Job approved. Your cleaner will receive payment during the next payout cycle.”

---------------------------------------------------------
6. MESSAGE TEMPLATES FOR CORE SCENARIOS
Client → After Job Completion
“Please review the before and after photos. Approve the job to release payment.”

Cleaner → New Job
“You’ve been selected for a new cleaning opportunity. Review the details and accept if available.”

Payment Confirmation
“Your credit purchase was successful. Your updated balance is now available.”

Dispute Notification (Client)
“We’ve received your dispute and are reviewing the photos and details. We’ll update you as soon as we make a decision.”

Dispute Notification (Cleaner)
“A client has opened a dispute for this job. Please review your photos while we investigate.”

Late Cancellation Warning
“Canceling this close to the appointment may affect your reliability score.”

8. MESSAGE STRUCTURE FRAMEWORKS
8A. How to explain a feature
What it does

Why it matters

What it protects

What the user should do

Example:

8B. How to communicate a rule
State the rule

Explain the reason

Describe the consequence

Example:
“Before and after photos are required for every cleaning. They help clients approve jobs safely and ensure fairness for cleaners. Missing photos may affect your reliability score.”

SECTION 1C — VISUAL IDENTITY SYSTEM (ULTRA EXPANDED)
=========================================================
The PureTask visual system must communicate:

clarity

“This platform is clean, fair, and trustworthy.”

---------------------------------------------------------
1. COLOR SYSTEM (FULLY EXPANDED)
PureTask uses a five-color brand palette, each with a defined purpose.

1.1 Primary Colors
PureTask Blue — #0078FF
Role: Action, trust, navigation

Should be used for:

primary buttons

key navigation elements

important highlights

key headers

Psychology:

clean

trustworthy

modern

Never use PureTask Blue for errors, warnings, or negative states.

PureTask Aqua — #00D4FF
Role: Accent, gradients, energy

Used for:

gradient accents

secondary highlights

subtle backgrounds

illustration accents

Psychology:

fresh

modern

“clean water” feeling

1.2 Neutrals
Graphite Slate — #1D2533
Role: High-contrast text, headers, icons

Used for:

primary text

logo version on light backgrounds

card titles

dark mode accents

Avoid using too much Graphite Slate to prevent heaviness.

Soft Cloud — #F7F9FC
Role: Backgrounds, UI surfaces, cards

Used for:

app background

card backgrounds

section separators

Soft Cloud is crucial for PureTask’s clean, airy feel.

Pure White — #FFFFFF
Used for:

full white backgrounds

modal surfaces

contrast against colored CTAs

1.3 Utility Colors
Fresh Mint — #28C76F (Success)
Used for:

approved jobs

success notifications

positive indicators

cleaner tier rewards

Never use Fresh Mint as a primary CTA color.

Safety Orange — #FF9F43 (Warnings)
Used for:

late cancellation warnings

missing check-in alerts

expired time windows

Error Red — #EA5455 (Errors)
Used for:

failed payments

dispute alerts

critical issues

---------------------------------------------------------
2. GRADIENT SYSTEM
PureTask uses a signature gradient:

Blue → Aqua
linear-gradient(90deg, #0078FF, #00D4FF)

This gradient is iconic and should be used for:

primary buttons

hero section backgrounds

onboarding screens

marketing graphics

app store screenshots

Gradient rules:

Should always flow Blue → Aqua (never reversed)

Angle can be 90° or 135°; never 0° or 180°

Should not be used behind text-heavy blocks

Avoid using gradient for background + button simultaneously

---------------------------------------------------------
3. TYPOGRAPHY SYSTEM
PureTask typography is designed to be:

readable

friendly

modern

trustworthy

3.1 Fonts
Fredoka (Bold, SemiBold, Medium)
Used for:

page titles

section headers

labels

navigation

Traits:

round

friendly

approachable

excellent for branding

Never use Fredoka for long paragraphs.

Verdana (Regular, Bold)
Used for:

all body text

paragraphs

instructions

descriptions

legal text

Traits:

readable

neutral

highly accessible

3.2 Typographic Hierarchy
Title / H1
Font: Fredoka Bold
Size: 32–40 px
Use: screen headers, landing hero copy

Section Header / H2
Font: Fredoka SemiBold
Size: 24–28 px

Subheader / H3
Font: Fredoka Medium
Size: 18–22 px

Body Text
Font: Verdana Regular
Size: 15–17 px

Small Text / Notes
Font: Verdana Regular
Size: 12–14 px

UI Labels
Font: Fredoka Medium
Size: 13–15 px

---------------------------------------------------------
4. SPACING & LAYOUT SYSTEM
PureTask’s spacing structure follows a 4-point grid.

The spacing increments:

4

8

12

16

24

32

48

Rules:

never use odd or inconsistent spacing

maintain consistent padding inside components

space sections with 24–48px separation

White space is a core part of the brand.
Crowding destroys trust.

---------------------------------------------------------
5. BUTTON SYSTEM (THE PURETASK PILL COMPONENT)
PureTask buttons use the signature full-pill shape, representing:

friendliness

modernity

cleanliness

smoothness

simplicity

5.1 Primary Button
Gradient (Blue → Aqua)
Text color: white
Shape: pill (radius: 9999px)
Padding: 14px vertical, 32px horizontal
Font: Fredoka Medium

Used for:

booking actions

approvals

payment steps

major actions

Never:

add borders

use all caps

add icons without spacing rules

5.2 Secondary Button
Background: Soft Cloud or white
Border: 1px Blue
Text: Blue

Used for:

lesser actions

filtering

“view details”

5.3 Destructive Button
Background: Error Red
Text: white

Used rarely:

dispute submission

cancel job

5.4 Disabled Button States
Gradient at 40% opacity
Text at 60% opacity
Cursor default

---------------------------------------------------------
6. CARD SYSTEM (COMPONENT SPECIFICATION)

history items

Elements:

16px padding

photo left, text right

badge top right

6.2 Job Card
Elements:

date/time

cleaner photo

CTA button

7. BADGES & LABELS
Badges communicate trust, status, or alerts.

7.1 Tier Badges
Colors by tier:

Bronze → muted brown
Silver → metallic grey
Gold → warm gold
Platinum → cool white/blue gradient

Rules:

always pill-shaped

short text (Bronze, Silver, Gold, Platinum)

7.2 Status Badges
Approved → Fresh Mint
In Progress → Blue
Awaiting Approval → Aqua
Disputed → Orange or Red

---------------------------------------------------------
8. SHADOWS & DEPTH SYSTEM
Use very subtle shadows—PureTask is clean and soft.

Standard Card Shadow
rgba(0,0,0,0.04)
y = 4px
blur = 12px

Button Shadow
rgba(0,0,0,0.08)
y = 2px
blur = 8px

Never use harsh shadows or large blurs.

---------------------------------------------------------
9. ICONOGRAPHY SYSTEM
PureTask icons must be:

simple

line-based

2px stroke

rounded corners

consistent scale

Icons should feel:

friendly

modern

minimal

Avoid:

filled icons

inconsistent stroke thickness

cartoon icons

---------------------------------------------------------
10. IMAGERY SYSTEM
PureTask imagery must be:

real

clean

clear

bright

10.1 Before/After Images
Rules:

must show identical angles

good lighting

no filters

no collage or dramatic templates

photos should be calm and neutral

10.2 Cleaner Photos
Rules:

natural lighting

friendly neutral expressions

plain or tidy backgrounds

avoid busy environments

10.3 Marketing Photos
Themes:

real homes

real cleaning work

minimal aesthetic

clean surfaces

warm tones

Avoid:

staged stock photos

chaotic rooms

unrealistic lighting

over-commercial aesthetics

---------------------------------------------------------
11. LAYOUT PRINCIPLES
11.1 PureTask Layout Philosophy
structure + clarity

whitespace heavy

clear top-to-bottom flow

no clutter or visual noise

11.2 Section Spacing
Use 32px or 48px between major sections.
Use 16px inside cards.
Use 12px inside smaller components.

11.3 Alignment
Left-align text.
Center large headers occasionally, never frequently.
Keep cards aligned in grids of 2 or 3 columns.

---------------------------------------------------------
12. CONSISTENCY RULES
PureTask design must:

use consistent spacing

use consistent color roles

use consistent typography

avoid unnecessary elements

maintain brand personality

stay minimal

Consistency = trust.

---------------------------------------------------------
13. MOTION PRINCIPLES
PureTask uses subtle, not flashy, motion.

Rules:

small ease-in-out transitions

button hover scale: 1.02

dropdown fade: 100–150ms

no bouncy animations

no overshoot animations

Motion should feel:

smooth

calming

modern

---------------------------------------------------------
14. ACCESSIBILITY RULES
minimum contrast ratio: 4.5:1

text never below 13px

avoid text over images

ensure button labels are clear

tap targets: 44px minimum

---------------------------------------------------------
15. BRAND SIGNATURE
The final, accumulated look of PureTask should communicate:

“Clean, friendly, modern trust.”

If a design feels:

cluttered

sharp

dark

heavy

overly playful

overly corporate

…it’s not PureTask.

SECTION 1D — IMAGERY, ICONOGRAPHY, & GRAPHIC LANGUAGE (ULTRA EXPANDED)
=========================================================
This section defines how PureTask visually communicates trust, professionalism, and clarity through photos, icons, graphics, illustrations, and layouts.

Everything here must be followed strictly to ensure:

brand cohesion

user trust

marketplace clarity

visual cleanliness

platform professionalism

PureTask is a visual trust product.
The imagery matters more than in almost any other app category.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. IMAGERY PRINCIPLES (THE CORE PHILOSOPHY)
PureTask imagery must express:

cleanliness

evidence

transparency

authenticity

trustworthiness

brightness

calmness

This means PureTask should always use images that feel:

real

natural

bright

minimally edited

cleanly composed

calm

And images/themes to avoid:

dark rooms

staged advertisements

messy stock photos

exaggerated before/after collages

dramatic lighting

PureTask is not selling “extreme transformations.”
We are selling:
trust. proof. transparency. clarity.

---------------------------------------------------------
2. BEFORE & AFTER PHOTO STANDARDS (CRITICAL)
These photos are the heart of the PureTask proof system.

They must be:

clean

consistent

angle-matched

well-lit

honest

Below are detailed rules for:

cleaners

clients

platform review

marketing teams

2.1 Before Photo Rules for Cleaners
Cleaners MUST follow these rules:

At least two angles per room

Show the full space (not just close-ups)

No tilted camera angles

No heavy shadows

Show real condition — do not tidy before taking photos

Avoid any personal reflections or sensitive objects

Keep camera at chest level for consistency

Turn on lights when possible

Objective:
Capture the “real starting point” with honesty and clarity.

2.2 After Photo Rules for Cleaners
Cleaners MUST:

Match the angle of the before photo

Ensure lights are on

Show the entire area cleaned

Avoid filters

Avoid wide-angle distortion

Capture details: counters, floors, bathroom surfaces

Take photos immediately after cleaning

Objective:
Visually prove the quality of work in a standardized, fair way.

2.3 Automatic Before/After Photo Approval Logic (Platform Rules)
The platform may expand into automated image checks:

angle similarity detection

brightness/luminosity check

photo completeness scoring

tagging of missing rooms

blurry image detection

These do not block job completion but help guide reliability scoring.

---------------------------------------------------------
3. CLEANER PROFILE PHOTOGRAPHY STANDARDS
A cleaner’s profile photo is crucial for trust.

Cleaners MUST:
use a clear, front-facing photo

have good lighting

avoid sunglasses or hats

use a neutral or tidy background

have a friendly, natural expression

ensure no clutter is visible

Cleaners MUST NOT:
use group photos

use selfies taken in cars

use dark or blurry images

use unprofessional photos (mirror selfies, filters, etc.)

use photos with other people in the background

3.1 Why It Matters
Client trust increases significantly when:

they see a real face

the photo looks professional

the image is clean and not distracting

Cleaners who upload strong profile photos convert more job assignments.

---------------------------------------------------------
4. ICONOGRAPHY SYSTEM (ULTRA DETAILED)
PureTask icons must be:

simple

rounded

line-based

friendly

2px stroke

visually consistent

Icons communicate reliability and clarity.

4.1 Icon Style Summary
Line icons, not filled

Rounded corners

2px consistent stroke width

Simple geometric shapes

No irregular shapes or abstract art

No shadows or gradients inside icons

Icons should “breathe,” not be cramped

4.2 Icon Themes Used in PureTask UI
cleaning tools

checkmark

timer / clock

location pin

GPS signal

camera

stars (ratings)

shield (trust)

wallet

credit icon

document icon

dispute icon

house outline

Each icon must be:

proportionally balanced

optically centered

aligned to component grid

4.3 Icon Usage Rules
icons should appear in lists, cards, and navigation

icons never replace text (they support it)

icons should be secondary, not dominant

---------------------------------------------------------
5. ILLUSTRATION STYLE (MARKETING & ONBOARDING)
PureTask uses minimal, line-based, soft-colored illustrations where appropriate.

Illustration rules:
simple shapes

soft shadows or none at all

pastel or neutral backgrounds

minimal text

clean compositions

ensure illustrations speak “trust + clarity”

Illustrations should not:

appear childish

be overly cartoonish

use bright or harsh colors

include too many elements

Illustrations are used sparingly:

onboarding screens

website hero sections

explainer materials

---------------------------------------------------------

PureTask uses:

pill-shaped components

rounded rectangles

modern + friendly + trustworthy.

6.1 Shape Vocabulary
Allowed:

Not allowed:

sharp edges

triangles

jagged shapes

chaotic compositions

6.2 Layout Themes
strong vertical flow

left-aligned text

large top padding

relaxed breathing room

simple header → content → CTA structure

PureTask marketing uses evidence-driven imagery.

wallet credits & payouts

Marketing must always feel:

bright

7.1 What Marketing Must Avoid
exaggerated transformations

fake reviews

staged stock cleaning

overly “glam” homes

meme-style graphics

cluttered text

PureTask = professional, modern, calm.

8. PHOTO DO’S AND DON’TS
This is critical for brand consistency.

DO:
use natural lighting

clean, minimal backgrounds

show real cleaning tools

keep compositions simple

DON’T:
use heavy filters

over-saturate colors

show messy, chaotic environments unless for before-photos

show unsafe behaviors

include children in photos

include pets

include personal clutter in cleaner portraits

horizontal scroll or grid

swipe-friendly

full-screen view on tap

zoom allowed

crisp edges, no rounded corners for proof photos

9.2 Cleaner Profile Image
Rules:

round frame

consistent padding

centered

no filters

high resolution

9.3 Job Feed Images
Used sparingly:

cleaner profile

Should visualize:

safety

professionalism

Understood — proceeding now with the full ultra-expanded SECTION 1E.

This section is crucial because it defines the Brand Architecture — how PureTask’s brand adapts, communicates, and positions itself differently depending on who it is speaking to.

PureTask serves three different audiences with very different emotional needs and motivations:

Clients (safety, trust, clarity)

Cleaners (opportunity, fairness, empowerment)

General public / marketing audiences (credibility, brand understanding)

The brand must feel unified while communicating different value systems to each group.

This section describes exactly how to do that.

=========================================================
SECTION 1E — BRAND ARCHITECTURE FOR PRODUCT, MARKETING, AND CLEANERS (ULTRA EXPANDED)
=========================================================
Brand Architecture = The structured system that determines:

the messaging pillars

the tone per audience

the emotional outcomes per audience

the communication style

how PureTask expresses value

how trust and opportunity are framed

how the brand adapts per use case

how the platform “feels” to each side

This is how PureTask maintains ONE unified brand with DIFFERENT messaging to each audience.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. THE THREE AUDIENCE SEGMENTS
PureTask serves:

1. Clients
Emotional need: Safety + Confidence
Decision drivers: proof, transparency, reliability

2. Cleaners
Emotional need: Opportunity + Fairness
Decision drivers: income potential, empowerment

3. Broader Marketplace / Public
Emotional need: Understanding + Credibility
Decision drivers: brand clarity, simplicity, and consistency

Each group must feel addressed, seen, and understood, but the brand must stay unified.

---------------------------------------------------------
2. CORE ARCHITECTURE PRINCIPLE
PureTask balances two sides of the marketplace without favoring one.

The brand must feel:

neutral

fair

structured

balanced

trustworthy

PureTask is not a typical gig platform.
It is not an agency.
It is an evidence-driven marketplace.

The brand architecture reflects that neutrality.

---------------------------------------------------------
3. PURETASK’S THREE BRAND PILLARS (Across All Audiences)
These are the non-negotiables:

Pillar 1 — Transparency
Everything is visible:

photos

GPS timestamp

reliability

pricing

approval process

Pillar 2 — Accountability
Every job is proven:

cleaners are credited for real work

clients pay only when satisfied

Pillar 3 — Empowerment
The platform empowers:

clients to trust

cleaners to earn

the market to operate fairly

These pillars are constant across audiences.

---------------------------------------------------------
4. BRAND COMMUNICATION TO CLIENTS (DEEP DIVE)
Core Emotional Outcome:
“I feel safe and in control.”

Client Pain Points:
worry about hiring strangers

inconsistent cleaning quality

unexpected costs

no accountability from cleaners

confusing scheduling

lack of transparency

Clients want:

reliability

clarity

proof

simplicity

fairness

Messaging Pillars for Clients:
A. Transparency in Every Step
“You see before & after photos before paying.”

B. Control Over Payment
“You approve every job. Nothing is charged automatically.”

C. Verified Professionals
“Cleaners are verified, rated, and scored for reliability.”

D. Accountability
“GPS check-in shows when they arrived. Photos show what they cleaned.”

E. Stress-Free Booking
“Book in minutes. Everything is automated.”

Tone for Clients
calming

authoritative

reassuring

confidence-building

helpful

Never:

pressure

fear

hyperbole

Client-Facing Brand Language Examples
“Book trusted cleaners with photo proof.”
“See the results before you pay.”
“You’re always in control.”
“Your cleaner provides photo proof after each job.”
“Approve or dispute with one tap.”

Client Trust Signals
PureTask must reinforce trust visually with:

clear UI

bright imagery

easy-to-understand buttons

badges (Verified Cleaner, High Reliability, GPS Confirmed)

timeline visualizations

---------------------------------------------------------
5. BRAND COMMUNICATION TO CLEANERS (DEEP DIVE)
Core Emotional Outcome:
“I can earn more and build a career here.”

Cleaner Pain Points:
low pay from agencies

inconsistent paychecks

unfair treatment

no protection against false complaints

no career progression

Cleaners want:

fairness

flexibility

growth

reliability

professionalism

predictable income

Messaging Pillars for Cleaners:
A. Earnings & Opportunity
“Earn more when you deliver great work.”

B. Professional Reputation
“Your reliability score helps you get more jobs.”

C. Instant Payout
“Cash out approved earnings immediately.”

D. Control Over Your Work
“Set your rates within your tier. Choose your jobs.”

E. Fair Dispute System
“Photo proof protects you from unfair complaints.”

Tone for Cleaners
motivational

respectful

empowering

supportive

direct

Never:

commanding

condescending

employer-like

PureTask is NOT their boss.

PureTask is the marketplace that helps them shine and earn more.

Cleaner-Facing Brand Language Examples
“PureTask rewards reliability with higher-tier earnings.”
“Build a career, not just a side gig.”
“Your work becomes your portfolio.”
“Instant payout when your job is approved.”
“The more reliable you are, the more you earn.”

Cleaner Opportunity Signals
Visual elements:

tier badges

reliability score dashboard

earnings previews

payout summaries

growth tips

These reinforce the idea:
“Your effort = your income.”

=========================================================
SECTION 1G — ANTI-PATTERNS (WHAT PURETASK MUST NEVER DO OR SAY)
=========================================================
PureTask is a trust-critical marketplace.
This section defines the exact behaviors, phrases, visual choices, and UX patterns PureTask must avoid at all times.

These are “brand red flags” that weaken credibility, damage trust, or make PureTask seem like an unsafe or unprofessional platform.

This is the "DO NOT DO" list.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. VERBAL ANTI-PATTERNS (LANGUAGE TO NEVER USE)
These forbidden categories protect the brand tone.

1.1 Fear-Based Messaging
PureTask must never use language that invokes fear, danger, or personal risk.

Forbidden examples:

“Avoid getting scammed.”

“Protect yourself from bad cleaners.”

“Don’t let them rip you off.”

“Stop dangerous workers from entering your home.”

Why:
Fear undermines trust and creates emotional volatility.

Correct tone:
Empowering, calm, factual.

Approved alternative:

“Every job includes GPS arrival confirmation and photo proof.”

1.2 Over-Promising or Unrealistic Claims
PureTask must never say:

“Guaranteed perfect results.”

“100% satisfaction guaranteed.”

“Flawless cleaning every time.”

Why:
Cleaning is subjective; PureTask cannot guarantee perfection.

Approved alternative:

“Approve the job when you’re satisfied with the results.”

1.3 Gig-App Language
PureTask is NOT a gig app or low-trust platform.

Never refer to cleaners as:

“gig workers”

“side hustlers”

“taskers”

“cheap cleaners”

Never refer to PureTask as:

a “gig app”

a “cheap cleaning service”

a “job board”

Approved language:

“professional cleaners”

“Marketplace for trusted cleaning services”

“verified cleaners”

“earn more through reliability”

1.4 Corporate or Bureaucratic Tone
Avoid cold, formal, overly complex language.

Forbidden:

“The user is obligated to adhere to system protocols.”

“Operational compliance deviations will be penalized.”

Approved:

“Please follow the check-in steps to stay compliant.”

1.5 Manipulative or Pressure Language
Forbidden:

“Book now before prices go up!”

“Your home will be dirty if you don’t act.”

PureTask does not pressure clients.

Approved:

“Book when you’re ready. Cleaners are available today.”

1.6 Casual Slang or Trendy Speech
Forbidden:

“We gotchu.”

“Clean vibes only.”

“This is insanely good.”

PureTask is warm, but not silly.

---------------------------------------------------------
2. VISUAL & UI ANTI-PATTERNS
This section ensures PureTask’s UI maintains a premium, clean, trustworthy aesthetic.

2.1 Overly Dark Interfaces
PureTask avoids dark, heavy backgrounds because they feel:

intimidating

corporate

distrustful

PureTask must prioritize:

light backgrounds

soft whites

airy neutrals

Dark mode may exist someday, but must remain clean, calm, and minimal.

2.2 Overly Busy Screens
No:

cluttered text

too many buttons

crowded cards

dense data tables

Visual noise = user distrust.

PureTask must always:

simplify

layer information

use space wisely

2.3 Harsh Shadows or Strong Contrast
Avoid:

deep shadows

gradients that look neon

sharp edges

PureTask is soft, calm, and friendly.

2.4 Stock Photos That Look “Fake”
Forbidden:

dramatic staged cleaning shots

models smiling unnaturally

extremely polished homes

stock imagery with gloves & random props

PureTask should use:

real homes

real cleaners

honest lighting

relatable imagery

2.5 Cartoonish Illustrations
Forbidden:

overly cute characters

silly mascots

harsh outlines

exaggerated poses

Illustrations should remain:

minimal

calm

simple

professional

---------------------------------------------------------
3. OPERATIONAL ANTI-PATTERNS
These are rules for support, disputes, and platform operations.

3.1 Taking Sides in Disputes
Support must NEVER say:

“The cleaner was wrong.”

“The client is right.”

“You must resolve this yourselves.”

PureTask is neutral and evidence-driven.

Correct:
“We will review the photos and details to make a fair decision.”

3.2 Allowing Emotionally Reactive Messages
Support should NOT:

mirror client anger

chastise cleaners

over-apologize

Tone must remain:
calm + factual + balanced.

3.3 Punitive Language Toward Cleaners
Never:

“You must…”

“You failed…”

“We are penalizing you…”

Approved:

“This action affects your reliability score.”

“Please follow these steps to stay compliant.”

3.4 Letting Clients Skip Photo Review
Under no circumstances can clients:

approve without seeing photos

skip photo requirement

bypass check-in data

This undermines the core brand promise:
“Proof before you pay.”

---------------------------------------------------------
4. PRODUCT & FEATURE ANTI-PATTERNS
These are UX/feature choices PureTask must never implement.

4.1 Auto-Charging Without Approval
PureTask must NEVER:

auto-complete job approvals

auto-charge without client review

automatically release funds

This breaks the platform’s #1 differentiator.

4.2 Hidden Fees
Forbidden:

cleaning agency-style add-ons

pricing surprises

forced upsells

hidden surcharges

PureTask must remain transparent.

4.3 Letting Cleaners Start Without Check-In
NEVER allow:

manual check-in

retroactive check-in

skip check-in

This would:

destroy trust

enable fraudulent reporting

harm cleaner accountability

4.4 Allowing Partial Photo Uploads to Count as Complete
PureTask image verification must enforce:

consistent angles

minimum number of photos

clear visibility

Inconsistent photo proof breaks the brand.

---------------------------------------------------------
5. BRAND BEHAVIORAL ANTI-PATTERNS
Avoid these psychological mistakes that weaken user trust.

5.1 Being Vague About Rules
No:
“Cleaners must follow all guidelines.”

That is unclear and unhelpful.

Approved:
“Cleaners must upload before-and-after photos for each room.”

5.2 Using Humor to Deflect Problems
PureTask must avoid:
“Oops! Something exploded. Our bad!”

Or:
“Tech gremlins got us again lol.”

Never use humor for:

errors

payments

disputes

compliance issues

5.3 Overly Emotional Messaging
No:

“We are VERY sorry!!!”

“Please don’t be upset.”

Use:
“We understand your concern. Here’s what we’re doing next.”

5.4 Making Cleaners Feel Like Employees
PureTask must not say:

“Your shift starts soon.”

“You must accept this job.”

“Clock in now.”

Correct:

“This job is available if you’d like to accept it.”

---------------------------------------------------------
6. MARKETING ANTI-PATTERNS
PureTask marketing must avoid:

6.1 Overly Promotional Language
No:

“You’ll make a fortune!”

“You’ll never have to worry again!”

Correct:

“Earn more by building your reliability.”

6.2 Fake Testimonials or Staged Content
PureTask must never:

fabricate cleaner stories

exaggerate transformations

use false quotes

Authenticity is essential.

6.3 Aggressive CTAs
No:

“Act now!”

“Don’t miss out!”

“Limited time only!”

Correct:

“Start when you’re ready.”

---------------------------------------------------------
7. LEGAL & TERMS ANTI-PATTERNS
PureTask must avoid language that causes:

misclassification of cleaners

unclear liability

credit misrepresentation

7.1 Never Call Credits “Money”
Credits are service units, not currency.

Forbidden:

“Add money to your wallet.”

“Get paid in cash units.”

Correct:

“Add credits to your wallet.”

7.2 Never Imply Cleaners Are Employees
Forbidden:

“Work for PureTask.”

“PureTask cleaner job.”

Correct:

“Earn on PureTask as an independent professional.”

---------------------------------------------------------
8. SUMMARY OF ALL ANTI-PATTERNS
PureTask must NEVER:

use fear

use hype

use slang

guilt-trip users

auto-charge without approval

allow poor photo proof

create cluttered UI

sound corporate or cold

show staged or fake imagery

misrepresent credits

treat cleaners like employees

take sides in disputes

pressure clients or cleaners

If ANY copy, visual, feature, or message violates these rules:
it must be rewritten or redesigned.

This section protects the brand forever.
