3M — SYSTEM-LEVEL AUTOMATIONS (ULTRA-EXPANDED CANON)
=========================================================
PureTask operates using a deep set of automations across:

Jobs

Cleaners

Clients

Credits

Wallet

Escrow

Payouts

Reliability Engine

Disputes

Notifications

Fraud Detection

Admin Tools

Backups & Logs

KPIs & Analytics

Automation is what transforms PureTask from a manual service into a smart, self-regulating marketplace.

We break automations into 10 major categories.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. JOB LIFECYCLE AUTOMATIONS
These ensure every job moves through the system smoothly.

1.1 Job Assignment Automation
When a client books:

system finds eligible cleaners

sends job to job feed

auto-assigns best cleaner if client chooses “Recommended Cleaner”

uses ranking factors:

tier

reliability

proximity

availability

job type

photos & dispute record

1.2 Pre-Job Reminder Automations
Triggers:

24 hours before

1 hour before

Sent to:

client

cleaner

1.3 Travel Reminder
30 minutes before job, cleaner receives:

“Your job starts soon. It’s time to travel.”

1.4 Check-In Overdue Automation
If cleaner does not check in after start time:

first alert: soft reminder

second alert: urgent reminder

after X minutes:

job flagged

admin alerted

reliability score impacted

1.5 Auto Check-In Override (Admin-Assist)
If cleaner is at location but GPS is malfunctioning:

system captures alternative evidence

admin receives override request

admin can force check-in

1.6 Missing Photo Automation
If cleaner hasn’t uploaded photos:

reminders every 10 minutes

job cannot complete

after 4 reminders → reliability warning

1.7 Auto-Complete Job (Cleaner Forgot to Press Submit)
If after photos uploaded but cleaner didn't finalize:

system asks “Finish Job?”

after X minutes → auto-submit

1.8 Auto-Approval Timer for Clients
If client does not approve job:

sends reminder

sends last reminder

auto-approves after 24 hours

This protects cleaners from client neglect.

---------------------------------------------------------
2. CREDIT SYSTEM AUTOMATIONS
These control the entire financial cycle of credits.

2.1 Escrow Hold Automation
When job is booked:

credits move from wallet → escrow instantly

2.2 Escrow Release Automation
Triggers when:

job approved

dispute resolved

partial payout decided

cancellation rules applied

2.3 Low Credit Warning Automation
If client tries to book with insufficient credits:

notify client

redirect to “Add Credits”

If during job approval (for added time):

notify client “Add credits to complete this job.”

2.4 Credit Expiration Automation
If credits expire after X months:

30 day notice

7 day notice

expiration day text & email

2.5 Refund Automation
When refund triggered by:

dispute

cancellation

platform error

Credits go → client wallet instantly.

---------------------------------------------------------
3. PAYOUT AUTOMATIONS
3.1 Weekly Payout Automation
Every Monday:

compile eligible earnings

send batch to Stripe

generate payout logs

notify cleaners

3.2 Instant Payout Eligibility Check
Trigger before instant payout:

System runs checks:

KYC complete?

fraud flags?

dispute flags?

reliability ≥ threshold?

minimum balance met?

Only then → allow instant payout.

3.3 Payout Failure Detection
If Stripe returns an error:

notify cleaner

log issue

freeze new payouts

ask for bank update

reattempt after fix

3.4 Payout Fraud Hold Automation
Triggered by:

rapid earnings spikes

metadata inconsistencies

multi-account patterns

System:

freezes payout

alerts admin

places account under review

---------------------------------------------------------
4. RELIABILITY ENGINE AUTOMATIONS
Reliability updates in real time.

4.1 Reliability Update on Every Event
When any job milestone happens:

check-in

before photos

after photos

client review

dispute outcome

cancellation

→ reliability recalculated instantly.

4.2 Streak Bonus Automation
When cleaner hits streaks:

X on-time arrivals

X perfect jobs

X zero-dispute jobs

Automatically adds reliability bonus.

4.3 Penalty Automation
Automatically deducts points for:

late arrival

missing photos

low quality photos

cancellation

dispute loss

suspicious activity

4.4 Inactivity Decay Automation
If no jobs in:

21 days → reliability drop

45 days → deeper drop

60 days → forced downgrade

4.5 Tier Adjustment Automation
Every Sunday:

updates tier based on reliability

sends tier up/down notifications

---------------------------------------------------------
5. DISPUTE PROCESS AUTOMATIONS
Automating as much as possible reduces admin workload.

5.1 Evidence Auto-Collection
When dispute is opened:

System gathers:

all photos

metadata

GPS logs

job timestamps

instructions

Builds complete “Dispute Packet” instantly.

5.2 Auto-Decision Rules (Simple Cases)
If cleaner completely fails basic requirements:

missing photos → auto partial refund

fake check-in → auto refund

cleaner no-show → auto refund

System resolves automatically without admin.

5.3 Dispute Response Timer
Cleaner gets 12 hours to respond.

If no response:

dispute escalated

admin notified

reliability penalty applied

5.4 Auto-Fraud Detection in Disputes
Detects:

duplicate photos

mismatched metadata

staged before/after sets

suspicious file sizes

identical angles across multiple jobs

Flags case for manual review.

5.5 Dispute Outcome Automation
Once admin selects outcome:

update wallet

release credits

update reliability

notify client and cleaner

---------------------------------------------------------
6. NOTIFICATION AUTOMATIONS
6.1 Critical Event Notifications
Triggered for:

check-in overdue

missing photos

dispute opened

payout failure

GPS anomalies

6.2 Reminder Automation
For:

review needed

pending approval

verification steps incomplete

low wallet balance

6.3 Push-to-SMS Fallback Automation
If push not delivered within 90 seconds and event is critical → send SMS.

---------------------------------------------------------
7. FRAUD DETECTION AUTOMATIONS
The fraud engine has multiple automated triggers.

7.1 GPS Spoof Detection
If GPS data inconsistent:

freeze job

alert admin

reliability penalty

7.2 Duplicate Photo Detection
If photos match previous jobs:

flag cleaner

hold payout

escalate to fraud team

7.3 Unusual Earning Spike
If cleaner earns unusually high amount:

freeze payout

trigger review

7.4 Client Dispute Abuse Detection
If client files too many disputes:

raise client risk score

restrict dispute ability

notify admin

7.5 Multiple Account Linking
If multiple cleaners share:

same device

same bank

same address

→ flagged as high risk.

---------------------------------------------------------
8. ADMIN OPS AUTOMATIONS
8.1 Daily Ops Summary
Sent to admin:

disputes

payouts

fraud flags

jobs at risk

low reliability cleaners

8.2 High-Risk Alert Queue
System queues:

risky cleaners

risky clients

disputed jobs

flagged GPS activity

8.3 Account Suspension Automation
Triggered when reliability < threshold OR fraud signals hit.

8.4 Auto-Reassignment if Cleaner Cancels
If cleaner cancels job:

job goes back into job feed

top cleaners notified

client updated

---------------------------------------------------------
9. BACKUP, LOGS, & FAILSAFE AUTOMATIONS
9.1 Daily Backup
Backs up:

job data

user data

payout logs

credit ledger

evidence sets

9.2 Audit Logs
Every major action logged:

admin adjustments

payout overrides

dispute resolutions

system errors

9.3 Error Handling
If any automation fails:

retry sequence (1 min, 5 min, 15 min)

notification to admin

fallback workflow

---------------------------------------------------------
10. ANALYTICS & KPI AUTOMATIONS
10.1 Daily KPI Refresh
Generates metrics for:

bookings

cancellations

disputes

earnings

marketplace utilization

10.2 Cleaner Performance Alerts
System identifies cleaners with:

declining reliability

multiple disputes

cancellation streak

photo issues

Automatically sends coaching messages.

10.3 Client Churn Prediction
Predicts which clients may churn based on:

gap between bookings

Triggers retention campaigns.

audit logs & compliance data

system architecture best practices

3N — DATA MODELS, DATABASE ARCHITECTURE & ENTITY DEFINITIONS (ULTRA-EXPANDED CANON)
=========================================================
PureTask operates as a complex service marketplace.
Its database must be:

reliable

normalized where appropriate

indexed for speed

flexible for future features

secure

audit-proof

automation-ready

Stripe-compliant

marketplace-friendly

We define the complete schema set below.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. HIGH-LEVEL ENTITY MAP
Here is the conceptual map of entities and how they relate.

Core Entities
User (general)

Client Profile

Cleaner Profile

Job

Job Photos

Job Timeline Events

Wallet

Credit Transactions

Escrow Holds

Earnings Ledger

Payouts

Stripe Connect Accounts

Disputes

Reliability History

Tiers

Notifications

Support Tickets

System Logs

Fraud Flags

Top-Level Relationships
User → Client Profile (1:1 optional)

User → Cleaner Profile (1:1 optional)

Client Profile → Wallet (1:1)

Cleaner Profile → Earnings Ledger (1:1)

Job → Client Profile (many:1)

Job → Cleaner Profile (many:1)

Job → Job Photos (1:many)

Job → Timeline Events (1:many)

Credit Transactions → Wallet (many:1)

Escrow Holds → Job (many:1)

Disputes → Job (1:1)

Payouts → Cleaner Profile (many:1)

Reliability History → Cleaner Profile (many:1)

Fraud Flags → User (many:1)

---------------------------------------------------------
2. USER TABLE (MASTER ENTITY)
This table defines ALL users (both clients and cleaners).

users
Field	Type	Notes
id	UUID	PK
role	ENUM(client, cleaner, admin, support)	multi-role allowed
full_name	text	
email	text (unique)	
phone	text	
password_hash	text	
is_verified	boolean	email/phone verified
created_at	timestamp	
updated_at	timestamp	
last_login	timestamp	
device_fingerprint	text	used for fraud detection
Indexes:

email (unique)

phone

role

device_fingerprint

---------------------------------------------------------
3. CLIENT PROFILE TABLE
client_profiles
Field	Type
user_id	UUID (PK, FK → users.id)
default_address_id	UUID
credit_wallet_id	UUID
dispute_count	int
lifetime_jobs	int
preferred_cleaner_id	UUID (optional)
created_at	timestamp
---------------------------------------------------------
4. CLEANER PROFILE TABLE
cleaner_profiles
Field	Type	Notes
user_id	UUID (PK, FK)	
tier	ENUM(bronze, silver, gold, platinum)	
reliability_score	int	0–100
verification_status	ENUM(pending, verified, rejected)	
dispute_count	int	
cancellation_rate	float	
punctuality_rate	float	
photo_compliance_rate	float	
completed_jobs	int	
earnings_ledger_id	UUID	
stripe_connect_id	text	
instant_payout_eligible	boolean	
created_at	timestamp	
updated_at	timestamp	
Indexes:

tier

reliability_score

stripe_connect_id

---------------------------------------------------------
5. ADDRESSES TABLE
Used for clients and jobs.

addresses
Field	Type
id	UUID (PK)
user_id	UUID (FK optional)
street	text
unit	text
city	text
state	text
zipcode	text
geo_lat	float
geo_lng	float
created_at	timestamp
---------------------------------------------------------
6. JOB TABLE (CRITICAL TABLE)
jobs
Field	Type	Notes
id	UUID (PK)	
client_id	UUID (FK → users.id)	
cleaner_id	UUID (FK → users.id)	nullable until assigned
address_id	UUID	
status	ENUM(created, assigned, upcoming, in_progress, awaiting_photos, awaiting_review, correction_requested, disputed, approved, completed, canceled_client, canceled_cleaner, canceled_system)	
scheduled_start	timestamp	
check_in_at	timestamp	
check_out_at	timestamp	
estimated_hours	float	
actual_hours	float	
credit_cost	int	total credits
escrow_hold_id	UUID	
dispute_id	UUID	
instructions	text	
created_at	timestamp	
updated_at	timestamp	
Indexes:

client_id

cleaner_id

status

scheduled_start

---------------------------------------------------------
7. JOB PHOTOS TABLE
job_photos
Field	Type
id	UUID
job_id	UUID
type	ENUM(before, after)
room	text
url	text
metadata	jsonb
uploaded_at	timestamp
Indexes:

job_id

type

---------------------------------------------------------
8. JOB TIMELINE EVENTS TABLE
Tracks events for audit and reliability.

job_timeline_events
Field	Type
id	UUID
job_id	UUID
event_type	ENUM(check_in, photo_upload, cleaner_note, client_update, completion, dispute_opened, dispute_resolved)
payload	jsonb
created_at	timestamp
---------------------------------------------------------
9. WALLET TABLE
Each client has a single wallet.

wallets
Field	Type
id	UUID
user_id	UUID
available_balance	int
escrow_balance	int
promo_balance	int
updated_at	timestamp
---------------------------------------------------------
10. CREDIT TRANSACTIONS TABLE
Logs every modification to a wallet.

credit_transactions
Field	Type
id	UUID
wallet_id	UUID
type	ENUM(purchase, escrow_hold, escrow_release, refund, adjustment, expiration)
job_id	UUID
amount	int
balance_after	int
metadata	jsonb
created_at	timestamp
Indexes:

wallet_id

job_id

---------------------------------------------------------
11. ESCROW TABLE
Tracks credits locked for jobs.

escrow_holds
Field	Type
id	UUID
job_id	UUID
amount	int
status	ENUM(held, released, refunded, forfeited)
created_at	timestamp
updated_at	timestamp
---------------------------------------------------------
12. EARNINGS LEDGER TABLE
Tracks cleaner earnings before payout.

earnings_ledger
Field	Type
id	UUID
cleaner_id	UUID
total_earnings	int
pending_payout	int
lifetime_earnings	int
updated_at	timestamp
---------------------------------------------------------
13. EARNING TRANSACTIONS TABLE
Logs job earnings and payout deductions.

earning_transactions
Field	Type
id	UUID
ledger_id	UUID
job_id	UUID
amount	int
type	ENUM(job_earning, payout, adjustment, hold, release)
balance_after	int
metadata	jsonb
created_at	timestamp
---------------------------------------------------------
14. PAYOUT TABLE
Tracks outgoing payments via Stripe.

payouts
Field	Type
id	UUID
cleaner_id	UUID
stripe_payout_id	text
amount	int
fee	int
status	ENUM(pending, processing, paid, failed, on_hold)
failure_reason	text
created_at	timestamp
updated_at	timestamp
---------------------------------------------------------
15. DISPUTE TABLE
disputes
Field	Type
id	UUID
job_id	UUID
client_id	UUID
cleaner_id	UUID
status	ENUM(open, awaiting_cleaner, awaiting_admin, resolved, closed)
outcome	ENUM(full_refund, partial_refund, full_release, re_clean, fraud)
client_reason	text
client_evidence	jsonb
cleaner_response	text
admin_notes	text
resolution_amount	int
created_at	timestamp
updated_at	timestamp
---------------------------------------------------------
16. RELIABILITY HISTORY TABLE
Tracks adjustments over time.

reliability_history
Field	Type
id	UUID
cleaner_id	UUID
change	int
reason	text
triggered_by	ENUM(job_event, dispute, cancellation, admin)
job_id	UUID
created_at	timestamp
---------------------------------------------------------
17. TIER HISTORY TABLE
Tracks tier movement.

tier_history
Field	Type
id	UUID
cleaner_id	UUID
previous_tier	text
new_tier	text
change_reason	text
created_at	timestamp
---------------------------------------------------------
18. FRAUD FLAGS TABLE
fraud_flags
Field	Type
id	UUID
user_id	UUID
type	ENUM(gps_spoof, photo_fraud, dispute_abuse, payment_fraud, multi_account, suspicious_activity)
severity	int
notes	text
created_at	timestamp
---------------------------------------------------------
19. NOTIFICATION LOG TABLE
For email/SMS/push audit.

notifications
Field	Type
id	UUID
user_id	UUID
channel	ENUM(push, sms, email, in_app)
template	text
payload	jsonb
status	ENUM(sent, delivered, failed)
created_at	timestamp
---------------------------------------------------------
20. SYSTEM LOGS TABLE
For admin & automation activities.

system_logs
Field	Type
id	UUID
actor	ENUM(system, admin)
admin_id	UUID (nullable)
action	text
entity	text
entity_id	UUID
metadata	jsonb
created_at	timestamp
---------------------------------------------------------
21. INDEXING STRATEGY
To ensure fast performance:

High-Frequency Queries → Indexes Needed
job.status

jobs.cleaner_id

jobs.client_id

payout.status

wallet.user_id

credit_transactions.wallet_id

earning_transactions.ledger_id

reliability_history.cleaner_id

disputes.status

Composite Index Examples:
(cleaner_id, status, scheduled_start)

(job_id, type) for photo queries

(created_at DESC) for all time-based dashboards

---------------------------------------------------------
22. DATA LIFECYCLE & RETENTION
Permanent Data:
jobs

payouts

disputes

credit transactions

earning transactions

reliability changes

fraud flags

system logs

Soft-Delete Entities:
user accounts

addresses

notifications

Retention Rules:
evidence photos retained 2–5 years

logs retained ≥ 7 years for audit

---------------------------------------------------------
23. BACKUP & RECOVERY REQUIREMENTS
Backups:
daily full backup

hourly incremental

disaster recovery in separate region

Failover Rules:
read replica for heavy queries

background jobs run on separate node

all critical writes must succeed with 2-phase commit

=========================================================
4A — CLEANER ONBOARDING & VERIFICATION SYSTEM (ULTRA-EXPANDED CANON)
=========================================================
The Cleaner Onboarding System is how PureTask turns a random applicant into a:

verified

reliable

well-trained

properly equipped

policy-aware

photo-proof-competent

professional cleaner who can safely interact with clients and the credit/payout system.

This system must:

filter out bad fits early

set expectations clearly

train cleaners on how PureTask works

test their ability to follow instructions

verify identity & payout info

initialize their profile, tier, and reliability score

protect clients and the brand

Think of this as “PureTask Cleaner Academy + Verification Pipeline.”

1. ONBOARDING STAGES — HIGH-LEVEL PIPELINE
Every cleaner passes through 8 stages:

Application & Basic Screening

Identity & Eligibility Verification

PureTask Education (How the Platform Works)

Policy & Rules Agreement

Skills & Practice (Photos, GPS, Checklists)

Equipment & Readiness Verification

Stripe / Payout Setup

Final Review → Activation (Tier + Reliability Starting Point)

No cleaner can receive jobs until passing all 8.

2. STAGE 1 — APPLICATION & BASIC SCREENING
2.1 Application Form (Cleaner-Facing)
Cleaner submits:

full name

email

phone

city / service area

years of cleaning experience

primary transportation (car, transit, other)

days / times available

languages spoken

basic equipment they already own

whether they’ve done professional cleaning before

prior platform/agency experience (optional)

They must confirm:

they are 18+

they can legally work in the country

they agree to independent contractor status

2.2 Automatic Application Filters
Auto-reject if:

missing legal age

outside service zones

cannot legally work

cannot agree to independent contractor terms

Auto-flag for manual review if:

location near edge of coverage

inconsistent answers

odd experience claims (e.g., 0 years experience but wants premium rate immediately)

3. STAGE 2 — IDENTITY & ELIGIBILITY VERIFICATION
Goal: confirm the cleaner is a real person, unique, and eligible.

3.1 ID Verification
Cleaner must upload:

government-issued ID (front + back)

selfie for face match

System checks:

name consistency

date of birth

validity of ID

liveness / match between ID and selfie

If fails:

ask for new image or manual review

if still fails → reject onboarding

3.2 Background / Safety Checks (Configurable by Region)
Depending on local laws/policies:

background check via third-party

results attached to cleaner record

On failure:

application declined

polite but firm message sent

3.3 Device & Duplicate Account Check
System checks:

same phone number previously banned?

same device fingerprint used with another banned profile?

same bank account as another cleaner?

If flagged:

hold onboarding

manual review by risk team

4. STAGE 3 — PURETASK EDUCATION MODULES
This is where PureTask teaches the cleaner how the platform works.

Modules (in-app, with short screens + quizzes):

4.1 Module 1 — “How Jobs Work”
Explains:

clients buy credits

credits → escrow

job booked

cleaner assigned

check-in with GPS

photos before & after

client approves → earnings available

payouts weekly / instant

Quiz question examples:

“Do clients pay you directly?” (Correct: No, all via PureTask)

“When do you get paid for a job?” (Correct: after client approves or auto-approval)

4.2 Module 2 — “Reliability & Tiers”
Explains:

reliability score (0–100)

starting reliability baseline

how it goes up (on-time, photos, job quality)

how it goes down (late, missing photos, disputes)

tier ranges: Bronze / Silver / Gold / Platinum

benefits of higher tiers (earnings, more jobs, instant payout)

Quiz examples:

“What happens if you miss before/after photos?” → reliability down + risk of dispute

“Can you reach higher pay by improving reliability?” → Yes

4.3 Module 3 — “Photo Proof Training”
Shows:

example before/after shots

acceptable vs bad photos (dark, blurry, wrong angle)

requirement: at least 2 angles per room

show how photos protect them in disputes

Quiz:

“Is one single photo for the whole house enough?” (Correct: No)

“Why are photos important?” (Correct: to prove your work and protect your earnings)

4.4 Module 4 — “GPS Check-In & Time”
Explains:

must check in when at client’s home

no early check-in from far away

no GPS spoofing

check-in time impacts reliability and payouts

Quiz:

“Can you check in from home then drive to client?” → No

4.5 Module 5 — “Conduct & Professionalism”
Explains key rules:

no harassment

no rude language

respect client’s home and privacy

no stealing

no bringing guests

no smoking inside

follow instructions

5. STAGE 4 — POLICY & RULES AGREEMENT
After education, cleaner must explicitly agree to platform rules:

5.1 Required Agreements
Cleaner Code of Conduct

Reliability Rules

Photo Requirements

GPS / Check-in Rules

Cancellation Rules

Dispute & Evidence Rules

Independent Contractor Terms

Payment & Payout Policies

No Off-Platform Transactions

Each must be:

shown clearly

accepted with a checkbox

timestamped & stored in DB

Feature: “View full policy again” available anytime in their profile.

6. STAGE 5 — SKILLS & PRACTICAL TESTS
This is where PureTask confirms cleaners can actually follow instructions inside the app.

6.1 Photo Practice Test
Cleaner must complete a mock job flow:

app generates a sample “practice home”

cleaner is asked to upload placeholder photos (could even be stock sample allowed here)

app evaluates:

are there enough photos?

are they properly oriented?

are they non-blurry?

If photo test fails:

show feedback

require retake

After X failed attempts:

flag for support or rejection

6.2 Checklist & Instruction Test
Cleaner is shown a mock job with:

instructions (e.g., “Focus on kitchen counters and bathroom sinks”)

checklist items

Mini-quiz:

“Which rooms are highest priority in this job?”

“What should you do if client’s instructions conflict with PureTask rules?”

6.3 GPS Simulation / Check-in Demo
Cleaner must:

simulate a check-in flow (without actual GPS lock)

understand that IRL they must be at client’s location

This ensures they know WHERE the button lives and HOW to use it.

7. STAGE 6 — EQUIPMENT & READINESS VERIFICATION
PureTask must ensure cleaners are properly equipped.

7.1 Equipment Checklist
Cleaner selects which they have:

vacuum

mop & bucket

microfiber cloths

non-abrasive cleaners

glass cleaner

bathroom cleaner

gloves

etc.

Certain jobs (e.g., standard vs deep clean) may require minimum equipment.

If cleaner lacks key tools:

show them what they need before they can accept certain job types

restrict job types until equipment confirmed

7.2 Equipment Policy Education
Clarify:

in most cases, cleaners are expected to bring supplies

in some markets, clients may provide supplies

must never use unsafe chemicals

must follow instructions when client specifies products (e.g., “only use this wood cleaner”)

8. STAGE 7 — STRIPE / PAYOUT SETUP
Cleaners must complete payout setup before activation.

8.1 Stripe Connect Account Creation
From within app:

cleaner enters legal name (must match ID)

confirms date of birth

adds bank account details

passes any required KYC questions

Status:

pending

verified

failed

If failed:

onboarding paused

cleaner notified to fix issues

8.2 Payout Education
Explains:

how weekly payouts work

how instant payout works

fees involved

required minimum balances

refunds never come from cleaner after payout (handled via system)

9. STAGE 8 — FINAL REVIEW & ACTIVATION
Before a cleaner is activated:

System checks:

application completeness

ID verification success

Stripe account status

education modules passed

practice tests passed

equipment minimum met

no fraud flags

9.1 Starting Reliability Score & Tier
Defaults (recommended):

Reliability: 70 (Silver baseline)

Tier: Bronze or Silver depending on screening & experience

Example setup:

If no prior experience: Bronze

If >1 year pro experience + great onboarding performance: Silver

No one starts at Gold or Platinum.

9.2 Activation State
When ready:

cleaner_status = “active”

jobs become visible in job feed

they can start receiving bookings

Notifications:

“You’re approved to start receiving jobs!”

“Your starting tier is: [Tier]. Here’s how to grow.”

10. AUTO-REJECTION & DISQUALIFICATION RULES
Auto-reject during onboarding if:

ID verification fails multiple times

Stripe identity checks fail and cannot be resolved

background check returns disqualifying result

duplicate device/fingerprint from banned account

repeated failure of training quizzes (e.g., 5 attempts)

aggressive or abusive in messages during onboarding

System sets:

cleaner_status = “rejected”

notes in admin dashboard

They may or may not be allowed to reapply in X months depending on reason.

11. ONBOARDING METRICS & KPIs
Track:

application → approval rate

time to complete onboarding

drop-off points (where do they quit?)

quiz pass rates

practice photo pass rates

percentage who activate and accept first job

performance of cleaners by onboarding cohort (long-term)

This allows PureTask to:

improve onboarding flows

tighten or loosen standards

optimize training content

12. OPERATIONS SOP FOR ONBOARDING SUPPORT
When cleaners get stuck:

Support can:
resend onboarding emails

manually review ID docs

provide guidance on Stripe/KYC

reset training modules

escalate risk flags to a specialist

Support must NOT:
bypass verification

push through suspicious accounts

manually force payouts outside system rules

✅ 4A COMPLETE — CLEANER ONBOARDING & VERIFICATION SYSTEM
Next in Section 4 is:

4B — Client Onboarding & Education System
That will cover:

how new clients are introduced to PureTask

how they learn credits, escrow, approval, disputes

how we set expectations about cleaners, photo proof, GPS, etc.

how we prevent misunderstandings that cause disputes later

retention-focused onboarding (turn first bookings into repeat behavior)

Perfect — continuing now with SECTION 4B, which defines the entire Client Onboarding & Education System.

This is one of the MOST important operational areas because client misunderstandings create disputes, cancellations, mistrust, low retention, and unnecessary support tickets.

A great client onboarding solves 80% of future problems.

Let’s build the full canon.

=========================================================
⭐ 4B — CLIENT ONBOARDING & EDUCATION SYSTEM (ULTRA-EXPANDED CANON)
=========================================================
Client onboarding has 3 core goals:

Teach clients how PureTask works (credits, escrow, approval).

Set expectations (photos, timing, cleaner responsibilities).

Guide them toward repeat bookings and loyalty.

Poor onboarding = high disputes + low retention.
Great onboarding = smooth operations + long-term revenue.

PureTask aims to create a zero-confusion onboarding, fully automated.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. CLIENT ONBOARDING FUNNEL — HIGH LEVEL
Client onboarding happens across 6 touchpoints:

App Install / Email Capture

Account Creation

Home Profile Setup

Education Screens (How PureTask Works)

First Booking Guidance

Post-First-Cleaning Education (Retention Booster)

Each part is designed to:

simplify

educate

reduce friction

prevent disputes

pre-frame proper expectations

---------------------------------------------------------
2. ACCOUNT CREATION (CLIENT)
Client provides:

name

email

phone

password

ZIP code (to check coverage area)

System checks:

location inside a service area

duplicate accounts

device fingerprint

If outside service area:

show “Join Waitlist” screen

store email for expansion campaigns

---------------------------------------------------------
3. HOME PROFILE SETUP
This is CRITICAL.
Most disputes happen because PureTask doesn’t know the correct home details.

Client must provide:

bedrooms

bathrooms

home type

square footage (optional but ideal)

cleaning frequency (optional)

Additional Home Info:
pets

flooring types

parking instructions

door/gate codes

special requests (optional)

supplies provided by client (if any)

Important UI Note:
Home profile persists → future bookings are one-click.

---------------------------------------------------------
4. PURETASK EDUCATION MODULES (Client Side)
Clients must understand:

what credits are

what escrow is

how approval works

why photos matter

what cleaners are responsible for

what clients are responsible for

how disputes work

how refund logic works

PureTask delivers this through simple onboarding cards.

4.1 Module 1 — “How PureTask Works”
Explains:

“You buy credits”

“Credits go into escrow during cleaning”

“Cleaner completes job with photos”

“You approve the cleaning”

“Credits release → cleaner gets paid”

This ensures clients don’t think:

they pay per hour

they pay directly to cleaner

they can skip approval

cleaners get paid regardless of quality

4.2 Module 2 — “What to Expect During a Cleaning”
Shows:

cleaner will check in with GPS

cleaner will upload before & after photos

cleaner will follow your instructions

cleaner must bring equipment (unless specified)

Shows examples of:

✔ acceptable before/after format
✔ correct angles
✔ lighting

4.3 Module 3 — “Your Responsibilities”
Clients MUST know they must:

give accurate home profile

provide safe access

provide clear instructions

approve or dispute within the window

upload any evidence for disputes

ensure pets are safe

If they are not home:

instruct how cleaner can enter

must leave access details

4.4 Module 4 — “Approval & Dispute Flow”
This is crucial to avoid misunderstandings.

Explains:

Approval:
review photos

approve

credits released

Dispute:
must provide evidence

must choose reason

must be within dispute window

cleaner can respond

admin reviews

Very clear:
Disputes cannot be opened after approval.

4.5 Module 5 — “Cleaner Tiers & Reliability”
Explains:

Bronze / Silver / Gold / Platinum

higher tier = higher quality + more experience

clients may choose or auto-assign

4.6 Module 6 — “Safety & Trust”
Shows trust-building elements:

verified identity

GPS check-in

before/after photo proof

reliability tracking

background checks (if region supports)

---------------------------------------------------------
5. FIRST BOOKING GUIDED EXPERIENCE
For NEW clients, the booking flow becomes guided:

Step 1 — Home Profile Confirmation
Shows the client their home details and asks to confirm.

Step 2 — Cleaner Selection Education
“All cleaners are verified and trained on PureTask’s standards.”

Step 3 — Pricing Explained
“We use a credit system (similar to tokens).
Credits are purchased once, used for any cleaning, and refundable according to policy.”

Step 4 — Booking Confirmation
Shows:

what will happen next

how the cleaner arrives

how you’ll receive photos

how you approve

---------------------------------------------------------
6. APPROVAL EDUCATION (BEFORE THEIR FIRST CLEANING)

Push Notification + In-App Banner:

“After your cleaning, you will receive before & after photos.
Please review and approve to complete the job.”

This ensures they are mentally ready for the approval step.

---------------------------------------------------------

“Your cleaner has checked in using GPS.”

“We will notify you when photos are ready.”

This reinforces trust again.

A. “How to Get Even Better Results” Tips
set recurring schedule

favorite your preferred cleaner

give clear instructions

update your home profile

B. Retention Nudges
“Would you like to rebook this cleaner?”

“Schedule your next cleaning now?”

C. Credit Reminder
“Keep credits in your wallet to book instantly anytime.”

Custom tooltip-driven flow for new users.

Automation 2 — Pre-Cleaning Reminder
“Cleaner will upload before & after photos for your approval.”

Automation 3 — Approval Reminder
If photos submitted:

reminder after 1 hour

final reminder before auto-approval

If client opens dispute but does not complete evidence upload:

gentle reminder

If client does not book again within 30 days:

send education tips

offer rebooking suggestions

10. CLIENT EXPECTATION MANAGEMENT (DISPUTE REDUCTION)
PureTask’s onboarding prevents 70% of disputes by setting correct expectations.

Clients learn:

Cleaning Time Expectations:
Cleaners are not handymen

Cleaners are not maids or housekeepers

They will clean surfaces, not deep repair

They follow a standard checklist

If client needs more time, they must book more credits

Photo Expectations:
Clients understand:

photos are the only evidence

if they want something cleaned, it must be visible

instructions must be clear

Access Expectations:
If cleaner cannot enter → client is charged no-show fee.

Dispute Expectations:
must be timely

must include evidence

cannot be used for buyer’s remorse

11. CLIENT SUPPORT ONBOARDING (INTEGRATED HELP SYSTEM)

Help Articles:
“How credits work”

“How disputes work”

Live Help:
in-app message

email

emergency cases

The help system is proactive.

When a client performs a risky action (e.g., unclear instructions), the app surfaces:

“Tip: Clear instructions help ensure the best cleaning results.”

false dispute claims can result in account review

no off-platform payments allowed

Everything is positioned positively:

“We take fairness seriously for both clients and cleaners.”

Goal:

Higher education = fewer disputes + higher retention.

Perfect — continuing now with SECTION 4C, which is one of the most operationally important sections of the entire PureTask system.

This is the Job Operations Playbook — the complete SOP for how every job in PureTask runs from start to finish, including every rule, condition, exception, and emergency protocol.

=========================================================
⭐ 4C — JOB OPERATIONS SOPs (ULTRA-EXPANDED CANON)
=========================================================
This section defines EVERY operational rule from booking → assignment → arrival → cleaning → approval → payout → resolution.

This operational canon ensures:

cleaners know exactly what to do

clients know what to expect

disputes are minimized

fraud is detected early

timing is predictable

photos are consistent

approvals are clean

credits flow correctly

reliability scoring remains fair

PureTask manages jobs differently than a normal cleaning company because it is a marketplace, so operations must be enforced at scale.

---------------------------------------------------------
0. JOB OPERATIONAL PHASES (HIGH-LEVEL)
Every job in PureTask passes through 12 system phases:

Booking Created

Cleaner Assigned

Pre-Job Preparation

Travel-to-Job Window

Arrival & GPS Check-In

Before Photos Taken

Cleaning In Progress

After Photos Taken

Job Completed by Cleaner

Client Review & Approval

Auto-Approval (if needed)

Escrow Release & Payout

Dispute (if raised)

Each phase has rules, timers, and automations.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. JOB ASSIGNMENT SOP
The moment a client books, the system must:

Step 1: Create Job in “Created” State
State = created
Escrow = credits held
Cleaner = null

Step 2: Assignment Logic Executes
Rules:

if client chose “recommended cleaner” → auto-assign best match

if client selected a specific cleaner → assign that cleaner

if no cleaner selected → push job to eligible cleaners

Step 3: Cleaner Receives Job Notification
Cleaner sees:

job type

estimated time

credits payout

distance

Cleaner must accept within X minutes or job goes back into pool.

Step 4: Cleaner Accepts Job → Job Becomes “Assigned”
Client notified:

“Your cleaner is confirmed for tomorrow at 10:00 AM.”

If No Cleaner Accepts:
System attempts:

round 2 assignment

notify client

option to reschedule or expand cleaner radius

If STILL no cleaner accepts:

job auto-cancels

credits refunded

client receives apology + retention offer

---------------------------------------------------------
2. PRE-JOB PREPARATION SOP
Once job is upcoming:

Cleaner Must:
review job details

review instructions

check equipment

clarify access instructions

confirm availability

Client Must:
update instructions if needed

ensure access is possible

secure pets

prepare home safely

System Sends:
24-hour reminder to both

1-hour reminder before job

Client Cancellation Rules Activate:
free cancellation until 24 hours out

late cancellation → partial credit forfeiture

---------------------------------------------------------
3. TRAVEL-TO-JOB SOP
Cleaner Should Leave in Time to Arrive:
at or before start time

no early check-in allowed unless within GPS radius

If cleaner appears too far away shortly before job:

system displays soft warning

reliability risk increases

Clients may see “Cleaner is on the way” if enabled.

---------------------------------------------------------
4. ARRIVAL & GPS CHECK-IN SOP (CRITICAL)
This is one of the HEARTBEATS of the PureTask platform.

Cleaner Check-In Rules:
Cleaner must be physically at the job location.

GPS coordinates must match the client address.

Cleaner taps “Check In.”

System logs:

latitude/longitude

timestamp

device ID

network info

If GPS Fails:
Cleaner receives troubleshooting steps.

Cleaner MUST NOT:

check in from the street far away

check in early while at home

spoof GPS

If GPS consistently fails:
cleaner flagged for “GPS Reliability Issue”

admin may require manual verification

Late Check-In SOP:
0–10 minutes late → soft penalty

10–20 minutes late → moderate reliability deduction

20+ minutes → severe penalty and client notified

If cleaner will be late:
Cleaner SHOULD message client via app.

---------------------------------------------------------
5. BEFORE PHOTOS SOP
Cleaner must upload before photos BEFORE any cleaning begins.

Requirements:
minimum 2 photos per room

show all surfaces

show clutter level

must be well-lit

must match angles of after photos

System Enforcement:
cannot proceed to “Start Cleaning” until before photos done

missing rooms → warning

blurry photos → retake prompt

Why this matters:
protects cleaners

protects clients

reduces disputes drastically

If cleaner skips before photos:
job cannot be approved automatically

heavy reliability penalty

admin review required

payout may be at risk

---------------------------------------------------------
6. CLEANING IN PROGRESS SOP
Cleaner Must:
perform tasks based on standard checklist

follow client instructions

update notes if needed

report problems (broken items, no supplies, unsafe conditions)

System Monitors:
timer

app activity

suspicious inactivity patterns

location drift

Common Issues Mid-Job:
Issue: Unsafe Environment
Cleaner reports and may leave → client charged cancellation fee.

Issue: Access Lost (door locked, client left)
Cleaner marks “lost access” → partial compensation given.

Issue: Client modifies instructions mid-job
Cleaner must follow app instructions, not verbal after start.
New instructions invalid unless updated in-app BEFORE job start.

---------------------------------------------------------
7. AFTER PHOTOS SOP
After cleaning is complete:

Cleaner must take after photos.

Requirements:
same room

same angle

same lighting if possible

minimum 2 per room

no filters

must clearly show cleaning quality

System checks:

are these different from before?

do angles match?

is lighting adequate?

are surfaces cleaner?

If mismatch:

system requests retake

flag for admin attention

Cleaner then taps:
“Submit Job for Review.”

State changes to: awaiting_review

---------------------------------------------------------
8. JOB COMPLETION (CLEANER SUBMISSION) SOP
When cleaner submits job:

System logs:

photo evidence

timestamps

cleaning duration

location verification

reliability score adjustments

potential fraud indicators

Client receives:

“Your cleaning photos are ready for review.”

Cleaner sees:

“Awaiting client approval.”

No earnings released yet.

---------------------------------------------------------
9. CLIENT REVIEW & APPROVAL SOP
This is a critical phase affecting payouts, disputes, and client trust.

Client sees:
before/after comparison

cleaner notes

duration

instructions vs results

Client must choose:
Approve

Request Fix (if enabled)

Open Dispute

If approve:

credits release

cleaner gets earnings

client prompted to rate cleaner

---------------------------------------------------------
10. AUTO-APPROVAL SOP
If client does nothing:

reminder sent at X hours

final reminder before deadline

auto-approval at 24 hours

Why we do this:

protects cleaner earnings

prevents stalled jobs

Cleaner receives:
“Job auto-approved. Earnings added.”

---------------------------------------------------------
11. DISPUTE INITIATION SOP
If client selects dispute:

job state → disputed

escrow locked

cleaner notified

cleaner must respond within 12 hours

admin notified

All dispute logic defined in Section 3H & 4F.

---------------------------------------------------------
12. CLEANER NO-SHOW SOP
Cleaner "no-show" = did not check in within grace period AND did not communicate.

Steps:

System flags job after X minutes.

Client notified “Cleaner is delayed; we are reviewing.”

After extended window → auto-cancel.

Client refunded fully.

Cleaner receives severe reliability penalty (-30 to -50).

If repeated → suspension.

---------------------------------------------------------
13. CLIENT NO-SHOW / ACCESS FAILURE SOP
If cleaner cannot enter home:

Cleaner taps:
“Client Not Home / Cannot Access.”

System requires:

photo of locked door OR

note explaining access issue

Then:

If client failed to provide access:
client charged no-show fee

cleaner receives partial payout (20–40% depending on market)

job ends

If cleaner made error:
no penalty to client

cleaner may face reliability deduction

---------------------------------------------------------
14. CLEANER CANCELLATION SOP
Cleaner cancels before job:

must cancel >24 hours notice → small penalty

<24 hours → moderate penalty

<2 hours → severe penalty + tier impact

frequent cancellations → suspension review

Client notified and offered:

reassignment

reschedule

cancel & refund

---------------------------------------------------------
15. CLIENT CANCELLATION SOP
Client cancels:

>24 hours:
full refund

<24 hours:
partial refund to client

partial payout to cleaner

After cleaner arrives / checks in:
full payment to cleaner

no refund

---------------------------------------------------------
16. JOB REASSIGNMENT SOP
Job requires new cleaner due to:

cancellation

no-show

late arrival

client request

system issue

System attempts:

Find new cleaner

Notify client

Adjust expected arrival time

If no cleaner accepts → refund

---------------------------------------------------------
17. SAFETY & EMERGENCY SOP
If cleaner encounters:

threatening behavior

aggressive pets

unsafe environment

illegal activity

Cleaner must:

leave immediately

mark job as unsafe

submit notes / photo if safe

admin notified instantly

System outcomes:

full or partial compensation to cleaner

client review / suspension

---------------------------------------------------------
18. QUALITY CONTROL SOP
Quality enforced through:

photo analysis

client ratings

random admin audits

AI cleanliness detection (future)

Cleaners failing QC:

receive coaching notifications

temporary tier freeze

reduced job visibility

required re-training

eventual suspension

=========================================================

4D — Cancellation & Reschedule Policies (Ultra-Expanded)

Perfect — continuing with SECTION 4D, the complete Cancellation & Reschedule Policies (Ultra-Expanded Canon).

This section defines every rule for:

client cancellations

cleaner cancellations

system cancellations

late changes

fees

credit refunds

penalties

exceptions

These rules are crucial because cancellations heavily affect:

marketplace stability

client satisfaction

cleaner trust

earnings predictability

scheduling efficiency

operational fairness

Let’s build the full canon.

=========================================================
⭐ 4D — CANCELLATION & RESCHEDULE POLICIES (ULTRA-EXPANDED CANON)
=========================================================
PureTask’s cancellation system is built on 3 principles:

Fairness: Both clients and cleaners are independent actors whose time matters.

Predictability: Clearly defined rules prevent confusion or “surprises.”

Trust: Canceling should never be weaponized or used to exploit the platform.

The cancellation system includes:

timing thresholds

credit refund logic

cleaner compensation

reliability scoring impacts

reassignments

exceptions for emergencies

automatic system rules

anti-abuse protections

---------------------------------------------------------
0. DEFINITIONS
Before we dive in:

Start Time
The scheduled start time of the job.

Late Cancellation
A cancellation that occurs within a penalty window.

No-Show
Failure to check in or failure to allow access.

Escrow Credits
Credits held during a job, not yet paid to cleaner.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. CLIENT CANCELLATION POLICIES
This governs when a client cancels a job.

Client cancellations have time-based tiers:

⭐ 1.1 Cancellation > 24 Hours Before Start
Client Refund:
✔ 100% of credits returned to wallet.

Cleaner Compensation:
✘ No payout (cleaner had enough notice).

Reliability Impact:
None.

Notes:
Clients can cancel freely ahead of time.

⭐ 1.2 Cancellation < 24 Hours Before Start (Late)
Late cancellation window: 24 hours → job start time.

Client Refund:
✔ Refund partial (example: 70–80%)
❗ Portion withheld is used to compensate cleaner.

Cleaner Compensation:
✔ Cleaner receives 20–30% of estimated payout.

Reliability Impact:
None (cleaner is not at fault).

Notes:
This discourages last-minute cancellations.

⭐ 1.3 Cancellation After Cleaner Has Begun Traveling
If cleaner has accepted job and begun approaching (system detects via time + radius):

Client Refund:
Partial refund (50–60%)

Cleaner Compensation:
Higher partial payout (30–50%)

Reason:
Cleaner already invested time.

⭐ 1.4 Cancellation After Cleaner Arrives (Before Check-In)
Cleaner arrives but cannot begin due to client cancellation or change of mind.

Client Refund:
Very low refund (0–30%)

Cleaner Compensation:
Cleaner receives 70–100% of payout.

Reliability Impact:
None.

⭐ 1.5 Cancellation After Check-In
Once cleaner checks in:

Client Refund:
0% refund.
Job treated as completed.

Cleaner Compensation:
Full payout releases.

Reason:
Cleaner is already working.

---------------------------------------------------------
2. CLIENT NO-SHOW / ACCESS FAILURE POLICIES
A client no-show occurs when cleaner cannot enter or client is unavailable.

⭐ 2.1 Client Not Home / Cannot Access
Cleaner must take photo proof (door, gate, etc.)

Client Refund:
0%

Cleaner Compensation:
60–100% payout (region dependent)

Reliability Impact:
Cleaner: None
Client: Access failure count increases

⭐ 2.2 Wrong Address / Incorrect Access Instructions
If client error prevents job success:

Client Refund:
0%

Cleaner Compensation:
Full payout

Notes:
This discourages incorrect home info.

---------------------------------------------------------
3. CLEANER CANCELLATION POLICIES
Cleaner cancellations harm marketplace trust more than client cancellations, so penalties are stricter.

Cleaner cancellation windows:

⭐ 3.1 Cleaner Cancellation > 24 Hours Before Start
Penalty:

small reliability deduction (-5)

client notified

system attempts reassignment

Notes:
Acceptable if rare.

⭐ 3.2 Cleaner Cancellation < 24 Hours Before Start
This is harmful to client trust.

Penalty:

moderate reliability deduction (-10 to -20)

tier freeze window (optional feature)

account review if repeated

Client Outcome:

reassignment attempt

small credit bonus (optional)

⭐ 3.3 Cleaner Cancellation < 2 Hours Before Start
Serious violation.

Penalty:

severe reliability deduction (-20 to -40)

potential tier drop

potential temporary suspension

placed in “low-trust cleaner pool”

Client Outcome:

emergency reassignment attempts

client gets credit bonus

PureTask may apply retention compensation

⭐ 3.4 Cleaner No-Show (Never Arrived / Never Checked In)
This is the most severe offense.

Penalty:

reliability: -30 to -50

immediate suspension until admin review

multiple offenses = permanent removal

Client Outcome:

full refund

reassigned cleaner if possible

credit bonus

---------------------------------------------------------
4. SYSTEM CANCELLATIONS
These occur when PureTask cancels a job automatically.

⭐ 4.1 No Cleaner Found
If no cleaner accepts the job in time:

Client Refund: 100%
Notes: No penalties for anyone.

⭐ 4.2 Fraud Detection Triggered
Example:

GPS spoofing

duplicate photos

account flagged

System cancels job:

Client Refund: 100%
Cleaner Compensation: None
Cleaner Impact: severe reliability drop

⭐ 4.3 Scheduling Conflicts / Platform Error
If PureTask causes the cancellation:

Client Refund: 100%
Cleaner Compensation: None
Extra: small bonus credits to client

---------------------------------------------------------
5. RESCHEDULING POLICIES
Rescheduling is treated differently than cancellation.

⭐ 5.1 Client Reschedule > 24 Hours Prior
Free reschedule.

⭐ 5.2 Client Reschedule < 24 Hours Prior
Handled like late cancellation:

cleaner receives partial payout

client is refunded partially

rescheduled job counts as new booking

⭐ 5.3 Cleaner Requests Reschedule
Cleaner cannot force reschedules.

If cleaner “asks client” inside app:

Client may choose:

accept

decline (forcing cancellation penalties)

Cleaner receives penalty if:

too close to job time

pattern of repeated attempts

---------------------------------------------------------
6. CANCELLATION PAYMENT LOGIC (CREDITS & PAYOUTS)
When client cancels:
Credits → returned to wallet (full or partial depending on timing).

Cleaner → receives compensation depending on rules.

When cleaner cancels:
Client → refunded 100%
Cleaner → receives no payout
Cleaner → reliability deduction

When system cancels:
Usually:

client refunded

cleaner not compensated (unless client at fault)

---------------------------------------------------------
7. RELIABILITY SCORE IMPACTS FOR CANCELLATIONS
Cleaner Reliability Penalties:
Scenario	Impact
Cancel >24h	-5
Cancel <24h	-10 to -20
Cancel <2h	-20 to -40
No-Show	-30 to -50
Abuse patterns	Suspension
Client Reliability / Risk Flags:
repeated late cancellations

repeated access failures

abusive refund claims

dispute abuse

Clients may be flagged “high-risk” internally.

---------------------------------------------------------
8. ABUSE DETECTION RULES
System automatically detects cancellation abuse.

Client Abuse Indicators:
repeatedly booking and canceling

last-minute cancellations >3 times/month

“no access” caused by client multiple times

repeated disputes after cancelling late

Cleaner Abuse Indicators:
cancellations clustered on weekend jobs

pattern of declining lower-value jobs

cancels after seeing home size

missing check-ins repeatedly

System responses:

flag the account

limit functionality

require manual approval

initiate review

---------------------------------------------------------
9. EXCEPTIONS & EMERGENCY POLICIES
Emergency Cases (Client or Cleaner)
Counted as excused if verified by support:

medical emergency

severe weather

car accident

sudden family emergency

Reliability / credits adjusted by admin discretion.

Weather Exceptions
If unsafe conditions:

system suspends cancellation penalties

jobs automatically rescheduled

Safety Threat
If cleaner feels unsafe:

job auto-cancels

client does NOT get refund (unless evidence contradicts)

cleaner compensated fully

---------------------------------------------------------
10. COMMUNICATION RULES FOR CANCELLATIONS
Client Receives Messages:
“Your job was canceled. Here’s what happened.”

“Your refund is processed.”

“Would you like to reschedule?”

Cleaner Receives Messages:
“You canceled a job. Reliability decreased.”

“Future cancellations may affect your tier.”

Admin Tools:
override refunds

override penalties

annotate account records

issue credits manually

=========================================================
⭐ 4D COMPLETE — CANCELLATION & RESCHEDULE POLICIES
=========================================================

support tone

SLAs

message templates

escalation rules

sensitive case handling

admin communication standards

This is one of the densest and most important sections for operations.

continue

Perfect — continuing now with SECTION 4E, one of the most essential and sensitive operational systems in PureTask:

=========================================================
⭐ 4E — CUSTOMER SUPPORT SOPs (ULTRA-EXPANDED CANON)
=========================================================
Customer Support is the communication backbone of PureTask.
It touches:

clients

cleaners

admins

disputes

cancellations

fraud reviews

escalations

payouts

emergencies

Support SOPs ensure:

consistent tone

fair decisions

fast responses

safety

trust

reduced churn

minimized legal exposure

Let's build the complete canon.

---------------------------------------------------------
0. CORE PRINCIPLES OF PURETASK SUPPORT
Support operates under 6 fundamental principles:

1. Neutrality
Support must remain unbiased between cleaner and client.
We operate as a third-party marketplace, not someone’s advocate.

2. Clarity
Always provide clear, simple explanations.
No jargon, no vague statements.

3. Empathy
Clients and cleaners must feel heard, even when enforcement is strict.

4. Evidence-Based Decisions
No decision is based on emotion.
Only based on:

photos

GPS logs

timestamps

dispute notes

system rules

5. Fairness & Consistency
Same problem → same outcome.
Zero arbitrary rulings.

6. Fast Response
Speed matters. The longer an issue is open, the higher the churn risk.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. SUPPORT CHANNELS & ACCESS
Clients access support via:
in-app messaging (primary)

email

emergency SMS (for safety issues only)

Cleaners access support via:
in-app

email

Admin dashboard shows:
queue status

priority tickets

dispute queue

fraud alerts

---------------------------------------------------------
2. SUPPORT PRIORITY LEVELS (SLA FRAMEWORK)
Every issue is classified into 5 priority levels, each with a required response time.

P1 — Emergencies (Respond ≤ 5 minutes)
Examples:

safety threats

cleaner locked inside home

aggressive pets

harassment

medical issues during jobs

P2 — Active Job Issues (Respond ≤ 10–15 min)
Examples:

cleaner cannot access home

cleaner is late

client claiming cleaner didn’t show

GPS check-in problems

P3 — Money Issues (Respond ≤ 1–2 hours)
Examples:

payout problems

credit refund questions

Stripe errors

P4 — Disputes (Respond ≤ 24 hours)
These take investigation and must be handled carefully.

P5 — General Questions (Respond ≤ 24–48 hours)
Examples:

“How do I change my address?”

“How do credits work?”

---------------------------------------------------------
3. SUPPORT TONE & LANGUAGE GUIDELINES
Support must sound:

calm

professional

knowledgeable

confident

friendly

never emotional

Forbidden Tone Examples:
❌ Passive-aggressive
❌ Sarcastic
❌ Defensive
❌ Blaming
❌ Taking sides prematurely

Required Tone Examples:
✔ “I understand why that was frustrating. Here’s what we can do.”
✔ “Let me walk you through how this works.”
✔ “Based on our policy, here’s the next step.”

Key Phrases to Use:
“Thanks for your patience.”

“I can help with that.”

“Here’s what I see in the system…”

“Let’s resolve this together.”

“We want to be fair to both you and your cleaner/client.”

---------------------------------------------------------
4. SUPPORT SCRIPTS (CORE TEMPLATES)
4.1 Client Asking: “Why do I need to approve the job?”
“PureTask uses a photo-based verification system.
Your approval confirms that the cleaner completed the work as shown in the photos.
Once you approve, credits release from escrow and the cleaner gets paid.”

4.2 Cleaner Asking: “Why didn’t I get full payout?”
“Your payout depends on client approval and PureTask’s policy. In this case, the job outcome involved [reason].
Here’s the exact breakdown of your earnings.”

4.3 Client Requesting Refund Past Approval
“Once a job is approved, credits release to the cleaner and the job is closed.
We can only open a dispute if the approval was made in error and with supporting evidence.”

4.4 Cleaner Complaining About Client Instructions
"Please follow the instructions shown inside the app.
If the instructions were unclear, let the client know through the chat feature, but continue using the app version as the official record.”

4.5 Client No-Show Fee Explanation
“Our system detected that the cleaner could not access the home.
Because access is the client’s responsibility, a no-show fee applies to compensate the cleaner’s time.”

4.6 Cleaner No-Show Message
“We did not receive your check-in within the required window.
This counts as a no-show and impacts reliability. If this was a mistake, please provide details so we can review.”

4.7 Dispute Intake Script
“I understand you're not satisfied with the results.
To help resolve this fairly, please upload photos showing the areas of concern.
Our team will review both sets of photos and make a decision based on policy.”

---------------------------------------------------------
5. SUPPORT PROCESS FLOWS (STEP-BY-STEP SOPs)
5.1 ACTIVE JOB SUPPORT SOP
When an active job has a problem:

Step 1 — Verify Status
Check:

check-in history

GPS data

photo uploads

timeline logs

Step 2 — Contact Cleaner
If needed, ask cleaner:

“Are you still on your way?”

“Can you share a photo of the door/access issue?”

Step 3 — Contact Client
If client is confused or waiting:

reassure them

explain cleaner ETA

Step 4 — Decide
Options:

continue job

reschedule

cancel with fees

cancel without fees

dispatch another cleaner

Step 5 — Log Notes
Support logs summary into system logs.

---------------------------------------------------------
5.2 DISPUTE SUPPORT SOP
Support’s job is NOT to take sides.
It is to enforce rules with evidence.

Steps:
Gather Evidence

before/after photos

client photos

instructions

GPS logs

timestamp logs

Send Cleaner Dispute Notification
Cleaner gets 12 hours to respond.

Analyze Evidence Objectively
Cleaner wins if:

before photos match reality

after photos show clear improvement

issue was not in original instructions

Client wins if:

clear areas were not cleaned

cleaner skipped photos

cleaner failed check-in

cleaner left early

Render Decision
Types:

full refund

partial refund

no refund

re-clean (optional marketplace feature)

fraud escalation

Apply System Updates

adjust wallet

adjust earnings

apply reliability penalties

log case

Close Dispute
Notify both parties with short, neutral explanation.

---------------------------------------------------------
5.3 PAYMENT & PAYOUT SUPPORT SOP
When payout is delayed or failed:

Step 1 — Check Stripe Dashboard
Common issues:

KYC incomplete

invalid bank

payout blocked for fraud

Step 2 — Notify Cleaner
Template:
“Your payout didn’t complete because [reason]. Please update your bank info.”

Step 3 — Manual Override (If Allowed)
Only in special cases.

---------------------------------------------------------
5.4 FRAUD SUPPORT SOP
If potential fraud:

freeze account

freeze payout

notify user

request ID verification

escalate case to fraud admin

evidence review

write fraud case summary

Fraud examples:

duplicate photos

GPS spoofing

repeated dispute abuse

using multiple accounts

---------------------------------------------------------
5.5 ACCESS FAILURE SUPPORT SOP
If cleaner cannot enter:

Step 1
Request photo of locked door/gate.

Step 2
Check client’s access instructions.

Step 3
If client error:

no refund

pay cleaner partial/full

If cleaner error:

refund client

reliability penalty

---------------------------------------------------------
5.6 CLEANER CONDUCT SUPPORT SOP
Reported issues include:

rudeness

inappropriate comments

dangerous behavior

poor hygiene

property damage

Support actions:

log complaint

request cleaner’s statement

check past behavior

determine penalty

decide disciplinary action (warning → suspension → removal)

---------------------------------------------------------
5.7 CLIENT MISCONDUCT SUPPORT SOP
Examples:

verbal abuse

false dispute attempts

inappropriate messages

harassment

cancellation abuse

Support actions:

log incident

issue warning

restrict account

blacklist client if needed

---------------------------------------------------------
5.8 SENSITIVE CASES & SAFETY ISSUES SOP
Support must escalate immediately.

Examples:

theft allegations

harassment claims

unsafe home environment

threats

discrimination

medical emergencies

Support steps:

Freeze job

Remove cleaner from location

Escalate to Tier 1 support supervisor

Document everything

Suspend parties involved until review complete

---------------------------------------------------------
6. ADMIN ESCALATION LADDER
Support follows escalation levels:

Level 1
General support agents
Handle: normal cases, simple disputes, refunds.

Level 2
Senior support / dispute specialists
Handle:

complex disputes

Handle:

Handle:

summary of incident

timeline

Goal:
High enforcement accuracy + high customer satisfaction.

Perfect — continuing now with SECTION 4F, one of the most mission-critical systems in the entire PureTask ecosystem:

=========================================================
⭐ 4F — DISPUTE RESOLUTION SOP (ADMIN PROCEDURES — ULTRA-EXPANDED CANON)
=========================================================
The Dispute Resolution System is the courtroom of PureTask.
It must be:

fair

consistent

unbiased

evidence-based

fast

predictable

resistant to manipulation

fully enforceable

A weak dispute system destroys trust.
A strong dispute system reduces:

refunds

fraud

churn

complaints

support workload

This canon defines EXACTLY how PureTask resolves disputes at scale.

---------------------------------------------------------
0. DISPUTE PHILOSOPHY (PURETASK STANDARD)
PureTask resolves disputes based on:

1. Evidence (not emotion)
Photos > claims
GPS logs > storytelling
Timelines > memory

2. Pre-defined rules
Consistent outcomes → predictable marketplace.

3. Speed
The longer a dispute stays open, the angrier both sides get.

4. Neutrality
PureTask NEVER assumes:

“clients are always right”

“cleaners are always right”

We remain independent.

5. Protection
We protect:

cleaners from unfair clients

clients from low-quality or dishonest cleaners

---------------------------------------------------------
1. DISPUTE TRIGGERS
Clients can open a dispute ONLY if:

they have NOT approved the job

they submit before the auto-approval window expires (e.g., 24 hours)

Dispute button appears ONLY after:

after photos are uploaded

client reviews them

client clicks “Dispute this cleaning”

Cleaner cannot dispute a client.
Cleaners may respond to disputes only.

---------------------------------------------------------
2. DISPUTE TYPES (CATEGORIES)
Every dispute must fall into one of these official categories:

⭐ 1. Quality Issue
Cleaner missed areas.

⭐ 2. Incomplete Job
Cleaner left early; job looks only partially done.

⭐ 3. Instructions Not Followed
Cleaner ignored specific client directions.

⭐ 4. Incorrect Before/After Photos
Cleaner took:

wrong rooms

inconsistent angles

unclear or blurry images

⭐ 5. Behavior Issue
Cleaner:

acted unprofessionally

was rude

created uncomfortable environment

⭐ 6. Property Damage
Broken items — requires photos or description.

⭐ 7. Fraud / Dishonesty
Cleaner:

reused old photos

staged photos

manipulated timestamps

spoofed check-in

⭐ 8. Access or Timing Dispute
Cleaner was very late or way too early.

---------------------------------------------------------
3. DISPUTE INTAKE SOP (CLIENT FLOW)
When client opens a dispute:

Step 1 — Client chooses category.
Step 2 — Client writes explanation.
Step 3 — Client uploads photo evidence.
Step 4 — Dispute enters awaiting_cleaner state.
Cleaner is notified instantly.

---------------------------------------------------------
4. CLEANER RESPONSE SOP
Cleaner MUST respond within 12 hours.

Cleaner must:

provide explanation

upload counter-evidence

clarify instructions

explain issues (e.g., unsafe environment, missing supplies)

If cleaner DOES NOT RESPOND:

admin escalated

job decided in client’s favor unless evidence clearly supports cleaner

cleaner reliability penalty applied (-10 to -30)

---------------------------------------------------------
5. ADMIN EVIDENCE PACKAGE (AUTO-GENERATED)
When a dispute is opened, PureTask automatically collects:

Evidence Collected:
all before photos

all after photos

room mapping

cleaner check-in GPS + timestamp

cleaner check-out GPS + timestamp

job duration

instructions

chat messages

system logs

dispute history of cleaner and client

metadata & fraud signals

This builds the Dispute Packet.

The admin reviews this, not scattered data.

---------------------------------------------------------
6. BURDEN OF PROOF RULES
⭐ If cleaner followed checklist + photos correct → cleaner protected.
⭐ If cleaner’s photos are missing or insufficient → client receives refund.
⭐ If client claims something with no evidence → claim dismissed.
⭐ If instructions were unclear → admin favors cleaner.
⭐ If cleaner ignored instructions → admin favors client.
⭐ If before photos show extreme mess beyond time booked → partial refund only.
⭐ If after photos show clear improvement → cleaner wins unless missing key areas.
⭐ If cleaner left early (via timestamps) → partial refund.
These rules guarantee consistency.

---------------------------------------------------------
7. EVIDENCE EVALUATION FRAMEWORK (ADMIN)
Admin must evaluate:

A. Before & After Photo Consistency
Check:

same angle?

same room?

similar lighting?

real difference shown?

B. Missed Areas
Ask:

did instructions mention these areas?

are they part of standard cleaning?

were they visible in before photos?

C. Job Duration
Compare:

scheduled hours

actual hours

were after photos rushed?

D. Cleaner Conduct
Check chat for:

politeness

professionalism

refusal to cooperate

E. Client Behavior
Check for:

unreasonable demands

poor instructions

pre-existing clutter not disclosed

F. Fraud Indicators
Red flags include:

identical photos to previous jobs

metadata mismatches

cleaners not at job location

clients staging conditions for refund abuse

---------------------------------------------------------
8. DISPUTE DECISION TYPES (OUTCOMES)
Admin may choose:

⭐ 1. FULL REFUND
Conditions:

cleaner missed major areas

photos missing

cleaner left early

fraudulent photos

unprofessional behavior

client was clearly correct

Cleaner consequences:

no payout

reliability: -15 to -40

possible suspension

⭐ 2. PARTIAL REFUND
Most common and fairest.

Conditions:

cleaner completed MOST but missed some parts

unclear instructions

home extremely messy

cleaner spent full time but did not achieve expectations

Refund % range:

20%

30%

40%

50%

Cleaner consequences:

partial payout

moderate reliability deduction

⭐ 3. FULL RELEASE (Cleaner Wins)
Conditions:

cleaner did quality work

evidence supports cleaner

client unreasonable

dispute abuse detected

instructions ambiguous

Client consequences:

dispute abuse flag if repeated

⭐ 4. RE-CLEAN OPTION
Optional product feature.

Conditions:

work unsatisfactory but not malicious

client willing to allow another cleaner

cleaner admits mistakes

Cleaner consequences:

re-clean performed by another cleaner

first cleaner may receive partial payout

reliability deduction small

⭐ 5. FRAUD CASE (Cleaner or Client)
If evidence supports fraud:

payout frozen

account suspended

escalated to Fraud Ops

police report available for serious cases

Examples:

repeated photo recycling

GPS spoofing

staged “dirty photos” by client

false claims

device fingerprint suspicious patterns

---------------------------------------------------------
9. DISPUTE COMMUNICATION TEMPLATES (CRITICAL)
Tone must remain neutral.

⭐ Cleaner Wins (Full Release)
"After reviewing the photo evidence and job records, we found that the cleaning met PureTask standards. No refund will be issued. Thank you for your understanding.”

⭐ Client Wins (Full Refund)
“Thank you for your patience. Based on the evidence reviewed, the cleaning did not meet PureTask standards. A full refund has been issued.”

⭐ Partial Refund
“We’ve reviewed all evidence and determined that part of the cleaning was completed and part was not. A partial refund of X credits has been applied.”

⭐ Fraud Warning
“Our review identified inconsistencies that violate PureTask rules. Your account is temporarily suspended pending investigation.”

---------------------------------------------------------
10. ADMIN ESCALATION LOGIC
Admin may escalate disputes to:

Level 2 — Dispute Specialist
unclear evidence

first-time errors

client emotional escalation

Level 3 — Risk & Fraud
metadata anomalies

photo duplication

GPS inconsistency

multi-account suspicion

Level 4 — Operations Lead
severe misconduct

threats

press/legal escalation

repeated fraud behavior

---------------------------------------------------------
11. POST-DISPUTE ACTIONS (SYSTEM EVENTS)
After the decision:

System applies:
wallet adjustments

escrow release/refund

reliability changes

tier recalculations

earning ledger updates

fraud flags (if needed)

Admin must:

document the case

tag dispute with category

add notes for pattern tracking

---------------------------------------------------------
12. DISPUTE PATTERN ANALYTICS
System tracks:

Client Patterns:
dispute rate

partial refund frequency

“refund-seeking” behavior

historical trust score

Cleaner Patterns:
number of disputes in last 30/60/90 days

dispute win/loss ratio

photo compliance patterns

lateness correlation

Marketplace Health Metrics:
dispute rate by tier

dispute rate per cleaner onboarding group

dispute categories trending

---------------------------------------------------------
13. DISPUTE ABUSE POLICY (CLIENT & CLEANER)
If client abuses disputes:
warning

temporary removal of dispute privileges

increased scrutiny

eventual removal

If cleaner abuses:
repeated poor performance

repeated missing photos

repeated mismatch angles

manipulation attempts

Outcome:

demotion

suspension

permanent removal

---------------------------------------------------------
14. DISPUTE CLOSURE SOP
A dispute is closed when:

decision issued

credits adjusted

cleaner payout updated

both parties notified

admin logs completed

Case becomes read-only and archived.
