Understood — continuing now with SECTION 4G, one of the most sensitive, complex, and strategically vital parts of the entire PureTask operational system:

=========================================================
⭐ 4G — FRAUD PREVENTION & RISK OPERATIONS (ULTRA-EXPANDED CANON)
=========================================================
Fraud destroys marketplaces.
Risk Ops protects:

payouts

trust

platform integrity

client safety

cleaner earnings

legal compliance

PureTask’s fraud system is designed to:

detect

prevent

investigate

document

escalate

enforce consequences

without harming legitimate cleaners or clients.

This is a multi-layered fraud and risk system.

---------------------------------------------------------
0. FRAUD PHILOSOPHY
PureTask fraud operations are built on 4 principles:

1. Presumption of Neutrality
Never assume guilt based on complaint tone.
Decisions = based on data, evidence, pattern recognition.

2. Layered Detection
Fraud is caught by:

automated signals

metadata analysis

behavior patterns

human review

cross-account linking

3. Silent Enforcement
Cleaners/clients should never know EXACT fraud detection mechanisms.

4. Payout Protection First
Fraud investigations always freeze funds until resolved.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. FRAUD SIGNAL CATEGORIES
Fraud signals fall into 7 main categories:

⭐ A. GPS FRAUD
spoofed location

check-in far from actual address

check-in before arriving

inconsistent radius changes

GPS jumps > 200 meters in 1 second

repeated “GPS unavailable” patterns

⭐ B. PHOTO FRAUD
reused before/after photos from old jobs

using internet or stock images

AI-generated or heavily edited images

metadata mismatch

same exact image in multiple disputes

camera noise pattern identical across jobs

angles do not match real before photo

⭐ C. TIME FRAUD
cleaner claims they spent X hours but timeline logs show less

extremely short check-in → check-out

check-out triggered without completing tasks

suspiciously long duration with no photo updates

⭐ D. DISPUTE FRAUD (Client or Cleaner)
By client:
filing disputes on every job

manufactured mess after cleaning

requesting refunds for subjective reasons

using old photos as evidence

By cleaner:
lying about instructions

denying missing areas when photos clearly show it

⭐ E. PAYMENT FRAUD
stolen credit cards

chargeback attempts

mismatched billing addresses

multiple failed payment attempts

⭐ F. MULTI-ACCOUNT FRAUD
Cleaner multi-accounting:
creating second account after penalty

sharing bank account with banned cleaner

using same device for multiple accounts

Client multi-accounting:
creating multiple accounts for promos

bypassing bans

⭐ G. BEHAVIORAL FRAUD
aggressive attempt to manipulate support

refusing to upload required evidence

threatening reviews unless refunded

“refund extortion”

---------------------------------------------------------
2. AUTOMATED FRAUD DETECTION SYSTEM (RISK ENGINE)
PureTask automates fraud detection with the Risk Engine, which evaluates:

GPS logs

metadata

timestamps

photo similarity

device identity

dispute patterns

financial signals

Every account has a Risk Score (0–100).
Scores update daily.

Risk Score Thresholds:
0–29 = normal

30–59 = low-risk

60–79 = medium-risk

80–100 = high-risk (flag for review)

---------------------------------------------------------
3. RISK ENGINE TRIGGERS
When any fraud signal appears:

Risk Engine computes a Flag Event, including:
reason

weight

timestamp

associated job ID

associated user

Certain events trigger Payout Hold or Account Freeze immediately.

---------------------------------------------------------
4. PAYOUT FRAUD PREVENTION SOP (CRITICAL)
Before every payout:

The system checks:
GPS integrity across all jobs

photo integrity

dispute history

bank account match

cleaner device fingerprint

earning spike anomalies

location transition patterns

repeated late cancels

metadata discrepancies

If ANY anomaly detected:

Payout = Frozen

cleaner notified: “Your payout is under review.”

Payout remains frozen until admin clearance.

---------------------------------------------------------
5. FRAUD INVESTIGATION WORKFLOW (ADMIN SOP)
When a fraud flag occurs:

⭐ Step 1 — Collect All Evidence Automatically
System compiles:

photo metadata

image hashing / similarity test

GPS logs

movement path

timeline events

chat logs

ID verification

Stripe account details

device fingerprint

account history

⭐ Step 2 — Admin Reviews Evidence Packet
Admin checks:

were photos reused?

does metadata match the job date/time?

was check-in legitimate?

were timestamps manipulated?

are there multiple accounts tied to same device?

⭐ Step 3 — Determine Category of Fraud
Fraud types:

Photo Fraud

GPS Spoofing

Time Manipulation

Staged Disputes

Payment Fraud

Multi-Accounting

Behavioral Abuse

⭐ Step 4 — Apply Temporary Action
Based on severity:

freeze payout

freeze account

suspend jobs

require ID verification

require video verification

request additional documents

⭐ Step 5 — Final Decision
Admin chooses:

1. No Fraud — Restore Account
Risk score reset.

2. Minor Violation — Warning + Penalty
reliability reduction

mandatory re-training

partial payout withheld

3. Moderate Fraud — Suspension
7–30 day suspension

payout forfeiture may apply

4. Severe Fraud — Permanent Ban
account closed

device fingerprint banned

bank account banned

phone/email banned

IP flagged

possible legal escalation

---------------------------------------------------------
6. FRAUD TYPE DEEP-DIVE SOPs
⭐ A. PHOTO FRAUD SOP
Red flags:
identical after photos across multiple jobs

metadata from wrong timestamps

AI artifacts

different home than the job location

after photos clearly not matching before photos

Admin Action:
compare photo EXIF

run image similarity check (hashing)

check job location vs photo location (if location embedded)

freeze payout

demand explanation

If fraud confirmed → permanent ban.

⭐ B. GPS SPOOFING SOP
Signals:
sudden teleportation

inconsistent device GPS signature

third-party GPS spoofing app detected

check-in far from home

Admin Action:
freeze payout

require cleaner to redo GPS test

possible re-training

high severity → account ban

⭐ C. MULTI-ACCOUNT CLEANER FRAUD SOP
Detection Signals:
same device fingerprint

same bank account

same address/ID

same IP repeatedly

same photos used across accounts

Admin Action:

freeze all linked accounts

investigate origin

ban all fraudulent accounts

allow legitimate family members only after rigid verification

⭐ D. CLIENT REFUND ABUSE SOP
Client repeatedly:

disputes everything

requests refunds after approval

tries to push cleaners below fair expectations

Admin Action:

mark client as high-risk

require supervisor approval for future refunds

remove ability to dispute

eventual account removal

⭐ E. PAYMENT FRAUD SOP
Triggers:

chargeback attempt

stolen card report

mismatched billing info

extremely rapid credit purchases + cancellations

Admin Action:

lock wallet

lock account

notify Stripe

legal protocol available

---------------------------------------------------------
7. AUTOMATED FRAUD SCORING (WEIGHTS)
Each fraud signal carries a different weight.

Severe (30–50 points)
duplicate photos

GPS spoofing

payment fraud

identity mismatch

multi-account

chargebacks

Moderate (10–20 points)
unclear metadata

repeated disputes from same user

mismatched timelines

Mild (1–10 points)
accidental wrong photo

minor lateness

occasional cancellation patterns

When Risk Score ≥ 80 → auto-freeze.

---------------------------------------------------------
8. FRAUD COMMUNICATION SOPs
Communication must be:

neutral

non-accusatory

procedural

We NEVER say:
“You committed fraud.”

Instead say:

“Your job evidence contained inconsistencies that need review.”

“Your payout is temporarily on hold pending verification.”

“We need additional information before releasing funds.”

“Your account is under investigation due to unusual activity.”

---------------------------------------------------------
9. FRAUD CASE DOCUMENTATION REQUIREMENTS
Every case must include:

summary of suspicion

evidence collected

admin notes

timestamps

final decision

actions taken

whether account banned or restored

Poor documentation = legal liability.

---------------------------------------------------------
10. FRAUD APPEALS PROCESS
Banned users may request a single appeal.

Process:

User submits appeal form

Must provide:

explanation

supporting evidence

Fraud specialist reviews

Decision:

upheld

overturned

probation reinstatement

No further appeals permitted.

---------------------------------------------------------
11. LONG-TERM RISK MITIGATION STRATEGIES
A. Random Quality Audits
Periodic spot-checks of cleaner results.

B. AI Photo Verification
Detects:

AI images

duplicates

inconsistencies

C. Pattern Detection
Flag:

fast-earning anomalies

repeated disputes

cluster of bad jobs

D. Marketplace Balancing
High dispute rate cleaners get fewer jobs.

🎉 4G COMPLETE — FRAUD PREVENTION & RISK OPERATIONS

Perfect — continuing with SECTION 4H, which covers the entire Quality Assurance & Marketplace Health System for PureTask.

This section is extremely important because it determines:

the cleanliness standard of the entire platform

how cleaner quality is measured, tracked, and improved

how the marketplace stays balanced

Let’s build the full canon.

=========================================================
⭐ 4H — QUALITY ASSURANCE & MARKETPLACE HEALTH SYSTEMS (ULTRA-EXPANDED CANON)
=========================================================
Quality Assurance (QA) is the heartbeat of PureTask’s long-term success.

If quality slips →
clients churn, disputes rise, refunds increase, trust erodes.

If quality is high →
cleaners earn more, clients return, disputes drop, operations scale smoothly.

PureTask’s QA system integrates:

photo analysis

client feedback

cleaner performance metrics

reliability scores

marketplace balancing algorithms

periodic audits

coaching workflows

automated alerts

This section defines the complete QA system.

---------------------------------------------------------
0. QA PHILOSOPHY (PURETASK STANDARD)
Quality is defined by three pillars:

1. Outcome Evidence (Photo Proof)
Before/after photos are the ultimate truth.
They override opinions, emotions, and “he said she said.”

2. Consistency
A cleaner must perform consistently across ALL jobs, not only good ones.

3. Client Satisfaction
Satisfaction is derived from:

quality

communication

professionalism

punctuality

All three must align.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. THE PURETASK QUALITY SCORE (CLEANER QA SCORE)
Every cleaner has a Quality Score separate from reliability.

Quality Score Components:
Component	Weight
Photo Quality & Consistency	35%
Checklist Completion	20%
Client Ratings	20%
Dispute Outcomes	15%
Random QA Audits	10%
This creates a 0–100 QA Score.

QA Score Tiers:
90–100 = Elite Quality

80–89 = Strong Quality

70–79 = Acceptable Quality

60–69 = Needs Improvement

0–59 = At-Risk / Intervention Required

QA score influences:

job visibility

tier eligibility

payout bonuses (future feature)

coaching requirements

risk flags

---------------------------------------------------------
2. PHOTO QUALITY STANDARDS
Photo quality is the #1 factor in verifying performance.

A correct photo must:

be well-lit

show all surfaces

match angles from before → after

not be blurry

not be taken too close or too far

not hide messes intentionally

Automatic Photo Analysis (System Rules)
PureTask uses automated logic:

angle similarity

brightness threshold

blur detection

duplication detection

room recognition (optional AI upgrade)

If photos fail threshold:

system flags cleaner

QA score reduced

reliability impacted

---------------------------------------------------------
3. CHECKLIST COMPLETION SYSTEM
Cleaners must complete the built-in checklist for every job.

Checklist items include:

bathroom sinks

tubs/showers

kitchen counters

floors

dusting

appliances

trash

etc.

Rules:
checklist must be completed BEFORE submitting job

incomplete checklist → lower QA score

missing required items → reliability penalty

repeated incomplete checklists → training required

---------------------------------------------------------
4. CLIENT FEEDBACK INTEGRATION
Clients rate jobs on:

cleaning quality (1–5 stars)

communication

professionalism

overall satisfaction

Optional (written feedback).

Rating Impact Logic:
5 stars → +2 QA points

4 stars → +1 QA point

3 stars → -1 QA point

2 stars → -3 QA points

1 star → -5 QA points

Extreme client feedback triggers:

risk review

coaching

potential suspension

All feedback analyzed for patterns.

---------------------------------------------------------
5. DISPUTE OUTCOME IMPACTS
If cleaner LOSES dispute → QA Score reduction:

Outcome	QA Penalty
Partial Refund	-5 to -10
Full Refund	-15 to -30
Fraud Finding	-40 to -60
If cleaner WINS dispute → QA Score increase:

minor boost (+1 to +3)

This rewards legitimate cleaners and discourages dishonest ones.

---------------------------------------------------------
6. RANDOM QA AUDITS (PROACTIVE QUALITY CHECKS)
PureTask performs random audits on:

photo sets

job timelines

client reviews

Audit types:

1. Standard Audit
Check:

photos match task

timeline realistic

quality acceptable

2. Deep Audit
When risk engine flags potential issues.

3. Tier Promotion Audit
Before moving to Platinum, cleaner must pass random audit.

4. High-Value Client Audit
VIP or recurring clients receive priority audits.

If cleaner fails audit:

QA score decreases

reliability decreases

possible tier freeze

---------------------------------------------------------
7. MARKETPLACE HEALTH METRICS (PLATFORM LEVEL QA)
PureTask monitors marketplace health through:

A. Supply-to-Demand Ratios
too many cleaners → not enough jobs

too many clients → not enough cleaners

System automatically adjusts cleaner visibility.

B. Dispute Rate
Target: <2% of all jobs
Warning Zone: 2–5%
Danger Zone: >5%

C. Approval Time
Average approval time should be <12 hours.

D. Cleaner Acceptance Rate
Healthy: 50–70% of jobs offered
Low: <30% = burnout or mispricing
High: >90% = desperation or quality risk

E. Cancellation Rate
Cleaners: <5%
Clients: <10%

F. Job Completion Consistency
Track time-in vs time-out across cleaners.

---------------------------------------------------------
8. CLEANER PERFORMANCE FLAGS & AUTOMATED ALERTS
System automatically generates alerts:

“Declining Quality Alert”
Triggered if cleaner’s last 5 QA Scores trend downward.

“High Dispute Risk Alert”
If dispute rate >10% for a cleaner.

“Photo Quality Alert”
If blur or lighting issues detected repeatedly.

“Checklist Consistency Alert”
If cleaner repeatedly forgets checklist items.

“Time Fraud Alert”
If cleaner repeatedly checks out too early.

Alerts automatically reduce:

job visibility

tier eligibility

reliability score

---------------------------------------------------------
9. COACHING & INTERVENTION WORKFLOWS
PureTask proactively improves cleaner quality through:

⭐ Phase 1 — Soft Coaching
Triggered when:

QA Score drops below 70

2–3 low ratings recently

Cleaner receives:

automated tips

training module reminders

best practices

⭐ Phase 2 — Performance Warning
Triggered when:

QA Score <65

dispute patterns emerging

Cleaner receives:

email warning

retraining requirement

limited job visibility

⭐ Phase 3 — Mandatory Retraining
Triggered when:

repeated QC failures

photo violations

checklist failures

Cleaner must watch:

photo training again

cleaning standard videos

reliability education

⭐ Phase 4 — Suspension
Triggered when:

unresolved quality issues

repeated low QC scores

dispute/fraud pattern

Cleaner may return only after:

passing re-training

admin review

⭐ Phase 5 — Permanent Removal
For:

repeatedly low quality

fraud attempts

refusing to comply with QC

---------------------------------------------------------
10. CLIENT SATISFACTION PROGRAM
PureTask uses:

A. NPS-style feedback
“How likely are you to book PureTask again?”

B. Issue Detection
If client gives low rating:

prompt follow-up

proactive credit gift (optional retention strategy)

C. Recurring Client Monitoring
For recurring clients, PureTask checks:

satisfaction trends

job quality consistency

cleaner-client pairing quality

---------------------------------------------------------
11. CLEANER–CLIENT MATCHING (QUALITY-BASED)
PureTask assigns cleaners based on:

tier

quality score

reliability

proximity

past performance with similar homes

dispute history

High-value clients → matched with Gold + Platinum cleaners.

Low-rated cleaners → fewer clients until performance improves.

---------------------------------------------------------
12. MARKETPLACE BALANCING (SUPPLY/DEMAND HEALTH)
PureTask uses dynamic balancing:

Too many cleaners → not enough jobs
Reduce visibility of low-quality cleaners.

Too few cleaners → too many jobs
Fast-track onboarding
Promote high-performing cleaners
Boost job notifications

Too many disputes
Lower visibility of problem cleaners
Coach or remove outliers

Too many cancellations
Analyze which side is causing problems
Apply corrective actions

---------------------------------------------------------
13. CLEANER TIER IMPACT ON QA
Tiers reinforce quality:

Bronze
strict monitoring

limited visibility

Silver
acceptable quality required

random audits frequent

Gold
high-quality consistency

fewer audits

Platinum
highest expectations

strict penalties for slip-ups

A cleaner cannot rise to Platinum if:

recent disputes exist

QA Score <90

photo quality inconsistent

---------------------------------------------------------
0. ADMIN ORGANIZATION STRUCTURE
PureTask operations are divided into 4 internal groups:

1. Support Team (Tier 1)
Handles:

general support

cancellations

basic refunds

simple disputes

troubleshooting

2. Dispute Specialists (Tier 2)
Handles:

complex disputes

photo evaluation

checklist failures

borderline cases

high-value clients

3. Risk/Fraud Team (Tier 3)
Handles:

fraud detection

GPS/photo anomalies

payment issues

identity mismatch

multi-account fraud

payout holds

4. Operations Leads / Platform Admins (Tier 4)
Handles:

escalations

legal-sensitive issues

safety incidents

PR threats

severe platform bugs

high-risk bans

Each level has increasing access, authority, and responsibility.

---------------------------------------------------------
1. ROLE PERMISSIONS MATRIX
Action	Support	Dispute Specialist	Risk/Fraud	Ops Lead
View user data	✔	✔	✔	✔
Edit user data	✘	✔ (limited)	✔	✔
Issue refunds	✔ (limited)	✔	✔	✔
Override payouts	✘	✘	✔	✔
Ban users	✘	✘	✔ (soft ban)	✔ (full ban)
Handle disputes	✔ (simple)	✔ (complex)	✔ (fraud-related)	✔
Freeze accounts	✘	✘	✔	✔
Access fraud tools	✘	✘	✔	✔
Modify system settings	✘	✘	✘	✔
Support has the smallest access.
Ops Lead has full platform authority.

---------------------------------------------------------
2. DAILY OPERATIONS CHECKLIST (ADMIN)
Admins follow a daily operational routine to ensure marketplace health.

A. Review Overnight Jobs
jobs awaiting approval

auto-approvals

disputes opened overnight

no-shows

Check for:

unresolved P1/P2 tickets

payout questions

C. Review Fraud Flags
Look at risk engine alerts:

duplicate photo detection

GPS anomalies

multi-account risks

D. Review Payout Queue
Check:

pending payouts

failed payouts

payouts on hold

E. Check Cleaner Performance Alerts
Look for:

low reliability

declining QA

dispute spike

F. System Error Logs
If automations failed overnight, escalate.

---------------------------------------------------------
3. WEEKLY OPERATIONS CHECKLIST
Once per week:

A. Tier Recalculation Audit
Verify:

all cleaners properly tiered

reliability adjustments accurate

no suspended cleaners accidentally promoted

B. Random Job Quality Audit
Pick X% of the week's photos:

check quality consistency

check against disputes

C. Review Marketplace Health Metrics
dispute rate

client retention

job completion time

D. Fraud Case Review
Check:

any unresolved fraud investigations

Automatically send:

Review:

5. ADMIN SHIFTS & HANDOFF PROTOCOLS
This prevents dropped cases or confusion.

safety issues

Handoff report must include:

summary line for each case

next required action

expected resolution timeline

Admins reviewing the handoff must acknowledge receipt.

---------------------------------------------------------
6. INTERNAL COMMUNICATION STANDARDS
Admins communicate internally using strict clarity standards.

Rules:
✔ concise
✔ evidence-focused
✔ no emotional speculation
✔ neutral reasoning
✔ reference job IDs and timestamps

Forbidden:
❌ vague accusations
❌ “I think” / “Feels like”
❌ taking sides prematurely
❌ unsupported judgments

Example:

Good:
“Photos show incomplete bathroom cleaning. Client’s evidence matches before photo. Recommend partial refund of 40%.”

Bad:
“Client seems upset, maybe refund?”

---------------------------------------------------------
7. DOCUMENTATION STANDARDS (CRITICAL)
Every admin action must be stored in system_logs with:

action type

user affected

admin identifier

evidence summary

policy justification

decision notes

timestamps

Proper documentation is essential for:

scalability

legal protection

internal accountability

---------------------------------------------------------
8. INTERNAL ESCALATION SYSTEM
The platform uses a strict 4-level escalation ladder:

Level 1 → Support
Handles:

simple user issues

standard refunds

cancellations

basic troubleshooting

Escalate to Level 2 when:
client threatens dispute escalation

evidence unclear

repeated complaints

high-value job

Level 2 → Dispute Specialist
Handles:

complex disputes

borderline evidence cases

partial refund decisions

pattern recognition

Escalate to Level 3 when:
fraud suspected

metadata inconsistent

GPS anomalies

multiple disputes across accounts

Level 3 → Risk/Fraud Team
Handles:

multi-account detection

high-risk payouts

identity mismatches

chargebacks

fraud allegations

Escalate to Level 4 when:
legal action threatened

severe safety incident

PR-sensitive issue

Level 4 → Operations Lead / Founder
Handles:

police involvement

theft allegations

physical altercations

sexual harassment cases

extremely sensitive disputes

global system outages

dangerous media exposure

This ensures that the right people handle the right level of severity.

---------------------------------------------------------
9. ADMIN OVERRIDE RULES
Overrides must be rare and justified.

Admins may override:

credits

refunds

reliability score

tier

suspension

But only with documentation such as:

“Client provided evidence not visible in app.”

“Cleaner confirmed app bug prevented photo upload.”

“Risk team confirmed false-positive fraud flag.”

Override abuse leads to internal review.

---------------------------------------------------------
10. EMERGENCY PROTOCOLS
A. Safety Threat (Cleaner or Client)
Admin must immediately:

Freeze job

Instruct cleaner to leave immediately

Offer emergency support to client if needed

Document thoroughly

Escalate to operations lead

B. Medical Emergency
Support must call emergency services if needed and stay on line until resolved.

C. Platform Outage
Admins must:

Halt all active jobs

Notify all users

Restore system

After resolution → issue compensation where needed

D. Payment Processor Outage (Stripe)
freeze payouts

notify cleaners

document

resume once Stripe stable

---------------------------------------------------------
11. INTERNAL SECURITY & ACCESS SAFETY
Admins must:

use 2FA

never share login credentials

never access user accounts without reason

store all documents securely

log out of shared devices

Violations lead to disciplinary action.

marketplace health

=========================================================
⭐ 5A — PURETASK CREDIT ECONOMY & ESCROW SYSTEM (ULTRA-EXPANDED)
=========================================================
PureTask uses credits (tokens) instead of direct dollar payments.

This gives the platform:

full control of money flow

ability to manage disputes

instant refunds

instant approvals

cleaner payout consistency

fraud protection

scalable automation without banking delays

1. CREDIT VALUE
1 credit = $1 USD (or local equivalent).
Simple, intuitive.

2. HOW CREDITS MOVE THROUGH PURETASK
Step 1 — Client purchases credits
Purchases with Stripe → credits added to wallet

Credits remain available until used

Step 2 — Client books a job
Estimated job total = X credits

Credits moved from wallet → escrow

Cleaner sees the payout value

Step 3 — Cleaner completes job + submits photos
Job enters “awaiting approval.”

Step 4 — Client approves
Escrow releases

Credits move from escrow → cleaner earnings wallet

Step 5 — Cleaner payout (weekly or instant)
Credits convert to USD and deposit to cleaner bank via Stripe.

3. ESCROW LOGIC (THE HEART OF THE SYSTEM)
Escrow protects both sides.

Credits cannot be released if:
dispute open

job not approved

photos missing

fraud flags active

client did not respond and auto-approval not triggered yet

Escrow release triggers:
client manual approval

auto-approval timer expires

Escrow holds stronger during:
disputes

late submissions

fraud or GPS anomalies

4. ESCROW EDGE CASES
A. Escrow Held Due to Dispute
Credits locked until admin makes a ruling.

B. Client Cancels Before Job
Credits return to wallet (full or partial depending on timing).

C. Cleaner No-Show
Escrow refunded fully to client.

D. Client No-Show / Access Failure
Escrow partially or fully released to cleaner.

E. Fraud Detected
Escrow frozen until fraud investigation complete.

F. Admin Override
Admins can manually release/reverse escrow in extreme circumstances.

5. ESCROW TRANSPARENCY
Users see:

Clients:
“Credits Held in Escrow: X”

“Pending Jobs: X”

Cleaners:
“Pending Earnings: X”

“Estimated Payout Date: Friday”

6. HOW ESCROW PREVENTS FRAUD
Escrow protects PureTask from:

client chargebacks

cleaners demanding early payouts

disputes without proof

incomplete jobs

staged job issues

cleaners who want to skip photos

clients who approve then demand refunds

It makes the system mathematically safe.

=========================================================
⭐ 5B — CLEANER EARNINGS SYSTEM (ULTRA-EXPANDED)
=========================================================
Cleaner earnings are based on:

job amount

quality

reliability

tiers

penalties

bonuses

Let’s break it down.

1. BASE EARNINGS = JOB VALUE
Example:
Client books $120 cleaning → cleaner sees 120 credits.

After approval → cleaner receives 120 credits in earnings wallet.

2. PARTIAL PAYOUT RULES (CRUCIAL)
Used when:

client cancels late

dispute results are partial

access failure

cleaner leaves early

job incomplete

extreme mess beyond booked time

Examples:
Scenario	Cleaner Receives
Client late cancellation	20–30%
Client access failure	50–100%
Cleaner partial completion	20–60%
Client wins partial dispute	40–80%
3. CLEANER PENALTIES THAT REDUCE PAYOUT
Violation	Earnings Impact
No before photos	payout reduced 20–40%
No after photos	payout withheld entirely until admin review
GPS spoofing	payout frozen
Leaving early	payout reduced based on time analysis
Fraud suspicion	payout frozen
Severe dispute loss	payout = 0
4. CLEAN TIER BONUS (OPTIONAL FEATURE)
Example:

Silver → +3% earnings

Gold → +5%

Platinum → +8%

Encourages quality and reliability.

5. CLEANER EARNINGS WALLET
Cleaner has two balances:

Pending Earnings
Jobs awaiting approval or auto-approval.

Available Earnings
Approved jobs ready for payout.

=========================================================
⭐ 5C — PAYOUT SYSTEM (WEEKLY + INSTANT PAY)
=========================================================
Cleaners are paid through Stripe Connect.

There are two payout types:

⭐ 1. WEEKLY PAYOUTS (DEFAULT)
Every Friday:

system sums available earnings

transfers to bank account

sends payout email

logs payout in ledger

If payout fails:

cleaner notified

bank info update requested

⭐ 2. INSTANT PAYOUT (OPTIONAL FEATURE)
Cleaner may tap “Instant Cash Out”, which:

charges instant payout fee (1–3%)

sends payout within minutes

increases platform revenue

Rules:

only available if risk score < threshold

cannot use during ongoing dispute

cannot use if fraud flag exists

3. PAYOUT HOLDS
Payout automatically paused if:

dispute open

fraud flagged

GPS anomaly detected

missing ID verification

bank account mismatch

negative balance

chargeback pending

Cleaner sees message:
“Your payout is temporarily on hold pending verification.”

4. NEGATIVE BALANCE HANDLING
Used when:

cleaner loses dispute after payout

admin reversal

penalty must be applied

Negative balance is deducted from future earnings.

=========================================================
⭐ 5D — FEES, PENALTIES & PLATFORM REVENUE MODEL
=========================================================
PureTask earns money through:

client credit purchases

platform fees

instant payout fees

cancellation fees

dispute outcome adjustments

Let’s detail all flows.

1. PLATFORM SERVICE FEE (CLIENT-SIDE)
When client buys credits:

Example:

client buys $100

platform fee 10%

client gets 100 credits

PureTask earns $10

Credits = full dollar value.
Fees taken at purchase, not from payout.

2. CLEANER DEDUCTION MODEL (OPTIONAL)
Instead of client fee → cleaner fee:

Cleaner receives:
job value × (100% – platform rate)

For example:
Platform rate 15% → cleaner receives 85%

Fees never double-charged. Only one model used.

3. INSTANT PAY FEES
Cleaner chooses instant payout:

1–3% fee

PureTask revenue

Example:
Cleaner cashes out $100 → receives $97
$3 becomes platform revenue.

4. CANCELLATION FEES
PureTask earns from:

Client Late Cancellation
client loses 20–30%

part goes to cleaner

remaining goes to platform

Cleaner Late Cancellation Penalty
platform retains penalty

no client loss

5. DISPUTE LOSS FEES
When cleaner loses:

payout reduced

platform retains difference

OR credits returned to client

Depends on policy.

=========================================================
⭐ 5E — REFUNDS, ADJUSTMENTS & RECONCILIATION
=========================================================
Refunds occur through credit-based system.

1. TYPES OF REFUNDS
Type	Description
Full Refund	Client receives all credits back
Partial Refund	Client receives percentage
Zero Refund	Cleaner wins dispute
Auto-Refund	No cleaner assigned
Refunds always go back to the client wallet, never to the card.

2. REFUND REASONS
client cancellation

dispute outcome

system error

safety issue

support override

3. REFUND RESTRICTIONS
Refund NOT allowed when:

client already approved job

dispute window expired

no supporting evidence

job completed successfully

4. LEDGER UPDATES FOR REFUNDS
Every refund triggers:

refund log

change in escrow

change in cleaner pending earnings

change in job state

audit entry

5. ADMIN OVERRIDES
Admin can override refunds ONLY with justification.
Overrides flagged for audit.

=========================================================
⭐ 5F — CHARGEBACK PREVENTION & RESPONSE
=========================================================
Chargebacks destroy marketplace profitability.
PureTask must prevent them aggressively.

1. PREVENTION THROUGH CREDIT ECONOMY
Clients NEVER pay for jobs directly → only buy credits.

If client disputes charge on card:

Stripe sees it as:

digital credit purchase

not service delivery

PureTask can:

freeze client account

provide credit purchase logs

submit evidence via Stripe

Marketplace safer.

2. CHARGEBACK RESPONSE SOP
When Stripe notifies of chargeback:

Step 1 — Lock client account
Cannot buy credits or book.

Step 2 — Pull internal evidence packet:
credit purchase

job logs

approval logs

photos

dispute history

Step 3 — Submit representment to Stripe.
Step 4 — If client loses:
Account remains locked until balance restored.

=========================================================
⭐ 5G — STRIPE CONNECT ARCHITECTURE & COMPLIANCE
=========================================================
PureTask uses Stripe Connect Standard or Express.

System must ensure:

KYC requirements met

banking/identity verified

tax reporting enabled

transfers safe and complaint

1. CONNECT ACCOUNT SETUP
Cleaners must complete:

ID verification

Address verification

Bank verification

If incomplete → payouts disabled.

2. REQUIRED DATA RETENTION
PureTask must retain:

payment logs

dispute logs

tax forms

client purchase receipts

cleaner payout receipts

In case of audits.

3. STRIPE WEBHOOKS REQUIRED
PureTask must listen to:

payment_intent.succeeded

payment_intent.failed

charge.refunded

transfer.paid

transfer.failed

payout.paid

payout.failed

customer.updated

Each updates system ledger.

=========================================================
⭐ 5H — FINANCIAL AUDITS, LOGS & LEDGER SYSTEM
=========================================================
Every credit movement must be recorded.

1. FINANCIAL LEDGER TYPES
Ledger A — Client Wallet
Tracks:

deposits

refunds

spends

adjustments

Ledger B — Escrow Ledger
Tracks:

job holds

releases

freezes

Ledger C — Cleaner Earnings Ledger
Tracks:

job earnings

penalties

adjustments

payouts

Ledger D — Platform Revenue Ledger
Tracks:

fees

penalties

instant payout fees

service fees

2. AUTOMATED DAILY RECONCILIATION
System checks:

total credits in circulation

total credits in escrow

total payouts

total platform revenue

inconsistencies

Any mismatches trigger immediate admin alert.

3. MONTHLY AUDIT SYSTEM
Includes:

fraud cases

payouts

refunds

ledger accuracy

dispute outcomes

Stripe transfers

Perfect — continuing with SECTION 6D, which defines the entire Notification System & Messaging UX for PureTask.

This system is critical because:

It drives user behavior

Reduces confusion

Ensures operational compliance

Prevents disputes

Reinforces reliability

Handles safety & emergencies

Creates a seamless user experience

Notifications must be:

timely

clear

actionable

non-annoying

context-aware

role-specific (client vs cleaner)

This canon defines all notification types, triggers, timing, and message templates.

=========================================================
⭐ 6D — NOTIFICATION SYSTEM & MESSAGING UX (ULTRA-EXPANDED CANON)
=========================================================
The Notification System includes:

Push Notifications

In-App Alerts

Email Notifications

SMS (optional for emergencies)

Automated System Messages (in chats)

Reliability & QA Alerts

Payment & Payout Alerts

Approval & Photo Alerts

Fraud, Safety, and Escalation Alerts

Each event in PureTask triggers specific notification logic.

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ PART 1: PUSH NOTIFICATIONS — CLIENT SIDE
Push notifications are used to keep clients informed in real-time.

A. Booking Notifications
Trigger: Client books a cleaning.

“Your cleaning for [DATE] at [TIME] is confirmed.”

“Cleaner [NAME] has been assigned to your job.”

Trigger: No cleaner assigned yet.

“We’re working to assign a cleaner. You’ll be notified soon.”

B. Pre-Job Notifications
24 hours before job:

“Reminder: Your cleaning with [CLEANER] is tomorrow at [TIME].”

1 hour before job:

“Your cleaner is on the way soon.”

C. Job In Progress
Cleaner checks in:

“Your cleaner has arrived and started the job.”

Cleaner submits job:

“Your cleaning is complete! Review the before & after photos.”

D. Approval Notifications
If client hasn’t reviewed after X hours:

“Your cleaning is awaiting approval.”

“Please review your cleaning photos before auto-approval.”

Auto-approval soon:

“Your job will auto-approve in 2 hours.”

After approval:

“Thanks for your review! Credits have been released.”

E. Dispute Notifications
Dispute Created:

“Your dispute has been received. We’ll review and update you soon.”

Dispute Resolved:

“Your dispute for job [ID] has been resolved.”

F. Cancellation Notifications
If job canceled by cleaner:

“Your cleaner canceled the job. We’re finding a replacement.”

If no replacement found:

“Your job has been canceled. Credits have been refunded.”

G. Wallet & Credit Notifications
“Your credits have been added successfully.”

“Your refund has been issued.”

“You may need more credits for your upcoming job.”

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ PART 2: PUSH NOTIFICATIONS — CLEANER SIDE
Cleaner notifications enforce operational rules.

A. Job Offers
When new job available:

“New job available near you. Earn [X credits]. Tap to view.”

Job expiring in X minutes:

“This job offer expires soon.”

B. Job Reminders
24 hours before job:

“Reminder: You have a job tomorrow at [TIME].”

1 hour before job:

“Your job starts soon. Please prepare.”

C. Check-In & Timing Notifications
If cleaner hasn’t checked in by start time:

“Your job has started. Please check in.”

If late:

“You are late for your job. This may affect your reliability.”

D. Photo Compliance Notifications
Before photos missing:

“You must take before photos to begin cleaning.”

After photos missing:

“After photos required before submitting job.”

Invalid photos detected:

“Some photos were unclear or mismatched. Please retake them.”

E. Earnings & Payout Notifications
After job approved:

“Job approved! You earned [X credits].”

Weekly payout:

“Your payout of [AMOUNT] has been sent.”

Instant payout:

“Your instant payout is complete.”

Payout failed:

“Your payout couldn’t be processed. Please update your bank info.”

F. Reliability Alerts
Low reliability warning:

“Your reliability has dropped below 80%. Fewer jobs may appear.”

Critical reliability warning:

“Your reliability is at risk. Please avoid cancellations or lateness.”

G. Disputes
New dispute opened:

“A client has disputed your recent job. Please respond within 12 hours.”

Dispute resolved:

“Your dispute for job [ID] has been resolved.”

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ PART 3: SYSTEM MESSAGES (IN-CHAT AUTOMATIC)
Automated system messages appear inside job chat for context.

Examples:

For Check-In:
“Cleaner checked in at [TIME].”

For Check-Out:
“Cleaner submitted job for review.”

For Cancellation:
“Job was canceled by the client/cleaner/system.”

For Access Issues:
“Cleaner reported access issue.”

For Disputes:
“A dispute has been opened for this job.”

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ PART 4: EMAIL NOTIFICATIONS
Email is used for:

receipts

onboarding

payouts

dispute summaries

fraud investigations

policy updates

important confirmations

Examples:
Receipt:

“Your credit purchase of $XX was successful.”

Payout:

“Your weekly payout of $XX has been processed.”

Suspension Notice:

“Your account has been temporarily suspended due to [reason].”

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ PART 5: SMS (OPTIONAL) FOR HIGH-SEVERITY EVENTS
Used only when:

safety threat

emergency access

cleaner stuck

client locked out

Example SMS:

“URGENT: Cleaner cannot access your home. Please respond.”

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ PART 6: TRIGGER-BASED NOTIFICATION ENGINE
The system triggers notifications based on events:

A. “Action Required” Events
missing photos

incomplete checklist

dispute response needed

payout blocked

ID verification required

B. “Time-Based” Events
job reminders

auto-approval countdown

dispute deadlines

C. “System Health” Events
payout failures

error during check-in

unusual GPS pattern

fraud flag

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ PART 7: NOTIFICATION PRIORITY SYSTEM
There are 4 priorities:

Priority 1 — Urgent
Must interrupt user:

safety alerts

dispute response deadline

payout failure requiring action

ID verification failure

Priority 2 — Important
Prominent but not urgent:

job reminders

job approval needed

missing photos

Priority 3 — Awareness
Informational:

payout success

refund issued

general updates

Priority 4 — Silent
Logged quietly:

background system updates

low-severity fraud flags

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ PART 8: MESSAGE TEMPLATES (SHORT & LONG FORMS)
Cleaner Running Late (Short Form)
“Reminder: Please check in to avoid reliability penalties.”

Cleaner Running Late (Long Form)
“You are past your start time for this job. Please check in as soon as possible. Lateness affects your reliability score.”

Client Approval Reminder
“Please review your cleaning photos so we can release payment.”

Dispute Opened
“A dispute has been submitted for this job. We’ll notify you once it’s reviewed.”

Payout Blocked
“Your payout is on hold due to account verification issues. Please complete your profile.”

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ PART 9: ANTI-SPAM LOGIC
Users should never feel overwhelmed.

Rules:

No more than 3 notifications per hour unless high-priority

No more than 7 per job cycle

Grouped notifications (example: 3 job reminders condensed into 1 push)

Silent background updates when appropriate

=========================================================

what logs get stored

how admin is alerted

These rules prevent system failures from becoming user frustration.

Perfect — continuing with SECTION 6E, one of the most important sections in product development:

Error States, Edge Cases & Fallback Rules
This section ensures:

the app never breaks

users always know what to do

failures are handled safely

operations continue even during unexpected issues

disputes don’t escalate due to confusion

payments don’t get stuck

check-in issues don’t destroy reliability unfairly

photo problems don’t ruin job quality

GPS failures don’t falsely penalize cleaners

This is the “what happens when things go wrong” master canon.

Let’s build it.

=========================================================
⭐ 6E — ERROR STATES, EDGE CASES & FALLBACK RULES (ULTRA-EXPANDED CANON)
=========================================================
PurTask’s product must handle every possible system failure, human mistake, device issue, or operational breakdown.

This section is divided into:

System Errors

Payment & Wallet Errors

GPS & Location Failures

Photo Upload Failures

Check-In / Check-Out Errors

Booking & Scheduling Errors

Job Flow Edge Cases

Dispute Flow Edge Cases

Cleaner Reliability Edge Cases

Payout Errors & Holds

Admin Override Conditions

Emergency & Safety Errors

Let’s go deep.

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ 1. SYSTEM ERRORS
1A. App Crash
If the app crashes:

state is saved locally

reopens to last known step

user sees:
“Something went wrong, but your progress is saved.”

1B. Server Unavailable
User sees:
“We’re experiencing a temporary issue. Please try again shortly.”
Retry button appears.

Jobs and payments never process during outages.

1C. Network Loss
Client screen:
“You’ve lost connection. We’ll retry automatically.”

Cleaner screen:
“Photos and GPS will upload once your connection returns.”

Offline mode caches:

GPS pings

photos

check-in attempts

checklist statuses

Uploads when connection restored.

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ 2. PAYMENT & WALLET ERRORS
2A. Credit Purchase Failure
UI shows:
“Payment failed. Your card was not charged.”

Retry options:

retry card

add new card

Apple/Google Pay

2B. Wallet Desync (rare)
If wallet amount doesn’t match ledger:

wallet locks

“We are verifying your wallet balance.”

admin receives alert

2C. Refund Failure
If refund cannot process:

credit refund queued

admin notified

client sees:
“We’re reviewing your refund. No action needed.”

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ 3. GPS & LOCATION FAILURES
This is a MAJOR edge case area.

3A. GPS Cannot Verify Location
Cleaner sees:
“GPS signal weak. Move closer to the home and try again.”

System gives cleaner:

2 retries

fallback “photo-based check-in”

3B. GPS Spoofing Suspected
Cleaner sees:
“We detected irregular GPS signals. Please retry.”

Admin alerted.

Cleaner cannot check in until GPS resolves or admin manually clears.

3C. No GPS Permission Granted
Cleaner sees mandatory modal:
“We need location access to verify your arrival.”

Button: “Enable Location Services”

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ 4. PHOTO UPLOAD ERRORS
4A. Upload Failure (Low Signal)
App shows:
“Upload failed. Retrying…”

If retries exceed limit:

cleaner can save locally

upload retried when signal returns

4B. Invalid File Format
Cleaner sees:
“Unsupported photo format. Please retake.”

4C. Blurry or Low-Light Detection
Cleaner sees:
“This photo is unclear. Please take a clearer shot.”

Cannot proceed until corrected.

4D. Duplicate Photo Detected
Cleaner sees:
“One or more photos appear to be reused. Please retake.”

Admin receives subtle risk flag.

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ 5. CHECK-IN / CHECK-OUT ERRORS
5A. Cannot Check In
System error checklist appears:

GPS

WiFi

device time sync

If still impossible:
Cleaner can submit manual check-in photo:

admin review required

reliability not penalized unless abuse detected

5B. Forgot to Check In
Cleaner attempts to upload before photos →
System blocks them:

“You must check in before uploading before photos.”

5C. Forgot to Check Out
Cleaner tries to submit after photos:
“You must check out before submitting.”

Check-out uses:

GPS

timestamp

If GPS fails → fallback local timestamp with risk flag.

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ 6. BOOKING & SCHEDULING ERRORS
6A. Cleaner Double-Booking
If cleaner accepts overlapping job:

system blocks acceptance

cleaner sees conflict modal

client sees “Assigning new cleaner…”

6B. No Cleaner Assigned
If job starts soon with no cleaner:

2 hours before job:

alert client

boost job visibility to cleaners

offer client option to reschedule

If no one accepts:

job cancels

client receives refund

admin notified

6C. Client Schedules Last-Minute
If scheduling within 1 hour:

surcharge (optional)

reduced cleaner availability

system warns client:
“Fewer cleaners available on short notice.”

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ 7. JOB FLOW EDGE CASES
7A. Cleaner Arrives Early
Cleaner cannot check in earlier than:

15 minutes before start

If early:
UI:
“You may check in 15 minutes before the scheduled time.”

7B. Cleaner Leaves Early
System calculates:

expected duration

actual duration

If significantly short:

reliability penalty

QA flag

admin validation

7C. Home Not As Described
Cleaner can report:

extra rooms

extreme mess

hazards

Admin options:

increase booking duration

cancel job

adjust payment

7D. Client Door/Access Code Wrong
Cleaner sees:
“Access issue. Please try alternate instructions or contact client.”

Client receives SMS if urgent.

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ 8. DISPUTE FLOW EDGE CASES
8A. Client Disputes After Approval
System blocks:
“You cannot dispute after approving a job.”

Only admin can override.

8B. Client Submits No Evidence
System prevents submission:
“We need at least one photo to proceed with the dispute.”

8C. Cleaner Responds Late
If dispute window expires:

cleaner loses by default

Cleaner UI shows:
“This dispute has closed. Please review the outcome.”

8D. Evidence Corrupted or Missing
If photos failed to upload during job:

system attempts to restore from local backup

if cannot → admin reviews and may ask cleaner to re-upload proof manually

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ 9. CLEANER RELIABILITY EDGE CASES
9A. Reliability Drop Due to System Error
If caused by:

GPS outage

server failure

validated bug
Admin can restore reliability with a log entry.

9B. Cleaner Cancels Due to Emergency
Cleaner selects:
“Emergency — no penalty”

Admin later verifies.

9C. Repeated Last-Minute Cancellations
System auto-flags:
“Your cancellation rate is too high. You may lose access to jobs.”

Admin reviews.

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ 10. PAYOUT ERRORS & HOLDS
10A. Payout Failed
Cleaner UI:
“Your payout failed. Please update your bank info.”

Admin sees reason:

invalid account

frozen Stripe account

fraud hold

10B. Identity Verification Fails
Cleaner sees:
“We couldn’t verify your identity. Please resubmit documents.”

During this time:

payouts paused

jobs allowed (optional setting)

10C. Negative Balance Logic
If dispute reversal causes negative earnings:

cleaner’s next payout reduced

cleaner notified transparently

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ 11. ADMIN OVERRIDE CONDITIONS
Admin can override only when:

system error occurred

evidence corrupted

GPS was unavailable but cleaner present

client incorrectly self-reported

bug affected check-in or photo upload

payout incorrectly withheld

Overrides require:

justification note

approval from senior admin for major changes

audit log entry

---------------------------------------------------------
⭐ 12. EMERGENCY & SAFETY ERRORS
12A. Unsafe Environment
Cleaner taps “Unsafe environment.”
System:

freezes job

alerts client

alerts admin

requests evidence

12B. Threat/Harassment
Cleaner taps:
“Client behavior unsafe.”

System:

stops job

pauses all communication

escalates to admin lead

protects cleaner identity (address hidden)

12C. Pet Aggression
Cleaner reports:
“Pet aggressive or loose.”

Client receives urgent message:
“Your cleaner feels unsafe due to an unrestrained pet.”

Admin may:

cancel job

require pet containment

Let’s begin with Marketplace Legal Structure.

=========================================================
⭐ 8A — MARKETPLACE LEGAL STRUCTURE & CLASSIFICATION
=========================================================
PureTask is legally a two-sided marketplace platform, not a cleaning company.

This distinction protects you from:

employment claims

liability for cleaner actions

wage/hour lawsuits

unionization issues

workers compensation requirements

1. Cleaners are Independent Contractors
They are NOT:

employees

agents

franchisees

partners

representatives

They control:

their schedule

their tools

their earnings timing

their jobs accepted

their routes and methods

PureTask provides:

job opportunities

escrow & payout system

dispute resolution

communication tools

reliability scoring

optional training

This model mirrors:

Uber

DoorDash

TaskRabbit

Thumbtack

⭐ 2. PureTask is Not a Cleaning Company
Platform explicitly states:

does not provide cleaning services

does not employ cleaners

is not responsible for work performed

is not liable for property condition before or after a job

is not responsible for damage caused by cleaners

PureTask:

connects clients and cleaners

facilitates secure payments

provides safety & verification tools

enforces marketplace standards

⭐ 3. Required Legal Statements
PureTask must explicitly display:
“PureTask is a marketplace platform. Cleaners listed on the platform are independent contractors, not employees.”

“PureTask does not control or direct cleaners in their work.”

“PureTask is not responsible for the quality of services performed by cleaners.”

These phrases appear in:

Terms of Service

Cleaner Agreement

Client Agreement

App onboarding

Website footer

=========================================================
⭐ 8B — CLIENT TERMS OF SERVICE (SUMMARY + FULL POLICY CANON)
=========================================================
The Client TOS governs:

bookings

cancellations

disputes

refunds

conduct

payments

limitations

Let’s break it down.

⭐ 1. Client Eligibility Requirements
Clients must:

be 18+

register with real name

provide accurate home details

maintain safe, sanitary environment

provide safe access (keys, codes, etc.)

Providing false information = account ban.

⭐ 2. Payment & Credits Terms
Clients agree that:
credits are non-transferable

credits are refundable only according to policy

credits cannot be exchanged for cash

credits represent prepaid balance

escrow protects both parties

payment releases only after approval

⭐ 3. Booking & Cancellation Terms
Client Cancellation Rules:
cancel before cutoff → full refund

cancel after cutoff → late cancellation fee

cancel during active job → credits partially forfeited

Cleaner Cancellation:
client gets full refund

PureTask attempts reassigning

PureTask not liable for inconvenience

⭐ 4. Approval & Dispute Terms
Approval Rules:
approval = final

after approval, no disputes allowed

Dispute Rules:
Client must:

submit within the dispute window

provide photo/video evidence

describe the issue clearly

PureTask may:

award refund

award partial refund

deny refund

Decision is final.

⭐ 5. Client Conduct Rules
Clients may not:

threaten cleaners

harass cleaners

make discriminatory comments

request illegal services

provide unsafe environment

allow aggressive pets freely

falsely report issues

Violations → account ban.

⭐ 6. Limitations of Liability
Client agrees PureTask is not responsible for:

cleaner performance

damage caused by cleaner

lost or stolen items

dissatisfaction with results

scheduling conflicts

travel delays

uncontrollable events

This protects you legally.

=========================================================
⭐ 8C — CLEANER AGREEMENT (INDEPENDENT CONTRACTOR TERMS)
=========================================================
The cleaner agreement is arguably the MOST important legal document.

⭐ 1. Cleaners Confirm They Are Independent Contractors
They:

choose when to work

choose which jobs to accept

provide their own tools

pay their own taxes

are not entitled to benefits

must maintain proper business licensing (if required)

⭐ 2. Cleaner Operational Requirements
They must:

arrive on time

check in via GPS

upload required photos

complete tasks with professionalism

follow instructions

maintain safe behavior

avoid theft or misconduct

⭐ 3. Payment Terms
Cleaners agree that:

earnings depend on job approval

earnings may be reduced due to disputes

earnings may be adjusted for penalties or fraud

payouts come through Stripe

payouts may be held for verification

negative balances may be recovered from future payouts

⭐ 4. Cleaner Conduct Rules
Cleaners cannot:

enter home without permission

take items

behave unprofessionally

smoke, vape, or drink on the property

act violently or inappropriately

falsify photos

manipulate GPS

ask for off-platform payment

bring unauthorized individuals

⭐ 5. Insurance & Liability
PureTask strongly recommends cleaners carry:

general liability insurance

bonding

Cleaners are responsible for:

property damage they cause

injuries they cause

incidents resulting from negligence

⭐ 6. Account Suspension / Removal
PureTask may suspend cleaner for:

poor reliability

low quality

disputes

misconduct

safety incidents

fraud indicators

violating platform rules

=========================================================
⭐ 8D — REFUND, CANCELLATION & DISPUTE POLICIES
=========================================================
These policies must be extremely clear to protect all parties.

⭐ 1. Refund Policy
Full Refund
Given when:

cleaner no-shows

client cancels early

unsafe environment prevents work (client fault)

major service failure proven

Partial Refund
Given when:

some tasks incomplete

photos show partial work

cleaner left early

client provided insufficient time

No Refund
When:

client provides no evidence

issue is preference-based

job was approved

dispute submitted too late

⭐ 2. Dispute Resolution Policy
PureTask resolves disputes based on:

before/after photos

GPS data

checklist completion

client evidence

cleaner response

past reliability patterns

Admin decision is:

final

binding

non-negotiable

⭐ 3. Cancellation Policy
Cleaner Cancellation:
clients refunded in full

repeated cleaner cancellations → penalties

Client Cancellation:
within allowed time → full refund

outside time → partial refund

mid-clean cancellation → partial refund

⭐ 9E — DISPUTE RESOLUTION HANDBOOK (FULL CANON)
=========================================================
This defines EXACTLY how disputes are handled.

⭐ Dispute Categories
Missed Areas

Incomplete Tasks

Poor Quality

Incorrect Instructions Followed

Cleaner Left Early

Damage

Property Condition Misrepresentation

Fraud Attempt (client or cleaner)

⭐ Refund Guidelines (Internal Only)
Full Refund
cleaner did almost nothing

photos clearly show no improvement

cleaner left extremely early

unsafe/unprofessional behavior

Partial Refund
Based on the percentage completed:

20–40% missing tasks

40–60% missing tasks

60–80% missing tasks

No Refund
good before/after

client preference complaint

insufficient evidence

dispute filed too late

cleaner followed instructions

⭐ Dispute Decision Template
Admins must follow this structure:

1. Summary
2. Evidence from cleaner (photos + timeline)
3. Evidence from client
4. Findings
5. Decision
6. Refund amount (if any)
7. Reliability & QA implications

⭐ 10A — LAUNCH OBJECTIVES & SUCCESS CRITERIA
=========================================================
PureTask’s launch goal is NOT to scale instantly — it’s to:

validate the system

stress test the flows

optimize quality

refine training & automations

achieve marketplace balance (supply <-> demand)

We define success thresholds for the first 90 days.

⭐ Launch Objective #1: Operational Stability
What this means:

cleaners understand flows

GPS + photos behave correctly

disputes resolved in < 24 hours

no payout errors

admin team comfortable using dashboard

Success Metric:
≥ 95% jobs run without manual admin intervention.

⭐ Launch Objective #2: Quality Consistency
low dispute rate

predictable job durations

minimal cancellations

Success Metric:
Dispute rate ≤ 5%
Cleaner cancellation rate ≤ 8%
Client cancellation rate ≤ 10%

⭐ Launch Objective #3: Positive Early User Sentiment
high NPS

strong reviews

repeat bookings

Success Metric:
Client NPS ≥ 45
Repeat booking rate ≥ 30% by month 2

⭐ Launch Objective #4: Marketplace Balance
A stable ratio of:

Active clients : Active cleaners = 10 : 1

(where each cleaner can handle 8–12 jobs/week)

⭐ Launch Objective #5: Unit Economics Validation
PureTask must hit:

efficient paid acquisition

strong organic referral strength

Success Metric:
CAC < $35
LTV > $200
LTV/CAC ≥ 4.0

=========================================================
⭐ 11B — PURETASK GLOSSARY (DEFINITIONS OF EVERY TERM IN THE PLATFORM)
=========================================================
This glossary ensures internal alignment and removes ambiguity across departments.

⭐ Core Platform Terms
Credits
The internal currency used for client payments and cleaner earnings. Non-transferable.

Escrow
Where credits sit until the client approves the cleaning.

Approval
The client’s confirmation of work after reviewing photos. Releases escrow to the cleaner.

Auto-Approval
The automated approval after a defined time window if the client does nothing.

Check-In
GPS-verified arrival of cleaner at client home.

Check-Out
Cleaner signals the cleaning is complete before uploading after photos.

⭐ Cleaner Performance Terms
Reliability Score
Measurement of cleaner dependability (lateness, cancellations, check-in errors).

QA Score
Quality average based on photo verification, dispute outcomes, and job completion.

Cleaner Tier
Tier 1–5 ranking determining visibility, pay multipliers, and job priority.

Probation Period
Cleaner’s first 5 jobs, monitored more closely.

⭐ Operational Terms
P1 Issue
High-severity issue requiring immediate support action.

Dispute Case Packet
The bundle of all photos, logs, evidence used in dispute resolution.

Risk Flag
Automated detection of suspicious activity (GPS or photo anomalies).

Override
Admin manually changes system-calculated value (rare).

⭐ Financial Terms
Payout Balance
Credits earned and awaiting transfer.

Instant Pay
Cleaner requests immediate payout with fee.

Chargeback
Client disputes credit purchase with bank. Sends risk flag.

⭐ Fraud Terms
Photo Fraud
Using reused, AI-generated, or irrelevant photos.

GPS Spoofing
Fake or manipulated location signals.

Duplicate Account
Client or cleaner operating multiple profiles.

⭐ Marketing Terms
CAC
Cost to acquire one client.

LTV
Lifetime value of a client.

Conversion Rate
% of visitors who make a booking.

⭐ 11C — ROLE-BASED PERMISSIONS MATRIX
=========================================================
Defines WHO can do WHAT.

⭐ Client
book jobs

cancel jobs

approve jobs

submit disputes

update personal/home info

Cannot:

edit cleaner profiles

override dispute decisions

request off-platform payments

⭐ Cleaner
accept jobs

check in / check out

submit photos

request payouts

Cannot:

modify dispute outcomes

see other cleaners’ data

change pay rates

⭐ Support Agent (Tier 1)
Can:

reply to tickets

adjust minor credits (< $10)

escalate issues

assist with access issues

Cannot:

issue refunds > $10

resolve disputes

⭐ Dispute Specialist (Tier 2)
Can:

view all evidence

issue partial refunds

issue full refunds

adjust reliability

log dispute decisions

Cannot:

override fraud holds

modify payouts directly

⭐ Risk Analyst
Can:

freeze payouts

freeze accounts

investigate fraud patterns

request ID verification

Cannot:

issue refunds unrelated to fraud

⭐ Operations Lead
Can:

override any admin decision

approve major payout releases

issue high-value refunds

ban accounts

⭐ Engineering Admin
Can:

access automations

view logs

change system rules

modify roles

update product settings

⭐ 11E — DATA FLOW OVERVIEW (CREDITS, PAYOUTS, JOBS, LOGS)
=========================================================
⭐ CREDIT FLOW (Client → Escrow → Cleaner)
Client purchases credits

Credits stored in wallet

Credits moved to escrow at booking

Cleaner completes job

Client approves

Credits released

Credits added to cleaner earnings

Cleaner requests payout or waits for weekly payout

⭐ PAYOUT FLOW (Cleaner Earnings → Bank Account)
Cleaner earnings accumulate

Weekly payout or Instant Pay initiation

Stripe verifies ID & bank info

Stripe transfers funds

Payout record stored in ledger

Notifications sent

If failed → payout hold + alert

⭐ JOB FLOW
Client creates booking

Escrow reserves credits

Cleaner accepts

Cleaner checks in

Cleaner takes before photos

Cleaning

Cleaner takes after photos

Job submitted

Client approves or disputes

Escrow releases

⭐ LOGS FLOW
Every action is logged:

timestamp

user

metadata

device

location

type

Logs feed:

the audit system

dispute engine

fraud engine

You’re 100% right to flag this — and you’re also right that several things we documented would put PureTask at real legal risk under independent contractor (IC) law, especially in the U.S. (IRS test, ABC test, Prop 22–style scrutiny, and Stripe/1099 compliance).

What you’re asking for now is the correct next step:
a legal consistency audit of the PureTask canon.

Below is a clear, honest review of where the contradictions are, why they’re risky, and exactly how to fix them while keeping PureTask operationally strong.

I’m going to do this in a very structured way so you can later rewrite the Master Manual cleanly.

BIG PICTURE (IMPORTANT)
PureTask currently mixes two conflicting models:

A true independent contractor marketplace (Uber / TaskRabbit side)

A managed workforce / quality-enforced operator (employee-like control)

⚠️ You can’t mix these without risk.

The law doesn’t care what you call cleaners — it cares about:

control

supervision

enforcement

penalties

training requirements

performance management

economic dependence

Right now, several systems imply employer-like control.

PART 1 — THE LEGAL STANDARD YOU MUST PASS (SIMPLIFIED)
1. IRS Common Law Test (Control Test)
You must NOT control:

HOW work is done

WHEN work is done

WHAT tools are used

DETAILED methods of performance

You CAN control:

marketplace rules

safety requirements

payment processing

fraud prevention

access to platform

2. ABC Test (California / High-Risk States)
To classify as IC, ALL 3 must be true:

A. Worker is free from control and direction
B. Work is outside your usual course of business
C. Worker is customarily engaged in an independent trade

Your biggest risk is A and B.

3. What Courts Look For (Reality Check)
Courts look at:

practical reality

enforcement behavior

penalties

how often you intervene

whether workers feel “managed”

PART 2 — MAJOR CONTRADICTIONS IN PURETASK (CRITICAL)
Below are specific contradictions in your current documentation.

❌ ISSUE 1: Mandatory Training That Teaches “How to Clean”
Where it appears
Cleaner Academy modules

Cleaning standards training

Required quizzes

“Must pass to work” language

Why this is dangerous
Mandatory training that teaches how to do the work is classic employee control.

Training is allowed ONLY if:

framed as optional

framed as best practices

framed as marketplace education

NOT required to perform tasks in a specific way

Legal risk level
🔴 HIGH

✅ How to fix it (REQUIRED)
Change language everywhere to:

“Optional marketplace education”

“Suggested best practices”

“Community guidelines”

“Information to help you succeed”

Cleaners must self-certify competence.

You can still:

require safety training

require fraud-prevention rules

require photo verification rules

You CANNOT:

require exact cleaning methods

enforce technique-specific steps

❌ ISSUE 2: Reliability Score = Behavioral Control
Where it appears
Reliability penalties

Lateness penalties

Cancellation penalties

“If below X%, lose access to jobs”

Why this is dangerous
This looks like performance discipline, especially when:

penalties are automatic

tied to attendance

tied to timing

tied to availability

Courts view this as employer scheduling control.

Legal risk level
🔴 HIGH

✅ How to fix it
Reframe reliability as:

a marketplace ranking signal

NOT a punishment system

NOT a disciplinary system

Key changes:

No language of “penalty”

No “must maintain X%”

Use “marketplace visibility may be reduced”

Example rewrite:
“Cleaners with higher reliability scores are shown to clients more often.”

NOT:
“You will lose access to jobs.”

❌ ISSUE 3: Tier Promotions/Demotions Managed by Admins
Where it appears
Admin promotion/demotion authority

Probation

Coaching

Performance improvement

Mandatory retraining

Why this is dangerous
This looks like:

performance reviews

managerial hierarchy

employee progression system

Legal risk level
🔴 VERY HIGH

✅ How to fix it
Tiers must be:

algorithmic

non-negotiable

non-managerial

marketplace-based

Admins should NOT:

“coach”

“promote”

“demote”

Instead:

system auto-calculates tiers

admins only resolve disputes/fraud

no subjective evaluations

❌ ISSUE 4: Admin Overrides of Cleaner Earnings
Where it appears
manual payout adjustments

penalties

clawbacks

“negative balances”

Why this is dangerous
Employers adjust wages.
Marketplaces do not.

This is especially dangerous if:

frequent

discretionary

punitive

Legal risk level
🔴 HIGH

✅ How to fix it
Earnings changes must ONLY happen due to:

client disputes

fraud

payment failures

Admins must not:

“penalize”

“dock pay”

“fine”

Language must say:
“Earnings adjusted based on dispute outcome.”

❌ ISSUE 5: Mandatory Schedules / Availability Expectations
Where it appears
required check-in times

lateness consequences

“job starts at X, must arrive by X”

Why this is dangerous
Time control = employment signal.

You can require:

agreed-upon service window

You cannot:

discipline lateness like an employer

require availability blocks

Legal risk level
🔴 MEDIUM–HIGH

✅ How to fix it
Frame time as:

client expectation

not platform enforcement

Example:
“Clients may rate reliability based on arrival time.”

NOT:
“Late arrival results in penalties.”

❌ ISSUE 6: Safety + Conduct Rules Overreach
Where it appears
zero-tolerance rules

mandatory behaviors inside the home

how cleaners must interact

Why this is dangerous
Behavioral control inside the job is scrutinized.

Legal risk level
🟠 MEDIUM

✅ How to fix it
You can enforce:

safety

legality

platform integrity

You must avoid:

etiquette rules

“professional behavior” language

micro-conduct rules

Rewrite as:
“Violations of safety or law result in removal from marketplace.”

SECTION 1 — WHAT PURETASK ACTUALLY IS (AFTER RECONCILIATION)

After reviewing all materials, PureTask is best described as:

A two-sided service marketplace platform that facilitates discovery, booking, payment, and dispute resolution between clients and independent cleaning providers, using evidence-based verification (photos, timestamps, GPS metadata) to reduce disputes and fraud.

What PureTask ACTUALLY does in practice:

Facilitates booking and payment using a prepaid credit system

Holds funds in escrow until client action or timeout

Provides tools for cleaners to submit proof of work

Provides tools for clients to review proof

Resolves disputes using evidence, not preference

Uses algorithms to rank and surface providers

Moderates access to the platform for safety, fraud, and integrity reasons

Does NOT directly perform cleaning services

Key intent signal (important):
PureTask’s core value is not “managing cleaners,” but “removing subjectivity from service verification.”

That intent is GOOD and defensible.

However, multiple systems unintentionally drifted into managed workforce behavior.

SECTION 2 — WHAT IS ALREADY IC-SAFE (DO NOT CHANGE)

2.1 Credit + Escrow System

Clients prepay credits

Credits sit in escrow

Release is triggered by client action or timeout

This mirrors Uber, Upwork, Airbnb

IC-safe

2.2 Evidence-Based Disputes

Decisions based on photos, timestamps, GPS metadata

Neutral arbitration

No “quality opinions” by admins

IC-safe when framed as platform arbitration

2.3 Fraud Prevention Systems

GPS anomaly detection

Payment fraud detection

IC-safe (platform integrity)

2.4 Client-Driven Outcomes

Client approval releases funds

IC-safe

Cleaners choose which jobs to accept

No exclusivity

IC-safe

Bans for fraud, safety, illegal behavior

IC-safe if framed as marketplace protection

SECTION 3 — BORDERLINE AREAS (LANGUAGE + STRUCTURE CONFLICTS)

3.4 Admin Overrides
Problem:

Language implies performance management

Mentions coaching, adjustments, penalties

Reality:

Admins mostly resolve disputes and fraud

Fix path:

Strip subjective authority

Limit to access moderation and arbitration

SECTION 4 — STRUCTURALLY UNSAFE ELEMENTS (MUST CHANGE)

These are the highest legal risk areas. They cannot be fixed with wording alone — they require structural reframing.

4.1 Mandatory Training on Work Methods
This is a classic employee signal.

Why unsafe:

Controls how work is performed

Required to access earnings

Required change:

Remove mandatory technique training

Only require agreement to marketplace rules, safety, and evidence submission

4.2 Probation / Coaching / Performance Improvement
These concepts are incompatible with IC classification.

Why unsafe:

Implies supervision

Implies employer correction

Required change:

Remove entirely

Replace with algorithmic visibility limits and client choice

4.3 Penalties Framed as Punishment
Any automatic deduction or “penalty” not directly tied to a dispute outcome is dangerous.

Why unsafe:

Looks like wage control

Required change:

Earnings only change due to:

client disputes

fraud

payment reversals

4.4 Admin-Controlled Promotions/Demotions
Admins deciding who “advances” is an employment signal.

Required change:

Admins cannot influence ranking outcomes

Only systems and client behavior can

4.5 Scheduling Enforcement
Anything that feels like attendance discipline is dangerous.

Required change:

Arrival time framed as client expectation, not platform enforcement

No instruction on how to clean

No performance discipline

No coaching

No probation

No penalties unrelated to disputes or fraud
