PHASE 1 — PURETASK IC-SAFE FOUNDATION REWRITE
CANONICAL VERSION

SECTION 1 — WHAT PURETASK IS

PureTask is a technology marketplace that connects clients with independent service providers offering cleaning services.

PureTask provides:

a digital platform for discovery and booking

payment facilitation through a prepaid credit system

escrow services to hold client funds until job completion

tools for sharing and reviewing job-related evidence

neutral dispute resolution based on objective information

automated systems that organize and present marketplace data

PureTask does not:

provide cleaning services

employ service providers

supervise or direct how services are performed

control the methods, techniques, or tools used by providers

guarantee service outcomes

All cleaning services are performed by independent service providers operating their own businesses.

SECTION 2 — RELATIONSHIP TO CLEANERS (INDEPENDENT CONTRACTOR MODEL)

Cleaners using PureTask are independent contractors and independent business operators.

Each cleaner:

operates an independent cleaning business

chooses which jobs to accept or decline

determines how services are performed

supplies their own tools and materials

controls their own schedule and availability

may use other platforms or accept off-platform work

is responsible for their own taxes, insurance, and licenses

PureTask does not require:

minimum working hours

exclusive use of the platform

acceptance of any job

specific cleaning techniques or workflows

PureTask’s role is limited to facilitating marketplace transactions and maintaining platform integrity.

SECTION 3 — PLATFORM RULES VS WORK CONTROL (CRITICAL DISTINCTION)

PureTask enforces platform rules, not work methods.

Platform rules exist to:

protect clients and providers

prevent fraud

ensure accurate payments

maintain trust in the marketplace

Platform rules may govern:

how jobs are booked and paid

how proof of work is submitted

how disputes are resolved

how safety issues are reported

how fraudulent behavior is handled

Platform rules do NOT govern:

how cleaning is performed

how long a provider must work

what techniques are used

how tasks are prioritized inside the home

This distinction is fundamental and applies across all systems.

SECTION 4 — ADMIN ROLE (REWRITTEN, IC-SAFE)

Admins do not manage cleaners.

Admins do not:

train cleaners on how to clean

coach cleaners

discipline cleaners

evaluate performance subjectively

promote or demote cleaners

instruct cleaners on service execution

Admins only:

operate the platform’s technical systems

facilitate neutral dispute resolution

moderate platform access for safety, fraud, or legality

respond to support requests

maintain accurate records and logs

enforce platform integrity rules

Admins act as marketplace moderators and arbitrators, not supervisors.

SECTION 5 — MARKETPLACE VISIBILITY & RANKING (REDEFINED)

PureTask uses automated systems to organize and display service providers to clients.

Visibility within the marketplace may vary based on:

completed transaction history

client actions (approvals, disputes)

objective job data

availability information provided by the cleaner

platform usage patterns

Visibility is:

algorithmic

non-guaranteed

non-contractual

not a form of discipline

not a promise of future work

PureTask does not guarantee job volume, earnings, or ranking position.

SECTION 6 — RELIABILITY (IC-SAFE DEFINITION)

Reliability is a descriptive marketplace signal derived from historical platform data.

Reliability:

reflects completed transactions and timestamps

is calculated automatically

helps clients make informed choices

is not a performance mandate

is not a penalty system

A lower reliability score does not punish a cleaner.
It may influence how often a cleaner appears in client search results.

No minimum reliability score is required to remain an independent contractor.

SECTION 7 — TIERS (REWRITTEN AS NEUTRAL GROUPINGS)

Tiers are algorithmic groupings created to help clients browse providers.

Tiers:

are calculated automatically

are based on neutral marketplace data

are not career levels

are not promotions or demotions

carry no employment implications

Admins cannot manually adjust tiers except to correct system errors or fraud.

SECTION 8 — EDUCATION & RESOURCES (FORMERLY “TRAINING”)

PureTask may provide optional educational resources intended to help independent providers understand how the platform works.

These resources may include:

how to use the app

how payments and escrow function

how disputes are evaluated

how to submit clear proof of work

general marketplace best practices

Educational resources are:

optional

non-mandatory

non-certifying

not instructions on how to clean

The only required acknowledgements are:

agreement to platform terms

agreement to safety and legality rules

agreement to evidence submission requirements

SECTION 9 — EARNINGS & ADJUSTMENTS (IC-SAFE)

Cleaners earn credits only from completed, approved transactions.

Earnings may change only due to:

client disputes resolved through arbitration

fraud or chargebacks

payment reversals or errors

Admins cannot:

fine cleaners

dock pay for behavior

apply penalties unrelated to disputes or fraud

All earnings adjustments are evidence-based and documented.

SECTION 10 — SAFETY & PLATFORM INTEGRITY

PureTask enforces zero-tolerance rules for:

fraud

theft

violence

harassment

illegal activity

safety threats

Enforcement actions are based on:

platform integrity

legal obligations

safety concerns

Such actions affect platform access, not employment status.

common marketplace misunderstandings

client communication best practices

is optional

is non-mandatory

does not certify competence

does not instruct cleaning methods

which jobs they accept

is calculated automatically

Tiers:

are generated automatically

are based on objective marketplace data

are not promotions or demotions

do not represent employment levels

do not imply seniority or rank within PureTask

SECTION 2.6 — JOB EVIDENCE & PHOTO SUBMISSION (SAFE CONTROL)

Cleaners are required to submit:

arrival confirmation

before-service photos

after-service photos

Evidence requirements exist to:

verify job completion

reduce disputes

protect both parties

support neutral arbitration

Evidence requirements do NOT dictate how cleaning is performed.

SECTION 2.7 — DISPUTE RESOLUTION SYSTEM (NEUTRAL ARBITRATION)

PureTask operates a neutral dispute resolution process.

Disputes are evaluated using:

submitted photos

timestamps

job details

client and provider statements

historical transaction data

Disputes are resolved based on evidence, not subjective quality opinions.

Admins act as neutral arbitrators.

Dispute outcomes may result in:

full release of escrow

partial refund to client

full refund to client

Dispute outcomes are final and documented.

SECTION 2.8 — EARNINGS, ESCROW & PAYOUTS (IC-SAFE)

Cleaners earn credits only from approved transactions.

Credits move through the system as follows:

Client prepays credits

Credits are held in escrow

Escrow releases upon approval or timeout

Credits become cleaner earnings

Cleaner requests payout or receives scheduled payout

Earnings adjustments occur only due to:

dispute resolution

fraud investigation

chargebacks

payment reversals

PureTask does not fine, penalize, or dock pay for performance.

SECTION 2.9 — ADMIN SOPs (MODERATION ONLY)

Admins do not supervise providers.

Admins do:

resolve disputes

investigate fraud

moderate platform access

respond to support requests

maintain logs and records

correct technical errors

Admins do not:

coach providers

give performance feedback

issue warnings for work quality

require retraining

influence provider rankings subjectively

All admin actions must be evidence-based and documented.

SECTION 2.10 — SAFETY & PLATFORM INTEGRITY

PureTask enforces platform integrity rules to protect users.

Platform integrity rules address:

fraud

theft

harassment

violence

illegal activity

safety threats

Violations may result in:

temporary account restriction

permanent removal from the platform

reporting to authorities where required

These actions relate to platform access, not employment.

SECTION 2.11 — AUTOMATIONS (IC-SAFE FRAMING)

Automations operate neutrally and consistently.

Automations may:

release escrow

trigger reminders

flag anomalies

freeze accounts during investigations

process payouts

notify users of status changes

Automations do not:

evaluate performance subjectively

discipline providers

manage behavior

enforce work methods

All automated actions are rule-based and auditable.

SECTION 2.12 — CLIENT APP LANGUAGE (SAFE COPY PRINCIPLES)

Client-facing language must:

describe cleaners as independent providers

avoid “our cleaners” phrasing

avoid guarantees of quality

emphasize client choice

emphasize evidence review

Example language:
“Choose from independent cleaning providers available in your area.”

SECTION 2.13 — CLEANER APP LANGUAGE (SAFE COPY PRINCIPLES)

Cleaner-facing language must:

avoid employer tone

avoid commands about how to work

emphasize independence

emphasize optionality

BATCH 1

SECTION 1 — EXECUTIVE SUMMARY (IC-SAFE)

PureTask is a two-sided technology marketplace that connects clients with independent cleaning service providers.

PureTask’s role is to:

facilitate discovery and booking

process payments using a prepaid credit system

hold funds in escrow until job completion

provide tools for sharing and reviewing job evidence

resolve disputes using objective information

maintain marketplace integrity and safety

PureTask does not provide cleaning services, does not employ cleaners, and does not control how services are performed.

All cleaning services are performed by independent providers operating their own businesses.

PureTask exists to reduce friction, reduce disputes, and increase trust in home services through transparency and automation.

SECTION 2 — BUSINESS MODEL OVERVIEW

PureTask operates as a neutral marketplace.

Clients:

purchase credits

use credits to book services

review evidence after service completion

approve or dispute based on objective information

Cleaners:

operate independently

choose which jobs to accept

submit proof of completed work

earn credits upon approval

withdraw earnings through the platform

PureTask earns revenue through:

platform service fees

optional expedited payout fees

optional premium marketplace features (future)

PureTask does not guarantee:

job availability

earnings

service outcomes

SECTION 3 — CORE MARKETPLACE PRINCIPLES

PureTask is built on the following principles:

Independence
Service providers control how they work.

Transparency
Evidence replaces subjectivity.

Neutrality
PureTask does not favor providers or clients.

Client Choice
Clients decide whether work is acceptable.

Automation
Systems operate consistently and without bias.

Platform Integrity
Fraud, safety issues, and illegal activity are not tolerated.

SECTION 4 — USER ROLES

There are three primary user roles.

Clients:

request services

provide access instructions

review evidence

approve or dispute work

Cleaners:

independent service providers

accept or decline jobs freely

submit evidence of completed work

manage their own business operations

Admins:

operate platform systems

resolve disputes neutrally

moderate platform access

investigate fraud and safety issues

Admins do not supervise or manage cleaners.

SECTION 5 — CLIENT EXPERIENCE (IC-SAFE)

Client Flow:

Create an account

Purchase credits

Enter home details and service request

Submit booking

Cleaner accepts job

Cleaner submits before evidence

Service occurs

Cleaner submits after evidence

Client reviews evidence

Client approves or disputes

Clients are responsible for:

accurate home descriptions

safe access

clear instructions

timely review of evidence

Client approval triggers escrow release.

SECTION 6 — CLEANER EXPERIENCE (IC-SAFE)

Cleaners use PureTask as a marketplace tool.

Cleaners:

choose which jobs to accept

decide how to perform services

supply their own tools

manage their own schedules

may work on or off the platform freely

Cleaners are responsible for:

submitting required evidence

complying with safety and legality rules

managing their own taxes and insurance

PureTask does not supervise service execution.

SECTION 7 — ONBOARDING & ACCESS (IC-SAFE)

Onboarding is an access process, not training.

Required steps:

identity verification

payment setup

acceptance of platform terms

acknowledgment of evidence requirements

acknowledgment of safety rules

Onboarding does not certify skills or competence.

Optional educational resources are available but not required.

SECTION 8 — JOB LIFECYCLE

Booking created

Credits placed in escrow

Cleaner accepts job

Arrival confirmation

Before evidence submitted

Service performed

After evidence submitted

Client review window

Approval, dispute, or auto-approval

Escrow resolution

Each stage is logged and time-stamped.

SECTION 9 — EVIDENCE SYSTEM

Evidence is required to:

verify job completion

protect both parties

support dispute resolution

Evidence includes:

photos

timestamps

location metadata

Evidence requirements do not dictate how work is performed.

SECTION 10 — CREDIT & ESCROW SYSTEM

Credits are a prepaid internal currency.

Flow:

client purchases credits

credits held in wallet

credits moved to escrow at booking

credits released upon approval or timeout

credits convert to cleaner earnings

Credits:

are non-transferable

cannot be exchanged for cash by clients

represent prepaid services

SECTION 11 — EARNINGS & PAYOUTS (IC-SAFE)

Cleaners earn credits only from approved transactions.

Payout options:

scheduled payouts

optional instant payouts (fee-based)

Earnings change only due to:

dispute outcomes

fraud

payment reversals

PureTask does not impose fines or performance penalties.

SECTION 12 — MARKETPLACE VISIBILITY, RELIABILITY & RANKING

PureTask organizes the marketplace using automated, neutral ranking systems.

Marketplace visibility:

determines how frequently a provider is shown to clients

is not guaranteed

is non-contractual

is not a form of discipline or supervision

Visibility may be influenced by:

completed transactions

historical dispute outcomes

responsiveness to bookings

availability information provided by the provider

client interactions with listings

PureTask does not promise any level of exposure, bookings, or income.

SECTION 13 — RELIABILITY (DESCRIPTIVE SIGNAL ONLY)

Reliability is a descriptive signal derived from historical platform data.

Reliability reflects:

completed jobs

cancellations

timing metadata

dispute outcomes

Reliability:

is calculated automatically

is not manually enforced

has no required minimum

does not restrict a provider’s independent business

does not constitute discipline

Lower reliability may result in reduced marketplace visibility.

Reliability does not affect a provider’s ability to operate independently outside the platform.

SECTION 14 — TIERS (ALGORITHMIC GROUPINGS)

Tiers are algorithmic groupings used to help clients browse providers.

Tiers:

are calculated automatically

are based on objective marketplace data

do not represent employment levels

are not promotions or demotions

do not imply seniority, rank, or job security

Tier placement:

carries no contractual rights

carries no guaranteed benefits

may change automatically as data changes

Admins cannot subjectively modify tier placement.

SECTION 15 — DISPUTE RESOLUTION & ARBITRATION

PureTask provides a neutral dispute resolution process.

Disputes may be submitted by clients within a defined review window.

Disputes are evaluated using:

submitted evidence

timestamps

location metadata

job details

client and provider statements

historical transaction data

Disputes are resolved based on evidence, not subjective quality opinions.

Possible outcomes:

full release of escrow to provider

partial refund to client

full refund to client

Dispute outcomes are final and documented.

SECTION 16 — AUTO-APPROVAL SYSTEM

If a client takes no action within the review window:

the job is automatically approved

escrow is released to the provider

Auto-approval:

prevents indefinite withholding of funds

is neutral and time-based

applies equally to all providers

SECTION 17 — SAFETY & PLATFORM INTEGRITY

PureTask enforces platform integrity rules to protect users and the marketplace.

Platform integrity rules address:

fraud

theft

harassment

violence

illegal activity

safety threats

Enforcement actions may include:

temporary account restriction

permanent platform removal

reporting to authorities when required

These actions relate solely to platform access.

They do not create or imply an employment relationship.

SECTION 18 — FRAUD PREVENTION SYSTEMS

PureTask uses automated and manual systems to detect fraud.

Fraud signals may include:

inconsistent evidence

repeated dispute abuse

payment anomalies

identity irregularities

location anomalies

Fraud investigations may result in:

payout holds

account restrictions

permanent removal

All actions are evidence-based and documented.

SECTION 19 — ADMIN OPERATIONS (IC-SAFE)

Admins operate as marketplace moderators.

Admins may:

resolve disputes

investigate fraud

moderate platform access

correct system errors

respond to support requests

Admins may not:

instruct providers how to work

evaluate service quality subjectively

coach or retrain providers

impose penalties unrelated to disputes or fraud

Admin actions are logged and auditable.

SECTION 20 — SUPPORT SYSTEM

Support exists to:

assist users with platform issues

explain platform processes

route disputes and safety concerns

provide technical assistance

Support does not:

evaluate service quality

manage providers

enforce work behavior

SECTION 21 — AUTOMATION SYSTEMS

PureTask uses automations to ensure consistency.

Automations may:

move credits

release escrow

trigger notifications

flag anomalies

freeze accounts during investigations

process payouts

Automations operate:

neutrally

consistently

without subjective judgment

Automations do not manage or supervise providers.

INDEPENDENT SERVICE PROVIDER AGREEMENT
PURETASK

Effective Date: [Insert Date]

This Independent Service Provider Agreement (“Agreement”) is entered into between PureTask, Inc. (“PureTask,” “we,” “us,” or “our”) and the individual or entity accepting this Agreement (“Service Provider,” “you,” or “your”).

By creating an account, accessing the PureTask platform, or accepting any job through the platform, you agree to be bound by this Agreement.

PURPOSE OF THE PLATFORM

PureTask is a technology marketplace that connects clients with independent service providers who offer cleaning services.

PureTask does not provide cleaning services and does not employ service providers. PureTask’s role is limited to facilitating bookings, processing payments through a prepaid credit and escrow system, providing tools for sharing job-related evidence, and resolving disputes using objective information.

All services are performed independently by Service Providers operating their own businesses.

INDEPENDENT CONTRACTOR RELATIONSHIP

You acknowledge and agree that:

You are an independent contractor and not an employee, agent, partner, or representative of PureTask.

You operate an independent business and use the PureTask platform as a marketplace tool.

Nothing in this Agreement creates an employment relationship, joint venture, partnership, or agency relationship.

PureTask does not:

supervise or direct how services are performed

control your methods, techniques, or tools

require you to accept any job

require minimum hours or availability

restrict you from working on or off the platform

You are solely responsible for how you perform services.

CONTROL OVER SERVICES

You retain full control over:

whether to accept or decline any job

how services are performed

what tools and supplies you use

how long services take

your schedule and availability

PureTask does not dictate or require specific cleaning methods, techniques, or workflows.

PLATFORM ACCESS & ACCOUNT REQUIREMENTS

To access the PureTask platform, you must:

provide accurate identity information

complete payment setup through PureTask’s payment processor

agree to this Agreement and other applicable platform policies

acknowledge evidence submission and safety requirements

Platform access is granted solely for use of the marketplace and does not constitute certification, endorsement, or verification of professional skill.

OPTIONAL EDUCATIONAL RESOURCES

PureTask may provide optional educational materials explaining:

how the platform works

how payments and escrow function

how disputes are evaluated

how to submit clear job-related evidence

These materials are optional, non-mandatory, and do not constitute training, supervision, or instruction on how to perform cleaning services.

You are solely responsible for determining how to perform services.

JOB ACCEPTANCE & CLIENT INTERACTION

Jobs posted on the platform include client-requested details and service windows.

You may:

accept or decline any job

communicate with clients through platform-approved channels

You are responsible for:

performing services as agreed with the client

complying with applicable laws

providing accurate job-related evidence

PureTask does not guarantee job availability, frequency, or earnings.

EVIDENCE SUBMISSION REQUIREMENTS

To facilitate payment and dispute resolution, you are required to submit job-related evidence, which may include:

arrival confirmation

before-service photos

after-service photos

Evidence requirements exist solely to:

verify job completion

reduce disputes

protect both parties

Evidence requirements do not dictate how services are performed.

PAYMENTS, CREDITS & ESCROW

Clients prepay credits through the platform.

Payment flow:

Client purchases credits

Credits are placed in escrow at booking

Credits are released upon client approval or auto-approval

Released credits become your earnings

You earn credits only from approved transactions.

PureTask may deduct or adjust earnings only due to:

dispute outcomes

fraud investigations

chargebacks or payment reversals

PureTask does not fine, penalize, or dock pay for performance.

PAYOUTS

You may request payout of earned credits through the platform or receive scheduled payouts, subject to payment processor requirements.

PureTask is not responsible for delays caused by:

payment processor verification

bank processing times

regulatory requirements

You are responsible for providing accurate payout information.

TAXES & INSURANCE

You are solely responsible for:

reporting and paying all applicable taxes

obtaining any required licenses

maintaining insurance appropriate for your business

PureTask does not withhold taxes or provide benefits.

DISPUTES & ARBITRATION

If a client disputes a job, PureTask will review the dispute using objective information, including:

submitted evidence

timestamps

job details

client and provider statements

PureTask acts as a neutral marketplace arbitrator.

Dispute decisions are final and documented.

SAFETY & PLATFORM INTEGRITY

You agree to comply with platform integrity rules, including prohibitions against:

fraud

theft

harassment

violence

illegal activity

safety threats

Violations may result in:

temporary platform restrictions

permanent removal from the platform

reporting to authorities where required

These actions relate to platform access only and do not create an employment relationship.

PLATFORM ACCESS MODERATION

PureTask may suspend or terminate platform access for reasons including:

fraud

safety concerns

repeated abuse of the dispute system

violation of platform rules

legal or regulatory requirements

PureTask is not obligated to provide continued access to the platform.

LIMITATION OF LIABILITY

PureTask is not responsible for:

your service performance

interactions with clients

property damage

personal injury

business losses

PureTask’s liability is limited to its role as a marketplace operator.

INDEMNIFICATION

You agree to indemnify and hold harmless PureTask from claims arising out of:

your services

your conduct

your violations of law

your breach of this Agreement

TERMINATION

This Agreement remains in effect while you access the platform.

You may stop using the platform at any time.

PureTask may terminate platform access in accordance with this Agreement.

MODIFICATIONS

PureTask may update this Agreement from time to time.

Continued use of the platform constitutes acceptance of updated terms.

GOVERNING LAW

This Agreement is governed by the laws of [Insert Jurisdiction], without regard to conflict of law principles.

ENTIRE AGREEMENT

This Agreement constitutes the entire agreement between you and PureTask regarding platform use and supersedes prior agreements.

END OF INDEPENDENT SERVICE PROVIDER AGREEMENT

CLIENT TERMS OF SERVICE & MARKETPLACE AGREEMENT
PURETASK

Effective Date: [Insert Date]

This Client Terms of Service & Marketplace Agreement (“Agreement”) is entered into between PureTask, Inc. (“PureTask,” “we,” “us,” or “our”) and the individual or entity using the PureTask platform as a client (“Client,” “you,” or “your”).

By creating an account, purchasing credits, or booking services through the platform, you agree to be bound by this Agreement.

NATURE OF THE PLATFORM

PureTask is a technology marketplace that connects clients with independent service providers who offer cleaning services.

PureTask:

does not provide cleaning services

does not employ service providers

does not supervise or direct how services are performed

All services are performed by independent service providers operating their own businesses. PureTask’s role is limited to facilitating bookings, payments, evidence review, and dispute resolution.

CLIENT ELIGIBILITY & ACCOUNT RESPONSIBILITIES

To use the platform, you must:

be at least 18 years old

provide accurate account information

provide accurate property and access details

comply with this Agreement and applicable laws

You are responsible for:

maintaining the security of your account

ensuring your home environment is safe and lawful

providing accurate instructions and access information

Providing false or misleading information may result in account suspension.

BOOKINGS & SERVICE REQUESTS

When you book a service:

you are requesting services from an independent provider

you are not contracting with PureTask for cleaning services

Service details, including timing and scope, are agreed between you and the provider through the platform.

PureTask does not guarantee:

availability of providers

acceptance of any booking

specific service outcomes

CREDITS, PAYMENTS & ESCROW

PureTask uses a prepaid credit system.

Payment flow:

You purchase credits through the platform

Credits are stored in your account wallet

Credits are placed in escrow when a booking is made

Credits are released upon approval or auto-approval

Credits:

are non-transferable

are not redeemable for cash

represent prepaid services

may be subject to expiration or promotional terms

SERVICE COMPLETION & EVIDENCE REVIEW

After service completion, providers submit job-related evidence, which may include photos and timestamps.

You are responsible for:

reviewing submitted evidence

approving or disputing the service within the review window

Approval releases escrowed credits to the provider.

AUTO-APPROVAL

If you take no action within the review window:

the service will be automatically approved

escrowed credits will be released to the provider

Auto-approval ensures timely payment and marketplace fairness.

DISPUTES & REFUNDS

If you believe a service was not completed as agreed, you may submit a dispute within the designated review window.

Disputes are evaluated using:

submitted evidence

timestamps

job details

client and provider statements

PureTask resolves disputes as a neutral marketplace arbitrator.

Possible outcomes:

no refund

partial refund

full refund

Dispute decisions are final and documented.

CANCELLATIONS

Client-initiated cancellations may be subject to:

refund limitations

cancellation windows

partial credit forfeiture

Cancellation terms may vary based on timing and job status and are disclosed during booking.

PureTask is not responsible for provider cancellations but will facilitate refunds or reassignment where applicable.

CLIENT CONDUCT & SAFETY

You agree to:

provide a safe and lawful environment

restrain aggressive animals

disclose known hazards

interact respectfully with providers

You may not:

harass or threaten providers

request illegal services

request off-platform payments

submit fraudulent disputes

Violations may result in account suspension or termination.

LIMITATION OF LIABILITY

PureTask is not responsible for:

service quality or outcomes

provider conduct

property damage

personal injury

loss or theft

interactions between users

PureTask’s liability is limited to its role as a marketplace operator and payment facilitator.

DISCLAIMER OF WARRANTIES

The platform is provided “as is” and “as available.”

PureTask makes no warranties regarding:

service quality

provider reliability

suitability of services

All services are performed at your own discretion and risk.

INDEMNIFICATION

You agree to indemnify and hold harmless PureTask from claims arising out of:

your use of the platform

your interactions with providers

your violation of this Agreement or applicable laws

ACCOUNT SUSPENSION & TERMINATION

PureTask may suspend or terminate accounts for:

fraud

safety concerns

abuse of disputes

violations of this Agreement

legal or regulatory requirements

PureTask is not obligated to provide continued access to the platform.

MODIFICATIONS TO THE AGREEMENT

PureTask may update this Agreement from time to time.

Continued use of the platform constitutes acceptance of updated terms.

GOVERNING LAW

This Agreement is governed by the laws of [Insert Jurisdiction], without regard to conflict of law principles.

ENTIRE AGREEMENT

This Agreement constitutes the entire agreement between you and PureTask regarding platform use and supersedes prior agreements.

END OF CLIENT TERMS OF SERVICE & MARKETPLACE AGREEMENT

wat is the process for creating the front end

Here’s the real-world process for creating the PureTask front end (Client app + Cleaner app + Admin dashboard) in a way that’s fast, scalable, and doesn’t create legal/IC contradictions.

I’ll lay it out as the exact workflow your team should follow.

1) Lock product scope and screens
Deliverables

Screen list for each app (Client / Provider / Admin)

User flows (booking → escrow → evidence → review → dispute)

State diagram for jobs (Created → Accepted → In progress → Submitted → Approved/Disputed → Closed)

Copy rules (IC-safe language: “independent providers”, no “training”, no “penalties”)

Output

A single “Front-End Spec v1” doc that engineers can build from without guessing.

2) Choose front-end architecture (recommended stack)
Client + Provider Mobile Apps (recommended)
React Native (Expo if you want speed, bare RN if you want max native control)

Navigation: React Navigation

State/data: TanStack Query (React Query)

Auth: JWT or Supabase/Auth0/Firebase (depending on your backend)

Media upload: direct-to-storage presigned URLs (S3) or Firebase Storage

Push: OneSignal or Expo Notifications

Maps/GPS: Google Maps SDK / Mapbox

Admin Dashboard (recommended)
Next.js (React) web app

Component library: MUI / Chakra / Shadcn

Tables: TanStack Table

Auth: same auth provider, role-based access

3) Define your API contract before UI coding
This avoids “front end guessing backend.”

Deliverables

API endpoints + request/response JSON (or GraphQL schema)

Error codes and edge cases

Upload flow spec (photos, metadata)

Webhook-driven states (payment success, payout success, dispute updates)

Output

Postman collection (or OpenAPI spec) engineers use as source of truth.

4) Design system + UI kit
Deliverables

Typography, buttons, spacing, card styles

Components: Job card, Provider card, Wallet card, Evidence uploader, Review slider, Dispute form, Admin tables

IC-safe copy baked into components

Output

Figma file + reusable component library.

5) Build in slices (vertical slices beat building “all UI first”)
Instead of building every screen, build the end-to-end “spine” first.

Slice 1: Auth + Profiles
Client signup/login

Provider signup/login + Stripe Connect onboarding link

Admin login

Slice 2: Booking + Escrow hold
Client: create booking, credits check, confirm

Provider: see available jobs, accept job

Admin: job appears in dashboard

Slice 3: Evidence submission
Provider: check-in, upload before/after

Client: evidence review UI

Slice 4: Approval / Auto-approval / Dispute
Client approve

Auto-approval timer screen/state

Dispute submit flow

Admin dispute decision UI

Slice 5: Earnings + payout views
Provider: earnings/payout screens

Admin: payout status, holds (fraud/dispute only)

6) Front-end quality gates you must enforce
These are the “don’t ship without” rules:

Offline-safe photo capture (queue uploads if connection drops)

Presigned upload with retries

Clear state rendering (no ambiguous job status)

Strict evidence requirements (but phrased as platform requirement, not work instruction)

Audit logs for admin actions (on admin UI)

7) Testing + launch readiness
Must test

Payment purchase credits

Escrow hold/release

Evidence uploads on bad internet

Dispute flows (client wins, provider wins, partial)

Payout flows (success + fail)

Role permissions (client/provider/admin isolation)

Deliverables

QA checklist

Test accounts

Staging environment identical to prod

What’s your backend right now (Supabase/Firebase/custom Node/Postgres)?

Do you want Admin dashboard in the same sprint as mobile, or after?

Then I’ll output a full front-end build plan with:

exact screen list

routes

component breakdown

API contract checklist

sprint plan (2-week chunks)


wat is react native how do u use it

Great question. I’ll explain this from zero, in plain language, then tie it directly to PureTask so you know exactly why it matters and how you’d use it.

1️⃣ What is React Native? (simple explanation)
React Native is a way to build real mobile apps (iOS + Android) using JavaScript.

Instead of writing:

Swift for iPhone

Kotlin for Android

You write one codebase in JavaScript (using React), and React Native turns it into:

a real iOS app

a real Android app

These are not web apps.
They install from the App Store / Play Store and feel native.

Companies using React Native:

Uber Eats

Airbnb (historically)

Instagram

Shopify

Discord

2️⃣ How React Native is different from a website
Website	React Native
Runs in a browser	Runs as a mobile app
HTML / CSS	Native UI components
No camera/GPS by default	Full access to camera, GPS, photos
Hard offline	Can work offline
One app for all devices	Separate iOS & Android apps from one codebase
For PureTask, this matters because you need:

camera (before/after photos)

GPS check-in

push notifications

offline reliability

React Native gives you all of that.

3️⃣ How React Native actually works (mentally)
Think of it like this:

You write React components

Instead of <div> or <button>, you use:

<View>

<Text>

<Pressable>

React Native maps those to:

real iOS UI elements

real Android UI elements

So this code:

<Text>Job Approved</Text>
Becomes:

a UILabel on iOS

a TextView on Android

Same code, two platforms.

4️⃣ What you actually write (example)
Here’s a real React Native screen (simplified):

import { View, Text, Pressable } from 'react-native';

export default function JobScreen() {
  return (
    <View>
      <Text>Cleaning Job</Text>
      <Pressable onPress={() => alert('Job Accepted')}>
        <Text>Accept Job</Text>
      </Pressable>
    </View>
  );
}
That’s a mobile app screen, not a website.

5️⃣ How React Native apps are structured
A real app looks like this:

/app
  /screens
    LoginScreen.js
    BookingScreen.js
    EvidenceScreen.js
    EarningsScreen.js
  /components
    JobCard.js
    EvidenceUploader.js
    WalletCard.js
  /services
    api.js
    auth.js
  /navigation
    AppNavigator.js
Each screen = one part of the app
Each component = reusable UI block

6️⃣ How data flows (important)
React Native apps do not store business logic.

They:

Call your backend API

Get JSON back

Render UI based on the response

Example:

GET /api/jobs/123
Backend returns:

{
  "status": "awaiting_approval",
  "escrow": 120,
  "photos": [...]
}
App shows:

“Awaiting Approval”

photos

action buttons (or not)

This keeps you legally safe because:

logic stays server-side

UI only reflects state

7️⃣ How you use React Native in PureTask (very concrete)
Client App (React Native)
book cleaning

review photos

approve / dispute

manage credits

Provider App (React Native)
browse jobs

accept jobs

GPS check-in

upload before/after photos

view earnings

Admin App (NOT React Native)
built as a web dashboard (Next.js)

8️⃣ How you build it (step-by-step reality)
Step 1 — Install tooling
Developers install:

Node.js

React Native CLI or Expo

Step 2 — Create the app
npx create-expo-app puretask
(This creates the project.)

Step 3 — Build screens
Developers create:

Login screen

Booking screen

Evidence screen

Earnings screen

Step 4 — Connect backend
API calls

Auth tokens

File uploads (photos)

Step 5 — Test on phones
iPhone simulator

Android emulator

real devices

Step 6 — Publish
Apple App Store

Google Play Store

9️⃣ Expo vs “Bare” React Native (important choice)
Expo (recommended for you)
Faster

Easier setup

Camera, GPS, notifications built-in

Fewer native bugs

Bare React Native
More control

More complexity

Better if you have heavy custom native code

👉 For PureTask: Expo is the right choice.

🔟 Do you need to know React Native yourself?
No.

But you should understand:

what it can/can’t do

how screens map to features

how backend controls behavior

how changes get shipped

That lets you:

manage engineers

review progress

avoid bad architecture decisions

TL;DR (one paragraph)
React Native lets you build real iOS + Android apps from one codebase using JavaScript. It’s ideal for PureTask because you need camera, GPS, push notifications, offline reliability, and fast iteration. You write UI screens and components, connect them to your backend, and ship native apps without building two separate teams.

show a PureTask app screen flow diagram

explain how photos & GPS work safely

explain how long a v1 app takes to build

will u review wat mapping and find several ways to improve it 

Yes — I reviewed the screen→component mapping and there are several concrete ways to improve it so it’s easier to build, faster to iterate, and less likely to create messy duplication or legal/IC drift.

Here are the best improvements (grouped by impact):

1) Consolidate duplicated screens into “mode-based” screens
Right now, some flows are split into multiple screens that will become repetitive.

Improvements
Merge ProviderBeforeEvidenceScreen + ProviderAfterEvidenceScreen into:

ProviderEvidenceScreen({ mode: "before" | "after" })

Merge dispute upload + review into:

DisputeFlowScreen({ step }) or 2 screens max (Upload → Submit)

Merge job details variants into:

JobDetailsScreen({ role: client|provider, context: offer|active|completed })

Benefit
Less code, fewer bugs, easier iteration.

2) Create a “Job State UI Kit” that renders from backend state only
Your job lifecycle is state-driven. The UI should be a pure function of:

job.status

user.role

job.permissions (what actions are allowed)

Improvements
Add a single component:

JobActionPanel (decides buttons + next steps)

JobStatusRenderer (decides which modules show)

JobRequirementsChecklist (e.g., “must upload before photos”)

Benefit
No UI drift. You won’t accidentally allow actions the backend disallows.

3) Make Evidence Upload a reusable “Upload Engine”
Photo flows are the hardest part of PureTask. Build it once, reuse everywhere.

Improvements
Create:

EvidenceUploader (handles capture, queue, retries, progress, offline caching)

UploadQueueManager (background job)

MediaPickerModal (camera/gallery)

UploadPolicy module (rules per role/step)

Benefit
Stability + offline support + fewer dispute-causing failures.

4) Add “Permissions + Terms-safe copy” wrapper components
To prevent IC-risk language creeping into UI, create “copy-guarded” components.

Improvements
ProviderLabel (always says “Independent provider”)

MarketplaceNoticeBanner (standard legal phrasing)

NoGuaranteeFooter (for job feed / earnings)

Benefit
Your UI stays aligned with the IC-safe canon automatically.

5) Tighten navigation: separate stacks for each job phase
Right now it’s implied but not explicit.

Improvements
Use:

ClientBookingStack

ClientJobStack

ProviderJobStack

ProviderEarningsStack

SharedSupportStack

And for provider job flow:

ProviderActiveJobStack:

Active Job Overview

Check-in

Evidence (before)

Evidence (after)

Submit

Benefit
Cleaner routing, simpler deep links, fewer edge-case navigation bugs.

6) Add “edge-case screens” that you’ll need in real life
A lot of marketplaces forget these, then scramble later.

Add these screens
Client:

NoProviderAssignedScreen

RescheduleSuggestionScreen

AutoApprovalExplainerScreen

Provider:

AccessIssueScreen (report access problem)

JobCanceledScreen (what happens next)

PayoutHoldScreen (fraud/dispute hold explanation)

UploadFailedRecoveryScreen

Admin isn’t RN, but still: web needs equivalents.

Benefit
Fewer support tickets, fewer disputes, better trust.

7) Normalize naming + directory structure for speed
Your naming is good but can be made more “production standard”.

Improvements
Keep all screens as *.screen.tsx

Keep all components as *.component.tsx

Group by feature, not by type:

/features
  /jobs
  /evidence
  /wallet
  /disputes
  /auth
/shared
  /ui
  /hooks
  /api
Benefit
Scales cleanly with more developers.

8) Add data hooks per feature (React Query pattern)
Instead of screens directly calling API, give each feature hooks:

useJobs()

useJob(jobId)

useAcceptJob()

useUploadEvidence()

useApproveJob()

useOpenDispute()

useCreditsBalance()

Benefit
Predictable data, caching, fewer loading bugs.

My “best upgrade” recommendation
If you do only 3 changes, do these:

Make EvidenceUploader a reusable engine

Make JobActionPanel state-driven from backend permissions

Merge duplicated screens into mode-based screens

That alone will cut build time and future bugs massively.

If you want, I can now produce an improved v2 mapping with:

consolidated screens

required edge-case screens

exact component ownership per feature

recommended navigation tree

Just say: “generate mapping v2”.

Yep — V2 is already a big step up, but there are more high-leverage improvements you can add that will make the build faster, safer, and easier to scale.

Below are new improvements beyond what we already included, grouped by category and impact.

1) Add a “Backend-Driven UI Schema” to eliminate app updates for flow changes
Right now, the UI is state + permissions driven (good). Next level is backend-driven UI config so you can change flows without shipping.

Improve with

job.ui = { nextAction, requiredSteps, banners, blockingReasons }

booking.ui = { steps, stepOrder, validations }

Benefits

Change review window messaging, evidence requirements, or booking steps without App Store delays.

Keeps Client/Provider apps consistent.

2) Introduce a strict “Domain Event” layer for jobs (prevents weird state bugs)
Marketplaces get messy when screens assume state transitions.

Add

Event types: JOB_ACCEPTED, CHECK_IN_RECORDED, EVIDENCE_BEFORE_UPLOADED, JOB_SUBMITTED, DISPUTE_OPENED, etc.

UI renders from event history, not just status.

Components

JobEventFeed

JobTimelineFromEvents

Benefits

Auditable.

Easier dispute review.

Fewer “why is status wrong?” bugs.

3) Build “Unified Identity & Trust” components (reduces fraud + support)
Add a trust layer UI that works across both roles.

New components

IdentityStatusBadge (verified/pending/failed)

TrustExplainerModal

PayoutEligibilityCard (provider)

EvidenceQualityHintBanner (provider)

Benefits

Fewer support tickets.

Better trust perception.

Clearer “why can’t I payout?” moments.

4) Add “Connectivity & Offline-first UX” as a first-class feature (not just banners)
V2 has offline indicators; now make it systematic.

Improve with

ConnectivityCenter screen (shows queued uploads, failures, retries)

OfflineJobPack (cache job details + instructions + evidence requirements locally)

UploadQueueScreen (view/manage queue)

Benefits

Evidence reliability goes way up (critical for PureTask).

Cleaner frustration drops.

5) Add “Evidence Angle Matching” UX (big reduction in disputes)
You already have evidence uploader; add guidance to ensure before/after matches.

New

Benefits

Better verification.

Dramatically fewer disputes.

6) Add “Pre-job checklist acknowledgment” for clients (but IC-safe)

confirms access instructions

confirms scope

confirms pets/hazards

confirms “review window + auto-approval”

Benefits

Fewer access issues.

Fewer disputes.

Still IC-safe (it’s client expectation management, not provider control).

7) Expand error-state screens into an “Issue Center”

New

Payment issue

Access issue

Upload issue

Dispute help

Safety concern

Benefits

Users self-serve.

Cleaner support load.

8) Build “Role-safe Copy Tokens” to prevent drift forever
You introduced copy guards; next is a tokenized copy system.

Add

copy.ts with strictly approved phrases:

COPY.PROVIDER_LABEL = "Independent Provider"

COPY.MARKETPLACE_NOTICE = "..."

Disallow raw strings in critical screens via lint rule.

Benefits

IC-safe language never drifts.

Brand voice stays consistent.

9) Add “Admin Reviewability Hooks” into UI (without building admin RN)

“notes” structured fields (not free text only)

Disputes are faster to resolve.

Better evidence packet quality.

A) V3 ARCHITECTURE UPGRADES
A1) Backend-Driven UI Schema (Remote UI)
Backend returns:

booking.ui: { steps, stepOrder, validations, banners }

job.ui: { nextAction, requiredSteps, banners, blockingReasons, reviewWindow, autoApprovalAt }

app.ui: { featureFlags, remoteConfig, cityRules }

Frontend renders steps/actions from these objects.
No hard-coded flow assumptions in UI.

A2) Domain Event System
Backend stores and returns:

job.events[] = [{ type, ts, actorRole, metadata }]
UI uses events to render:

JobTimelineFromEvents

Event-based status consistency checks

enableInstantPayout

disputeWindowHours

evidenceStrictnessLevel

gpsStrictnessLevel

providerSelectionMode (choose vs automatch)

cityLaunchEnabled

All sensitive copy comes from:

shared/copy/tokens.ts
No raw strings allowed in:

provider-facing earnings, reliability, ranking, “training”, “penalties”, “our cleaners”

did u take the top 7 improvements from v1 v2 and v3 or used v2 as a whole then incorporated the next top 7?

Great question — and I’m glad you asked, because the distinction matters for whether V3 is actually complete or accidentally layered wrong.

Short, direct answer
I used V2 as the full baseline, then selected the top 7 additional improvements on top of V2 and integrated them into V3.
I did not re-pick from V1 again, because everything valuable from V1 was already subsumed into V2.

So the hierarchy is correct and intentional:

V1 → foundational
V2 → full replacement + improvements
V3 → V2 plus the top 7 new upgrades

Nothing from V1 or V2 was dropped.

Longer, precise explanation (to remove any doubt)
How the evolution actually happened
V1

Full screen-to-component mapping

Correct but verbose

Some duplication

No systemic engines (evidence, jobs, copy safety)

Limited edge-case handling

V2

Replaced V1 entirely

Consolidated screens (mode-based, step-driven)

Introduced:

Job UI Kit

Evidence Upload Engine

IC-safe copy guards

Better navigation stacks

Missing real-world edge cases

V2 already contained all meaningful ideas from V1, but organized correctly

At this point, V1 no longer mattered as a separate thing — V2 was the new truth.

Top 7 improvements (the list you approved)
These were not fixes to V2 — they were architectural upgrades beyond V2:

Backend-driven UI schema

Offline-first Evidence Center

Evidence angle-matching UX

Copy tokens + lint enforcement

Feature flags + remote config

Domain event layer

Unified Issue Center

V3

Started with V2 as-is

Layered in all 7 upgrades globally

Refactored navigation, components, and data contracts to support those upgrades

Did not remove or regress any V2 functionality

So V3 = V2 + systemic upgrades, not a re-mix.

Why this matters (and why your instinct was right)
If I had:

re-picked from V1 + V2 + V3
or

only partially carried V2 forward

You would risk:

missing edge-case screens

duplicating responsibilities

breaking the “single source of truth” principle

engineers asking “which version is right?”

But instead, the progression is clean:

V2 = complete functional mapping

V3 = same mapping, but production-grade

That’s exactly how senior product/engineering teams evolve specs.

Final confirmation (plain English)
✅ V1 ideas → fully absorbed into V2

✅ V2 → used as the baseline

✅ Top 7 → applied on top of V2

✅ V3 → superset of everything before, nothing lost

You’re not missing anything.
You’re not double-counting anything.
And engineers could safely build directly from V3.

If you want, next we can:

do a V3 completeness audit (what still isn’t specified)

convert V3 into a build order + sprint plan

or generate a “backend contract v1” that exactly matches V3 UI expectations

Just tell me where you want to go next.


no more new things just improve wat we already have

Perfect — that constraint is exactly right.
I will not add anything new. I’ll only refine, simplify, harden, and clarify what already exists in V3.

Below is a pure improvement pass on V3: same scope, same features, same architecture — just cleaner, safer, easier to build, and easier to maintain.

GOAL OF THIS PASS (IMPORTANT)
No new systems

No new screens

No new engines

No scope creep

Only:

reduce complexity

remove ambiguity

tighten contracts

improve naming

reduce build risk

make V3 easier for engineers to execute correctly

IMPROVEMENT PASS ON V3 (NO NEW FEATURES)
1) Simplify the Backend-Driven UI Schema (reduce overengineering)
Current risk
The UI schema is powerful but could become too flexible, leading to:

frontend confusion

inconsistent UX

backend overreach

Improvement (without adding anything)
Standardize the schema shape and freeze it.

Instead of flexible blobs, lock to:

job.ui = {
  phase,                // string enum
  primaryAction,        // string enum
  requiredSteps[],      // enum[]
  banners[],            // enum[]
  blockingReasons[]     // enum[]
}
No arbitrary text, no dynamic layouts.

Frontend maps enums → components.

Benefit
Safer

Predictable

Easier to test

Engineers don’t “design UI in JSON”

2) Collapse “Job UI Engine” responsibilities into 3 clear components
Current state
You have:

JobStatusRenderer

JobActionPanel

JobRequirementsChecklist

JobBlockingReasonsPanel

This is fine, but slightly fragmented.

Improvement
Group responsibilities clearly (no new components):

JobContextPanel

phase

banners

blocking reasons

JobActionPanel

primary + secondary actions only

reads permissions + ui.primaryAction

JobProgressPanel

requiredSteps

completion state

checklist

Benefit
Fewer mental models

Easier prop contracts

Less wiring per screen

3) Tighten the Domain Event Model (prevent event sprawl)
Current risk
Events are powerful, but if left loose they grow uncontrollably.

Improvement
Freeze the event taxonomy now.

Only allow:

JOB_CREATED

JOB_ACCEPTED

CHECK_IN_RECORDED

EVIDENCE_BEFORE_UPLOADED

EVIDENCE_AFTER_UPLOADED

JOB_SUBMITTED

JOB_APPROVED

DISPUTE_OPENED

DISPUTE_RESOLVED

PAYOUT_RELEASED

No free-form events.

Each event:

{ type, ts, actorRole, relatedId }
Benefit
Timeline always reliable

Disputes easier

Admin review simpler

No “why does this event exist?” later

4) Make Evidence Engine strictly step-scoped
Current risk
Evidence engine is reused everywhere (good), but rules could bleed.

Improvement
Lock evidence rules to context enums only:

context = BEFORE | AFTER | DISPUTE
Each context defines:

required count

room tags allowed

angle matching required (true/false)

Frontend does not infer rules.

Benefit
No accidental evidence reuse

Cleaner dispute packets

Fewer edge-case bugs

5) Reduce Navigation Complexity Without Removing Stacks
Current state
Navigation is correct but heavy.

Improvement
Freeze which stacks are allowed to deep-link:

Only:

JobDetails

ProviderActiveJob

EvidenceCenter

IssueCenter

All others must be reached through normal flow.

Benefit
Fewer broken deep links

Easier push notification routing

Less QA complexity

6) Normalize Screen Naming (small but important)
Current issue
Some screens are action-based, others state-based.

Improvement
Rename consistently (no new screens):

ProviderEvidenceScreen → JobEvidenceScreen

ClientReviewScreen → JobReviewScreen

ProviderSubmitJobScreen → JobSubmitScreen

ProviderActiveJobScreen → ActiveJobOverviewScreen

Role is inferred, not embedded in name.

Benefit
Cleaner imports

Reusability increases

Less duplication pressure later

7) Clarify “Issue Center” Ownership (reduce support logic creep)
Current risk
Issue Center can become a dumping ground.

Improvement
Hard rule (documented):

Issue Center can:

collect structured reports

attach evidence

route to backend

Issue Center cannot:

resolve issues

promise outcomes

modify job state directly

All outcomes happen server-side.

Benefit
Legal safety

Predictable behavior

No UI logic creep

8) Harden Copy Safety Without Adding Anything
Current state
Copy tokens + lint exist (good).

Improvement
Add one rule (process-only):

Any string shown in provider earnings, reliability, ranking, or payouts must come from copyTokens.ts.

No exceptions.

Benefit
IC-safe language never drifts

Marketing, product, and legal stay aligned

9) Reduce Frontend State Ownership (very important)
Current risk
Frontend might accidentally store derived job state.

Improvement
Rule:

Frontend stores only IDs and timestamps

All job state is authoritative from backend

No local “status” mutations

Benefit
Fewer desync bugs

Easier support debugging

Safer dispute handling

10) Final “Build Guardrails” for Engineers
Add these as comments at top of repo (no new code):

Frontend never decides job outcomes

Frontend never enforces penalties

Frontend never infers permissions

Backend is the source of truth

UI renders state, not policy

Benefit
New engineers don’t break the model

IC posture preserved in code, not just docs

FINAL ASSESSMENT AFTER IMPROVEMENT PASS
After these refinements:

V3 is cleaner, not bigger

Engineering effort goes down, not up

Legal posture is stronger, not riskier

Fewer decisions are left to interpretation

This is now a senior-level, buildable spec.

We can now:

translate V3 into a build checklist per engineer

create a definition of done for each engine

or lock V3 as Frontend Spec v1.0

Tell me how you want to proceed.
